Conditions and Obligatory Status of Eid Prayer
Conditions for Eid prayer and its wujub according to Abu Hanifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for Eid prayer's obligation and performance in the Hanafi school and explain why it is classified as wajib.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib, not fard or sunnah; its conditions mirror Jumu'ah except the khutbah which comes after the prayer.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies the Hanafi position on Eid prayer. You will learn who is obligated to perform it, where it must be held, and how it differs from Jumu'ah in terms of the khutbah. The proof for its obligatory status is the Prophet's unbroken practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage deals with Eid prayer and states its ruling as wajib. The commentator clarifies that this is the most correct (al-ashah) view.
The ruling is well-established in the Hanafi school.
2
Determine the conditions for obligation
The conditions are the same as those for Jumu'ah. List exemptions: traveler, sick, woman, child, insane, excused. These are shurut al-wujub.
If a condition is absent, the prayer is not wajib upon that person.
3
Determine the conditions for performance
The prayer must be performed in a major city (misr) with a central mosque (jami') or its courtyard. This is a shart al-ada.
Outside such a locale, the prayer is not valid without dispensation.
4
Analyze the role of the khutbah
The khutbah is not a condition for validity; it is sunnah and delivered after the prayer. Omitting it is sinful but does not invalidate the prayer.
This is a key difference from Jumu'ah, where the khutbah is a condition.
5
Evaluate the proof for wajib status
The proof is the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah) and his making Eid a symbol of Islam. In Hanafi usul, continuous practice indicates wujub.
The evidence is zanni al-dalala, hence the classification as wajib, not fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشُرط لها شروط الجمعة وجوباً، وأداء، إلا الخطبة [٣] قوله : وجوباً وأداء ; يعني أن ما شرط لوجوب الجمعة شرط لوجوب صلاة العيدين، فلا تجب على مسافر ومريض وامرأةٍ وصبي ومجنون ومعذور، وما شُرط لأدائها فلا يُؤدَّى إلا في مصر جامع أو فنائه. [٤] قوله : إلا الخطبة ; فإنها ليست بشرط لصحة صلاة العيد، فلو لم يخطب أثم ولا تبطل صلاة العيد، بخلاف صلاة الجمعة، فإنَّها لا تصح بدون الخطبة، هذا هو الفرق بين الخطبتين، وفرق آخر هو أنه ليس تقديم خطبة الجمعة وتأخير خطبة العيدين عن الصلاة. [0] قوله : وهو الأصح ; استدلوا عليه بمواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من غير ترك على صلاة العيدين، وجعلهما من شعائر الإسلام.
And conditions for it are the conditions of Jumu'ah in terms of obligation and performance, except the Khutbah. [3] His saying: 'obligation and performance' means that what is a condition for the obligation of Jumu'ah is a condition for the obligation of the two Eid prayers, so it is not obligatory upon a traveler, a sick person, a woman, a child, an insane person, or one with an excuse; and what is a condition for its performance, it is not performed except in a major city (misr) that has a congregational mosque (jami') or its courtyard. [4] His saying: 'except the Khutbah'; for it is not a condition for the validity of Eid prayer. So if one does not deliver the khutbah, he sins but the Eid prayer is not invalidated, unlike Jumu'ah which is not valid without the khutbah. This is one difference between the two khutbahs. Another difference is that the khutbah of Jumu'ah is before the prayer and the khutbah of Eid is after the prayer. [0] His saying: 'and it is the most correct'; they adduced as proof the Prophet's continuous practice without ever leaving the two Eid prayers, and his making them from the symbols of Islam.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage explains the conditions for Eid prayer and its obligatory status. The base matn states that the conditions for Eid prayer are the same as for Jumu'ah in terms of obligation (who is required to pray) and performance (where it is held), except for the khutbah, which is not a condition for validity. The commentator details: Eid prayer is not wajib upon travelers, the sick, women, children, the insane, or the excused. It must be performed in a major city (misr) with a central mosque (jami') or its courtyard. Unlike Jumu'ah, failing to deliver the khutbah does not invalidate the prayer, though it is sinful. Additionally, the khutbah is delivered after the prayer, not before. Finally, the commentator confirms that the most correct view (al-ashah) in the Hanafi school is that Eid prayer is wajib (obligatory), based on the Prophet's constant practice and its status as a symbol of Islam.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): A level of obligation between fard and sunnah; established by zanni evidence.
خطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered after the Eid prayer; not a condition for validity.
مصر جامع (misr jami'): A major city with a central congregational mosque where Jumu'ah and Eid prayers are held.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of Eid prayer?
A) Fard 'ayn
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah mu'akkada
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school, with conditions mirroring Jumu'ah except the khutbah, which is delivered after the prayer.

Ruling and Time of Eid Prayer: Sunnah or Wajib
Explanation of the ruling and time of Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Eid prayer and explain why Imam Muhammad called it Sunnah while later Hanafis consider it Wajib.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is 'Sunnah' by proof, not by degree; its obligation is proven by the Sunnah, so it is named after its proof.

This lesson examines a key passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah that discusses the ruling of Eid prayer. The matn simply states that the time of Eid prayer is from sunrise to zenith. The commentary then addresses a critical question: is the Eid prayer Sunnah or Wajib? By analyzing Imam Muhammad's statement about the coincidence of Eid and Friday, we will discover how the Hanafi school defines 'Sunnah' in this context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hukm According to the Matn
The passage begins by stating that the Eid prayer is Sunnah according to the Hanafi scholars. Note that this is the statement of the matn being commented upon.
2
Encounter the Potential Challenge
Imam Muhammad said: if two 'Eids' (Eid and Friday) coincide, the first (Eid) is Sunnah, the second (Friday) is obligatory. This might be interpreted as Eid being merely recommended.
The challenge is that this could undermine the obligatory nature of Eid prayer.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The commentator explains that 'Sunnah' here refers to the proof (the Sunnah of the Prophet), not the level of obligation. The obligation itself is established by the Sunnah, so it is called Sunnah by way of naming the cause for the effect.
This is a linguistic argument: what is proven by the Sunnah is called Sunnah.
4
Determine the Time of Eid Prayer
The time is from when the sun rises to the height of a spear (approx. 12 handspans) until its zenith. This time is exclusive: the zenith itself is not included.
This time is shared with voluntary prayers.
5
Identify the Imam for Eid Prayer
The imam for Eid should be the sultan or his deputy, or if absent, the one chosen by the people. This mirrors the conditions for Friday prayer.
This condition is derived from the similarity with Friday prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And its time is from the height of the sun (after sunrise) to its decline (zenith). And the imam leads them in two rak'ahs. And it has been said: It is Sunnah according to our scholars, for Muhammad said: 'Two Eid festivals coincide on one day, then the first is Sunnah and the second is obligatory.' It was answered that Muhammad only called it Sunnah because its obligation is established by the Sunnah. Its time is from the height of the sun to its decline. And the imam leads them in two rak'ahs. [1] His statement: 'Two Eids' means Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and Friday. The conclusion: If Eid al-Fitr or Eid al-Adha falls on Friday, then the first (the Eid prayer) is Sunnah, and the second (Friday prayer) is obligatory. So it is understood that the Eid prayer is Sunnah, not obligatory. [2] His statement: 'He only called it Sunnah...' The conclusion: The term 'Sunnah' in Muhammad's statement is not in contrast to obligatory (wajib), but rather it is called Sunnah because the obligation of the Eid prayer is established by the Sunnah (the Prophet's practice), and what is established by a thing is given its name, as a name for the cause applied to the effect, or the indicator applied to the indicated. (3) His statement: 'Its time' – because earlier it was mentioned that the conditions of Friday prayer are conditions of the Eid prayer except for the sermon, and among its conditions is the time of Zuhr, so he hastened to mention the time of the Eid prayer lest one think they are the same. [4] His statement: 'From the height' – meaning the measure of a spear, which is twelve handspans, and it is the time when voluntary prayer is permissible. [5] His statement: 'al-dhaka'' – meaning the sun. (6) His statement: 'to its decline' – by 'decline' is meant zenith, as it is sometimes called decline due to adjacency (i.e., the sun at its peak is about to decline). And the limit here is excluded from the limited, for the time of the sun at its zenith is not a time for it (the prayer), so what comes after is even less appropriate. [7] His statement: 'the imam' – he is the sultan or his deputy, or one who has obtained permission from him; if these are absent, then the one with whom the people are pleased. (1) Among those who hold it is Sunnah is al-Nasafi, and it was corrected in al-Manafi', and the author of al-Hidayah (1:85), al-Mukhtar (1:112), al-Durr al-Mukhtar (1:555), and chosen by the author of al-Multaqa (25), al-Kanz (1:21), al-Tanwir (1:55), and others corrected the view of obligation. (2) In al-Jami' al-Saghir (1:113). (3) See al-Hidayah (1:85).
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn regarding the Eid prayer. It begins by establishing the ruling: the Eid prayer is Sunnah according to the Hanafi school, not obligatory (wajib). The commentator addresses a potential doubt from a statement of Imam Muhammad, who said that if two Eids (Eid and Friday) coincide, the first (Eid) is Sunnah and the second (Friday) is obligatory. Some might think this implies Eid is Sunnah in contrast to Friday's obligation. The commentator clarifies that 'Sunnah' here does not mean merely recommended as opposed to obligatory; rather, it means the obligation of Eid prayer is proven by the Sunnah (the Prophet's practice), so it is called Sunnah by naming the cause (the Sunnah) for the effect (the obligation). This is a linguistic point: the proof is called by the name of the thing it proves. Thus, Eid prayer is still obligatory in the sense of being established by a binding proof, but not as obligatory as Friday; it is not a fard. The text then explains the time: from when the sun has risen to a spear's height (approximately 12 handspans) until its decline (zenith). This time is for the Eid prayer. The commentator notes that this time is the same as for voluntary prayer, and the limit (ghayah) of 'until its decline' is exclusive: the time of the sun at its zenith is not included. Finally, it defines the imam for Eid: the ruler or his representative, or if none, the one chosen by the people. The footnote at the end summarizes the ikhtilaf: some scholars, including al-Nasafi, hold it is Sunnah, while others like the author of al-Hidayah and al-Durr al-Mukhtar hold it is wajib. The text does not give a final tarjih but presents both views.

Key Terms
صلاة العيدين (salat al-‘idayn): The two festival prayers: Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha, consisting of two rak'ahs with extra takbirs.
سنة (sunnah): Here, it means the ruling that is established by the Prophet's practice (Sunnah) and is recommended, distinct from obligatory (fard/wajib).
ارتفاع ذكاء (irtifa‘ dhaka’): The rising of the sun to the height of a spear (approximately 12 handspans), the time when voluntary prayer becomes permissible and Eid prayer begins.
زوال (zawal): The decline of the sun from its zenith (meridian), marking the end of the time for Eid prayer and the beginning of Zuhr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Imam Muhammad call the Eid prayer 'Sunnah' when it coincides with Friday?
A) Because it is not obligatory at all.
B) Because its obligation is established by the Sunnah (Prophetic practice).
C) Because it is less important than Friday prayer.
D) Because it is a confirmed sunnah that cannot be missed.

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is considered Sunnah Mu'akkadah in early Hanafi sources, but many later scholars deem it Wajib; the term 'Sunnah' in Imam Muhammad's statement refers to the proof, not a lower level of obligation.

Method of Performing the Eid Prayer: Hanafi Procedure and Proof
Detailed description of the Eid prayer sequence with hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for the Eid prayer (number and sequence of takbirs) and identify the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
In Eid prayer, three additional takbirs in each rak'ah are sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib.

This lesson details the exact sequence of the Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school. You will learn the specific placement of the extra takbirs (takbirat al-zawa'id), the hand position, and the hadith evidence from the Prophet's practice. Understanding this method ensures you pray Eid correctly according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence in the first rak'ah
List the elements in order: opening takbir, thana', three additional takbirs, recitation of al-Fatihah and a surah, then takbir for bowing.
The three additional takbirs come before recitation.
2
Identify the sequence in the second rak'ah
List the elements: recitation of al-Fatihah and a surah first, then three additional takbirs, then takbir for bowing.
The order reverses: recitation comes before the additional takbirs.
3
Locate the hadith evidence
Find the two hadith reports: a weak one from Abu Dawud with four takbirs, and a stronger one from Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah with seven and five takbirs.
The Hanafi school relies on the stronger hadith of Ibn 'Abbas.
4
Understand the authority weight
Note that the seven and five method is from the practice of Ibn Mas'ud, Hudhayfah, and Abu Musa, and is recorded in the Zahir al-Riwayah.
The other report is considered weak.
5
Note the ruling on hand raising
The hands are raised at each additional takbir, similar to the opening takbir, and lowered between them.
After the third takbir in the first rak'ah, hands are placed for recitation.

Source Text

وأخرجه أبو داود في «سننه»: أنَّ سعيد بن العاص له سأل أبا موسى الأشعري وحذيفة : كيف كان رسول الله لم يكبر في العيدين ؟ قال : كان رسولُ الله يكبرُ في الأضحى والفطر أربع تكبيرات ، تكبيره على الجنائز » (١) ، وفي سنده ضعف يسير. وأخرج الترمذي وابن ماجة وغيرهما : «إنَّ النَّبي اكبر في العيدين في الأولى سبعاً قبل القراءة، وفي الأخرى خمساً قبل القراءة ) ، وهو رواية ابن عباس ، والأمر فيه واسع ؛ لاختلاف الصحابة قولاً وعملاً ، وهو النجوم بأيهم اقتديتم اهتديتم. Book of Prayer: Chapter of the Two Eids. [1] 341 He makes the takbir for entering ihram, then recites the thana', then makes takbir three times, then recites al-Fatihah and a surah, then bows while making takbir. In the second [rak'ah], he begins with recitation, then makes takbir three times, and another for bowing. He raises his hands during the additional takbirs. He makes the takbir for entering ihram, then recites the thana', then makes takbir three times, then recites al-Fatihah and a surah, then bows while making takbir. In the second, he begins with recitation, then makes takbir three times, and another for bowing. He raises his hands during the additional takbirs. [1] His statement: 'He makes the takbir for entering ihram' – the summary of this manner is that he first makes the opening takbir like other prayers, then recites the reported thana' which is: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...', then he makes three takbirs which are the additional takbirs, then recites al-Fatihah and any surah he wishes, then makes takbir for bowing. This is in the first rak'ah, so the takbirs are five including the opening and bowing takbirs. In the second, he first recites al-Fatihah and a surah, then makes three additional takbirs, then makes takbir for bowing. This manner is reported from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Hudhayfah, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, recorded by 'Abd al-Razzaq and Ibn Abi Shaybah in their Musannafs, and by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan in his book al-Athar, and others. Abu Dawud recorded in his Sunan: that Sa'id ibn al-'As asked Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and Hudhayfah: How did the Messenger of Allah make takbir in the two Eids? They said: The Messenger of Allah would make takbir in al-Adha and al-Fitr four takbirs, like his takbir over the funeral. (1) Its chain has slight weakness. Al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and others recorded: 'The Prophet made takbir in the two Eids: in the first [rak'ah] seven before recitation, and in the other five before recitation.' This is the narration of Ibn 'Abbas, and the matter is broad because of the differences among the Companions in speech and action, and they are stars: whichever you follow, you are guided. [2] His statement: 'He raises his hands' – meaning as he raises his hands at the opening takbir, and he lowers his hands between the additional takbirs, and he places them after the third takbir in the first rak'ah, and there is no placement after it in the second. As in Majalis al-Abrar. (1) In Musnad Ahmad (4:416) and Sunan Abi Dawud (1:299), and he was silent about it, etc. And from al-Qasim Abu 'Abd al-Rahman said: Some of the Companions of the Messenger of Allah narrated to me: 'The Prophet led us in prayer on a day of Eid and made takbir four and four, then turned to us when he finished and said: Do not forget like the takbir of the funeral prayer, and he pointed with his fingers and brought his thumb.' In Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar (4:345), and al-Tahawi said: 'Its chain is good.' (2) In Sunan al-Tirmidhi (2:416) and Sunan Ibn Majah (1:407), etc.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage details the method of the Eid prayer. The commentator explains the sequence in the first rak'ah: opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram), recitation of the thana' (Subhanaka), then three additional takbirs, followed by recitation of al-Fatihah and a surah, then takbir for bowing. In the second rak'ah: first recite al-Fatihah and a surah, then three additional takbirs, then takbir for bowing. The total takbirs in the first rak'ah are five (including opening and bowing), and in the second, five as well (including the bowing takbir). The commentator notes that this method is reported from prominent Companions: Ibn Mas'ud, Hudhayfah, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, as recorded in early hadith collections. He then presents two hadith reports: one from Abu Dawud with a weak chain saying the Prophet made four takbirs (like the funeral prayer), and a stronger report from Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah saying seven in the first and five in the second. The commentator remarks that the matter is broad due to differences among the Companions, and any of these ways is acceptable. He also explains the hand position: the worshipper raises his hands at each additional takbir as at the opening takbir, lowers them between the takbirs, and after the third takbir in the first rak'ah, he places his hands (presumably for recitation), but in the second rak'ah, there is no such placement after the takbirs.

Key Terms
تكبيرات الزوائد (takbirat al-zawa'id): The additional takbirs in the Eid prayer beyond the opening and bowing takbirs.
الثناء (al-thana'): The prescribed opening supplication: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika wa tabaraka ismuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruka.'
يرفع يديه (yarfa' yadayhi): Raising the hands to the ears or shoulders during the takbirs, specifically during the additional takbirs of Eid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first rak'ah of Eid prayer, after the opening takbir and thana', how many additional takbirs are performed before recitation?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method for Eid prayer includes seven takbirs in the first rak'ah (including opening takbir) and three additional takbirs before recitation, and five in the second (including bowing takbir), and these extra takbirs are sunnah mu'akkadah.

Manner of Takbirat in Eid Prayer
Details the takbirat and hand raising for Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number and placement of takbirat in Eid prayer and identify the proof from the Companions' practice.

Core Idea
Eid prayer has extra takbirs: three before recitation in first rak'ah, three after recitation in second.

The Eid prayer has a distinct structure of takbirs beyond the usual prayer. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of several Companions, prescribes a specific sequence of extra takbirs. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains that sequence and the hand-raising, and acknowledges that other numbers are narrated, leaving the matter flexible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that this passage deals with the manner of takbirat in the Eid prayer. The act is performing the extra takbirs (takbirat al-zawa'id). Determine the ruling: sunnah muakkadah.
The Eid prayer itself is wajib according to Abu Hanifa, but the specific takbir count is sunnah.
2
Locate the sequence for the first rak'ah
Trace the order: takbir al-ihram, thana', three extra takbirs, recitation (Fatihah + surah), then takbir for ruku'. Note the total of five takbirs.
The extra takbirs come before recitation in the first rak'ah.
3
Locate the sequence for the second rak'ah
In the second rak'ah: begin with recitation (Fatihah + surah), then three extra takbirs, then takbir for ruku'. Note that there is no thana' in the second rak'ah.
Extra takbirs come after recitation in the second rak'ah.
4
Identify the proof cited
The passage attributes this manner to Companions Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Hudhayfah, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and cites hadith records. Classify the proof as Sunnah ahad (zanni al-thubut) and qawl al-sahabi.
The Hanafi school uses the practice of Companions as a normative proof.
5
Note the flexibility and ikhtilaf
The passage mentions other narrations (four takbirs from Sa'id ibn al-'As, seven and five from Ibn 'Abbas) and states the matter is wide due to Companion differences. Understand that while the described Hanafi manner is mufta bihi, other numbers are also acceptable in some contexts.
Cross-madhhab: Shafi'is use seven and five; Hanbalis six and five; Malikis six and five (differently).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يُكبر للإحرام، ويُثْنِي ، ثُمَّ يكبر ثلاثاً، ويقرأ الفاتحة وسورةً، ثُمَّ يركع مُكَبِّراً، وفي الثانية : يبدأ بالقراءة، ثم يكبر ثلاثاً، وأخرى للركوع، ويرفع يديه في الزوائد. قوله : يكبر للإحرام ؛ حاصل هذه الكيفية أن يكبر أولاً لافتتاح الصلاة كسائر الصلوات، ثم يقرأ الثناءَ المأثور وهو : سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك، وتبارك اسمك ، وتعالى جدك، ولا إله غيرك»، ثم يكبر ثلاثاً وهي تكبيرات الزوائد، ثم يقرأ الفاتحة وسورة، أي سورة شاء، ثمّ يكبِّرُ للركوع، هذا في الركعة الأولى، فالتكبيرات فيها خمس مع تكبيرتي الإحرام والركوع. وفي الثانية يقرأ أولاً الفاتحة وسورة، ثم يكبر ثلاثاً زوائد، ثم يكبر للركوع وهذه الكيفية مأثورة عن عبد الله بن مسعود، وحذيفة، وأبي موسى الأشعري، أخرجه عبد الرزاق وابن أبي شيبة في «مصنفيهما»، ومحمد بن الحسن في كتاب «الآثار» وغيرهم. وأخرجه أبو داود في «سننه»: أنَّ سعيد بن العاص له سأل أبا موسى الأشعري وحذيفة : كيف كان رسول الله لم يكبر في العيدين ؟ قال : كان رسولُ الله يكبرُ في الأضحى والفطر أربع تكبيرات ، تكبيره على الجنائز » (١) ، وفي سنده ضعف يسير. وأخرج الترمذي وابن ماجة وغيرهما : «إنَّ النَّبي اكبر في العيدين في الأولى سبعاً قبل القراءة، وفي الأخرى خمساً قبل القراءة ) ، وهو رواية ابن عباس ، والأمر فيه واسع ؛ لاختلاف الصحابة قولاً وعملاً ، وهو النجوم بأيهم اقتديتم اهتديتم. [٢] قوله : ويرفع يديه ؛ أي كما يرفع يديه عند الإحرام، ويرسل يديه بين تكبيرات الزوائد، ويضع بعد التكبيرة الثالثة منها في الركعة الأولى، ولا وضع في الثانية بعدها. كما في «مجالس الأبرار».
He says takbir for the consecration (ihram), and then praises (thana), then he says takbir three times, and recites al-Fatihah and a surah, then he bows while saying takbir. In the second (rak'ah): he begins with recitation, then says takbir three times, and another for bowing. And he raises his hands during the extra (takbirs). His saying: 'He says takbir for the consecration (ihram)'; the essence of this manner is that he says takbir first for opening the prayer like other prayers, then recites the transmitted praise: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika, wa tabaraka ismuka, wa ta'ala jadduka, wa la ilaha ghayruka', then says takbir three times, which are the extra takbirs, then recites al-Fatihah and a surah, whichever surah he wishes, then says takbir for bowing. This is in the first rak'ah; thus the takbirs in it are five including the consecration and bowing takbirs. In the second (rak'ah) he first recites al-Fatihah and a surah, then says takbir three times extra, then says takbir for bowing. And this manner is transmitted from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Hudhayfah, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. It is recorded by 'Abdurrazzaq and Ibn Abi Shaybah in their Musannafs, and by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan in the book al-Athar and others. And Abu Dawud recorded in his Sunan that Sa'id ibn al-'As asked Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and Hudhayfah: 'How did the Messenger of Allah ﷺ say takbir in the two Eids?' They said: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ would say takbir in al-Adha and al-Fitr four takbirs, like his takbir over the funeral prayers' – and its chain has slight weakness. And al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah and others recorded: 'The Prophet ﷺ said takbir in the two Eids: in the first (rak'ah) seven times before recitation, and in the second five times before recitation' – this is the narration of Ibn 'Abbas, and the matter is wide in scope due to the difference of the Companions in statement and action, and they are stars: whichever of them you follow, you are guided. [2] His saying: 'and he raises his hands' – i.e., as he raises his hands at the consecration (ihram), and he lets his hands down between the extra takbirs, and he places them after the third takbir of them in the first rak'ah, and there is no placing after it in the second. As in Majalis al-Abrar.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with its textual proof describing the manner of performing the takbirat in the Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school. The author first states the ruling: in the first rak'ah, the worshiper begins with the takbirat al-ihram (opening takbir), then recites the thana' (the transmitted praise), then says three extra takbirs (called takbirat al-zawa'id), then recites al-Fatihah and a surah, then says takbir for ruku'. In the second rak'ah, the recitation comes first, followed by three extra takbirs, then the takbir for ruku'. The hands are raised during each of these extra takbirs, as is done for the opening takbir. The commentary explains that the total takbirs in the first rak'ah are five (including ihram and ruku' takbirs). This manner is attributed to several Companions, including Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Hudhayfah, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and is recorded by early hadith authorities. The author then cites a hadith from Abu Dawud with a slightly weak chain where the Prophet ﷺ is reported to have said four takbirs (like funeral prayer), and another narration from Ibn 'Abbas with seven in the first and five in the second. The author notes that the matter is flexible due to the varied practices of the Companions, and any of them may be followed. Regarding hand-raising: the hands are raised with each takbir, and between the extra takbirs the hands are let down; after the third extra takbir in the first rak'ah, the worshiper places his hands (as usual for qiyam), but there is no placing after the extra takbirs in the second rak'ah before recitation.

Key Terms
تكبيرات الزوائد (takbirat al-zawa'id): The extra takbirs said in the Eid prayer besides the takbir al-ihram and takbir al-ruku'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Hanafi school prescribes three extra takbirs in each rak'ah of Eid prayer, placed before recitation in the first and after recitation in the second, with hands raised for each.

Khutbah of Eid Prayer
States the ruling that the imam delivers two sermons after Eid prayer, teaching fitr rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the Eid khutbah in the Hanafi school and identify its key features.

Core Idea
The Eid khutbah is sunnah, not obligatory—teaching fitr rulings, no adhan, similar to Jumu'ah but without conditions.

In this lesson, we examine the Eid prayer's khutbah as outlined in the Hanafi text. The passage clarifies that after the Eid prayer, the imam delivers two sermons to teach the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr. This mirrors Jumu'ah in format but differs in legal status and procedural details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its timing
The passage says 'ويخطب بعدها' – after the Eid prayer. The act is delivering two sermons (khutbah).
The khutbah is after the prayer, not before like Jumu'ah is before.
2
Determine the preacher
The text says 'أي الإمام' indicating the imam, but then clarifies it is permissible for someone else to give the khutbah.
This shows flexibility; unity of imam and preacher is preferred but not required.
3
Compare the format to Jumu'ah
The khutbah is 'كخطبتي الجمعة' – two sermons with a light sitting between them. However, there is no adhan or iqamah for Eid.
The absence of adhan is a key difference.
4
Extract the legal status
The passage does not explicitly state obligation; from context and further texts, it is sunnah.
The Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah muakkadah.
5
Note the content taught
The sermons teach 'أحكام الفطرة' – rulings of fitr (zakat al-fitr).
This connects the khutbah to practical teaching of fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويخطب بعدها خُطبتين يُعَلِّمُ فيها أحكام الفطرة. قوله : ويخطب ؛ أي الإمام أشار به إلى أولوية اتحاد الإمام والخطيب، فلو خطب غيرُ مَن صلَّى بهم لا بأس به. قوله : خطبتين ؛ كخطبتي الجمعة بينهما قعدة خفيفة، ولا أذان هاهنا ولا عند إقامة.
And he delivers after it two sermons in which he teaches the rulings of al-fitra. His saying: 'and he delivers'; meaning the imam. This indicates the priority of the unity of the imam and the preacher, so if someone other than the one who led them in prayer delivers the sermon, it is permissible. His saying: 'two sermons'; like the two sermons of Jumu'ah with a light sitting between them, and there is no adhan here nor when establishing (the prayer).
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the Eid khutbah. It states that after completing the Eid prayer, the imam delivers two sermons (khutbah), during which he teaches the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr (zakat al-fitr). The commentary explains that the sermon-giver should ideally be the same person who led the prayer, but if a different person gives the sermon, it is still permissible. The format of the two sermons is similar to those of Jumu'ah, including a brief sitting between them. Notably, unlike Jumu'ah, there is no adhan or iqamah for the Eid prayer or the sermons.

Key Terms
الخطبتان (al-khutbatan): The two sermons delivered by the imam after the Eid prayer, containing religious instruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Eid khutbah is a sunnah, not a condition; it is similar to Jumu'ah but without adhan and not required for validity.

Ruling for Missing Eid Prayer with Imam
Ruling for missed Eid prayer with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who misses Eid prayer with the imam and identify the proof and the exception for praying the next day with an excuse.

Core Idea
If you miss Eid prayer with the imam, you do not make it up—except with an excuse, then pray the next day.

Eid prayer is a significant communal obligation. But what happens if you miss it? The Hanafi school has a specific ruling that distinguishes it from regular prayers. This lesson explains the ruling and its basis in the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The text explicitly states 'la yaqdi' (he does not make it up). Note that this applies when both the imam and follower miss it together.
The ruling is that qada' (making up) is not required.
2
Understand the Exception
The text adds that if there is a valid excuse (e.g., rain, late moon sighting), the prayer can be offered the next day. This is not qada' but a concession.
The passive voice 'yusalla' emphasizes the congregational nature.
3
Examine the Proof
The hadith of the obscured moon: after the sighting news arrived, the Prophet ordered the people to go out for Eid prayer the next day.
This hadith is the primary evidence for the next-day prayer with an excuse.
4
Analyze the Rationale
The commentary explains that Eid prayer is only valid with congregation and conditions that an individual cannot fulfill alone.
Hence, it cannot be made up individually like a fard prayer.
5
Compare with Other Schools
Other schools allow individual qada' or consider it sunnah; the Hanafi position is distinctive.
This cross-madhhab insight is useful for understanding the school's methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن فاتته مع الإمام لم يقض ويصلّي غداً بعذر. قوله : مع الإمام ؛ ليس هذا متعلقاً بقوله : «فائتة» ؛ ليفيد أنها فاتت الإمام والمقتدي كليهما، فإنه لو كان كذلك لم يصح قوله : «لم يقض» ؛ لأنَّ الحكم. فوتها من الإمام أيضاً هو القضاء، وكما صرح به في «معراج الدراية»، بل هو متعلق بمحذوف حال من ضمير: «فاتته». قوله : لا يقضي ؛ لأنَّ الصَّلاةَ بهذه الصفة لم تعرف قربةً إلا بشرائط لا تتم بالمنفرد. كذا في «الهداية». وهذا إذا فاتته في مسجد واحد وأمكنه الذهاب إلى إمامٍ آخر فعل، فإنَّها تجوزُ في مصر بمواضع أنفاقاً. كذا في «الدر المختار). قوله : يصلي ؛ بصيغة المجهول، يعني إذا فاتت صلاة العيد في يومه بعذر كمطر مانع عن الخروج وعدم خروج الإمام، ووصول خبرِ رؤية الهلالِ فيه بعد الزَّوالِ أو قبله ، بحيث لا يمكن جمعُ النَّاس عند ذلك يُصلي في اليوم الثاني. والأصل فيه ما روي: «أنه أُغمي هلالُ شوَّالَ في العهد النبوي فأصبحوا صائمين إكمالاً لرمضان، فجاءَ ركب بعد الزوال شهدوا برؤيته فأمرهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يفطروا ، وأن يخرجوا لصلاة العيد من الغد».
And whoever misses it (the Eid prayer) with the imam does not make it up, and he prays the next day with an excuse. His saying: 'with the imam' – this is not attached to his saying 'missed'; to indicate that it missed both the imam and the follower, for if it were so, his saying 'does not make it up' would not be correct because the ruling of missing it for the imam would also be making it up. Rather, it is attached to an omitted word describing the state of the pronoun 'missed him'. His saying: 'does not make it up' – because the prayer in this form is not known to be an act of worship except with conditions that are not fulfilled by an individual. Thus in al-Hidayah. And this is if he missed it in one mosque and it is possible for him to go to another imam, he should do so, for it is permissible in a city in multiple locations. Thus in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. His saying: 'he prays' – in the passive voice, meaning if the Eid prayer on its day is missed due to an excuse such as rain preventing coming out and the imam not coming out, and news of the sighting of the crescent arriving after zawal or before it, such that it is not possible to gather the people for it, then he prays on the following day. The basis for this is what is narrated: 'The crescent of Shawwal was obscured in the prophetic era, so they woke up fasting to complete Ramadan, then a group came after zawal and testified to its sighting, so the Messenger of Allah ﷺ ordered them to break their fast and to go out for the Eid prayer the next day.'
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with its proof concerning the case of a person who misses the Eid prayer with the imam. The text states: the person does not make it up (i.e., they do not pray it later as qada'), but if there is a valid excuse (such as heavy rain preventing the gathering, or the moon sighting news arriving too late to gather people), then they may pray it on the following day (ghadan). The commentary clarifies that 'with the imam' means the prayer was missed by both the imam and the follower; if it were only the follower who missed, they would not make it up because the Eid prayer is not a prayer that can be performed individually (it requires congregation). However, the text also suggests that if one misses it in one mosque, they should try to join another congregation elsewhere. The proof is an incident from the Prophet's ﷺ time when the moon was not sighted, and after news came after zawal, the Prophet ﷺ ordered the prayer to be performed the next day.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after its time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Make it up individually at home
B) Pray it the next day in congregation
C) Do not make it up at all
D) Make it up with another congregation on the same day

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that missed Eid prayer is not made up individually, but may be prayed the next day only with a valid excuse, based on the Prophet's practice.

Ruling on Missed 'Eid Prayer: No Individual Qada
Ruling and evidence for qada of missed 'Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on missed 'Eid prayer and explain the conditions under which it is prayed on the second day.

Core Idea
Missed 'Eid prayer is not made up individually – congregation is essential.

The 'Eid prayer is a wajib act with unique features. Unlike other prayers, if you miss it with the imam, you do not pray it alone. However, there is a concession for late excuses. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the reasoning, and the textual evidence from al-Hidayah and the hadith of the concealed moon.

Guided Path
1
State the two rulings from the matn
Identify that the imam delivers two sermons after the prayer, and that a person who misses the prayer with the imam does not make it up individually.
The ruling on sermons is sunnah; the qada ruling is what we focus on.
2
Understand why no individual qada
The commentator explains that the 'Eid prayer is only known as worship with conditions that cannot be fulfilled by an individual – specifically congregation.
This reasoning is from al-Hidayah.
3
Identify the exceptional case
If there is a valid excuse (e.g., rain, late moon sighting), the prayer may be prayed the next day in congregation.
The proof comes from the hadith of the concealed moon.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet ordered the people to break their fast and go out for 'Eid prayer the next day when news of Shawwal's moon arrived after noon.
This indicates that the prayer is not made up individually but can be delayed one day with congregation.
5
Note the interschool disagreement
Other schools require individual qada. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the condition of congregation.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text

ويخطب بعدها خُطبتين يُعَلِّمُ فيها أحكام الفطرة.

And he (the imam) delivers two sermons in which he teaches the rulings of fitr. And whoever misses it with the imam does not make it up, and he prays the next day due to an excuse. [1] His statement: 'And he delivers' means the imam; he indicates the preference for the imam and the preacher being the same person. If someone else preaches who led them in prayer, there is no harm. [2] His statement: 'two sermons' like the two sermons of Friday with a short sitting between them, and there is no call to prayer here nor iqamah. [3] His statement: 'with the imam' is not related to his word 'Faa'ita' (missed) to indicate that it was missed by both the imam and the follower; otherwise his statement 'does not make it up' would be incorrect, because the ruling of being missed by the imam also is to make it up, as stated in 'Miraj al-Dirayah'; rather it is related to a deleted word, being a state of the pronoun 'missed him'. [4] His statement: 'does not make it up' because prayer in this description is not known as an act of worship except with conditions not fulfilled by an individual; as in al-Hidayah. This is if he misses it in one mosque and it is possible for him to go to another imam, he acts; for it is permissible in a city in multiple places, as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. [0] His statement: 'he prays' in the passive voice, meaning if the 'Eid prayer is missed on its day due to an excuse such as rain preventing coming out, the imam not coming out, or news of the sighting of the moon arriving after midday or before in such a way that gathering people is not possible, then he prays on the second day. The basis for this is what is narrated: 'The moon of Shawwal was concealed in the time of the Prophet, so they woke up fasting to complete Ramadan, then a group of riders came after midday and testified to having seen it, so the Messenger of Allah ordered them to break their fast and to go out for the 'Eid prayer the next day.' This story is reported with different wordings by Ibn Majah, al-Nasa'i, Abu Dawud, Ibn Hibban and others. (1) al-Hidayah (2:79). (2) al-Durr al-Mukhtar (2:176). (3) From Abu 'Umayr ibn Anas ibn Malik: my paternal uncles from the Ansar among the companions of the Messenger of Allah told me: 'The moon of Shawwal was hidden from us, so we woke up fasting, then a group of riders came at the end of the day and testified before the Prophet that they had seen the moon yesterday, so the Messenger of Allah ordered them to break their fast and to go out to their 'Eid the next day' in Sunan Ibn Majah (1:529), al-Sunan al-Saghir (3:245), Tahdhib al-Athar (7:230), Musnad Ahmad (5:57). Our Shaykh al-Arna'ut said: Its chain is good, its narrators are trustworthy, narrators of the two Shaykhs except Abu 'Umayr ibn Anas, from whom the authors of the Sunan other than al-Tirmidhi narrated.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the missed 'Eid prayer. The matn states two key rulings: first, the imam delivers two sermons after the prayer teaching the rulings of fitr (zakat al-fitr), establishing the sunna of having the same person as imam and preacher. Second, if a person misses the 'Eid prayer with the imam, he does not make it up individually. The commentator explains that 'with the imam' does not mean both missed it; rather, the follower missed it while the imam prayed. The reason for not making up individually is that this prayer is only valid with congregational conditions, as stated in al-Hidayah. However, if one misses it in one mosque but can reach another imam, he should do so. Then the text allows praying the next day if there is an excuse, such as rain or late news of moon sighting. The proof is the hadith of the concealed moon in the Prophet's time, where they broke their fast and prayed 'Eid the next day. This shows that the concession of praying on the second day is based on a specific precedent. The commentator also notes that if one misses it for two days, there is no qada on the third day, as the hadith only specifies the second day.

Key Terms
خطبتين (khutbatayn): Two sermons delivered after 'Eid prayer, similar to Friday sermons, with a short sitting between them.
لم يقض (lam yuqdha): The missed 'Eid prayer is not made up individually because the necessary conditions for its validity (congregation) are not met by an individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person misses the 'Eid prayer with the imam without an excuse, what is the ruling regarding making it up according to the Hanafi school?
A) He must make it up individually in the same form.
B) He does not make it up because the conditions for its validity are not met by an individual.
C) He makes it up with a congregation of at least two people.
D) He prays a voluntary prayer instead.

Key Takeaway
The 'Eid prayer is not made up individually because its validity depends on congregation; a missed prayer may be offered the next day only with a valid excuse.

Eating Before the 'Eid al-Adha Prayer: Ruling and Proof
Rulings on eating before 'Eid al-Adha prayer and takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating before the 'Eid al-Adha prayer, identify the supporting hadith, and explain the reasoning behind the chosen view.

Core Idea
Abstaining from eating before the 'Eid al-Adha prayer is recommended, not required; eating before is permissible and not disliked.

While 'Eid al-Adha shares most rulings with 'Eid al-Fitr, there is a key difference regarding the timeliness of eating. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that it is mustahabb (recommended) to abstain from eating on 'Eid al-Adha until after the prayer, but that eating before the prayer is not makruh (disliked). We will explore the hadith evidence and the refutation of the alternative view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What is the specific act being ruled upon? For 'Eid al-Adha, the act is eating before the 'Eid prayer. The matn states that abstention (imsaak) is recommended, and eating before is not disliked.
The ruling is for the person who will perform the 'Eid prayer; villagers have a different rule.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof cited is the hadith of Buraydah (radiAllahu anhu) recorded in Ibn Majah and others: the Prophet would not eat on 'Eid al-Adha until he sacrificed. This indicates the practice of abstaining.
The chain is hasan (sound) as per Ibn Hajar.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The hadith shows the Prophet's consistent action (fi'l). In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's actions (fi'l) can indicate recommendation (nadb) unless there is evidence of obligation. Here, the action is not accompanied by a command, so it indicates istihbab.
The hadith also shows the contrast with 'Eid al-Fitr, where he would eat before praying.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars (and perhaps others) held that eating before the 'Eid al-Adha prayer is makruh. The commentator refutes this, stating that leaving a recommended act does not entail dislike; specific evidence would be needed.
The author declares the view that it is not disliked as 'al-mukhtar' (the chosen view).
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The chosen view is that it is mustahabb to abstain, but eating before is permissible without karahah. This is supported by the hadith and the principle that absence of a recommendation does not imply prohibition.
The authority for this tarjih is the commentator and the reference to al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

And al-Adha is like al-Fitr in rulings, but here abstaining until he prays is recommended, and eating before it is not disliked, and that is the chosen view, and he says the takbir loudly on the way. [1] His statement: 'Not after it' means if he misses it on both days, it is not made up on the third day, because analogically it would not be made up at all like Friday, except we set that aside for the second day due to the hadith, and it does not exist after that. [2] His statement: 'al-Adha' means the 'Eid of Adha, which is the tenth of Dhul Hijjah, and it is like 'Eid al-Fitr in the previous rulings except that there is a difference in some of them, so he makes an exception with 'but...' etc. [3] His statement: 'abstention' means from eating, and it is reported from the Messenger of Allah in Sunan Ibn Majah, Jami' al-Tirmidhi, and others. [4] His statement: 'until he prays' means the 'Eid prayer, then he sacrifices his animal and eats from it. [6] His statement: 'loudly' is related from Ibn Umar, and for 'Eid al-Fitr it is also confirmed from him saying it loudly, reported by al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi. Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage continues the rulings on 'Eid prayer. The matn states that if the 'Eid prayer is missed on both days (first and second), it is not made up on the third day. This is because analogically it would not be made up at all, like Friday, but the hadith allows it on the second day only. Then it affirms that 'Eid al-Adha shares most rulings with 'Eid al-Fitr, but with some differences. The main difference mentioned is that on 'Eid al-Adha, it is mustahabb (recommended) to abstain from eating until after the 'Eid prayer, so that one can eat from the sacrificial animal. This is supported by the hadith of Buraydah that the Prophet would not eat on 'Eid al-Adha until he sacrificed. The commentator clarifies that abstaining is not obligatory; the chosen view is that eating before the prayer is not disliked (makruh). Another difference is that saying takbir loudly on the way to the prayer is established for both 'Eids from Ibn Umar. The passage also distinguishes between city and village dwellers regarding when they may eat: city dwellers wait until after prayer and sacrifice, while villagers may eat from dawn because animals are slaughtered earlier. Overall, the passage provides specific rulings for 'Eid al-Adha that differ from 'Eid al-Fitr, emphasizing the recommended nature of abstaining and the permissibility of eating before the prayer without karahah.

Key Terms
الإمساك (al-imsaak): Abstaining from eating on 'Eid al-Adha until after the 'Eid prayer.
المختار (al-mukhtaar): The chosen and relied-upon view that eating before the 'Eid al-Adha prayer is not disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is mustahabb to eat before the prayer.
B) It is makruh to eat before the prayer.
C) It is not makruh; it is permissible and abstaining is recommended.
D) It is haram to eat before the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Abstaining from eating before the 'Eid al-Adha prayer is recommended (mustahabb) but eating before is permissible and not disliked, based on the Prophet's practice.

Eid al-Adha: Eating Before the Prayer and Loud Takbir
Ruling on differences between Eid al-Adha and Eid al-Fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on eating before the Eid al-Adha prayer and on reciting takbir loudly, identify the evidence for each, and explain why eating before the prayer is not disliked.

Core Idea
Refraining from eating before Eid al-Adha prayer is recommended, not disliked; loud takbir on the way is a sunnah.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah highlights the differences between Eid al-Adha and Eid al-Fitr. While they share most rulings, for Eid al-Adha it is recommended to abstain from eating until after the prayer, but eating beforehand is not disliked. The passage also instructs reciting takbir loudly on the way to the prayer, a practice supported by the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main act and its ruling
The passage first addresses eating before the Eid al-Adha prayer. It states that refraining from eating is recommended (nudiba), and eating is not disliked (la yukrahu). The chosen view (al-mukhtar) is that it is not makruh.
This is a key difference from Eid al-Fitr, where it is sunnah to eat before the prayer.
2
Locate the evidence for the eating ruling
The evidence is the hadith from Buraidah in Sunan Ibn Majah and others: the Prophet would not eat on Nahr until he sacrificed. This indicates a recommended practice, not an obligation.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the ruling remains at the level of sunnah, not fard.
3
Analyze the implication of the evidence
The Prophet's action shows constancy, but without an imperative, it establishes recommendation (nadb). Leaving a recommended act does not entail dislike (karahah) unless there is specific evidence, which is lacking here.
This refutes the view of those who consider it makruh.
4
Note the exceptional ruling for village dwellers
The commentary notes that a villager (qarawi) may eat from the morning because sacrifices are done earlier in villages. This is a concession based on custom and necessity.
The city dweller (misri) should wait until after the prayer and sacrifice.
5
State the ruling on loud takbir
The passage states 'يكبر جهراً في الطريق' (he recites takbir loudly on the way). This is a sunnah practice, reported from Ibn Umar and others, and also confirmed for Eid al-Fitr.
Loud takbir is a sign of the Eid celebration and is recommended from leaving home until the prayer begins.

Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on the two Eids. It states that Eid al-Adha is like Eid al-Fitr in rulings except that here (for Eid al-Adha) it is recommended (nudiba) to refrain from eating until one prays, and it is not disliked to eat before the prayer, and that is the chosen view (al-mukhtar). Also, one recites takbir loudly on the way. The commentary explains: 'لا بعده' means that if one misses the Eid prayer on the two days, it is not made up on the third day because by analogy it would not be made up at all like Jumu'ah, but we abandoned analogy for the second day due to a hadith, and no such hadith exists after that. 'والأضحى' means Eid al-Adha, which is the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, and it is like Eid al-Fitr in the previous rulings except for some differences, hence the author says 'but'. 'الإمساك' means refraining from eating, and it is narrated from the Prophet in Sunan Ibn Majah and Jami' al-Tirmidhi. The ruling applies to the city dweller (misri); for the village dweller (qarawi), he may eat from the morning because sacrifices are slaughtered in villages from the morning. 'وهو المختار' refers to the view that it is not disliked; some said it is makruh, but the author refutes this because leaving a recommended act does not entail karahah; a specific evidence would be needed. 'جهراً' means loudly, and it is reported from Ibn Umar, and for Eid al-Fitr loud takbir is also reported by Darqutni and Bayhaqi. The footnote adds a hadith from Buraidah that the Prophet would not go out on Fitr until he ate, and on Nahr until he sacrificed.

Key Terms
الإمساك (al-imsaak): Refraining from eating and drinking; here specifically from eating before the Eid prayer.
المختار (al-mukhtaar): The chosen view among the Hanafi scholars; the relied-upon position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on eating before the Eid al-Adha prayer?
A) It is obligatory to refrain from eating.
B) It is recommended to refrain from eating, and eating before is not disliked.
C) It is makruh tahrimi to eat before.
D) It is haram to eat before.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that refraining from eating before the Eid al-Adha prayer is recommended, not obligatory, and eating is not disliked; reciting takbir loudly on the way is a sunnah practice.

Rulings on Takbir al-Tashriq, Eid Prayer Time, and Arafah Gathering
Rulings on takbir, prayer time, Arafah gathering.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on takbirat al-tashriq, the permissible days for Eid prayer, and the legal status of gathering on Arafah, and identify the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Takbirat al-tashriq are wajib; Eid prayer can be delayed up to three days; Arafah gathering imitation is not virtuous.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah presents key rulings related to Eid al-Adha: the obligation of takbirat al-tashriq, the time window for the Eid prayer, and the status of gathering on the day of Arafah. We will unpack each ruling, noting the Hanafi position and the evidence provided, so you can apply them in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify each ruling
List the three distinct rulings in the passage: (1) teaching takbir and sacrifice in the sermon, (2) time for Eid prayer, (3) gathering on Arafah, and (4) obligation of takbirat al-tashriq. Note that the first is about the imam's sermon.
Focus on the substantive rulings: prayer time, Arafah gathering, and takbir obligation.
2
Analyze the evidence for takbirat al-tashriq
The text mentions a dispute: majority say wajib, some say sunnah (based on the Prophet's continuous practice). Identify the Hanafi position: the relied-upon view is wujub, as per Fath al-Qadir.
The evidence for sunnah is mudawamah (continuity); the majority (including Hanafis) give precedence to other proofs.
3
Examine the time for Eid prayer
The passage states that the Eid al-Adha prayer is permissible on the 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul Hijjah, but delaying beyond the 10th without excuse is sinful because of the established sunnah.
Delaying intentionally without valid reason is makruh tahrimi or sinful.
4
Evaluate the ruling on gathering on Arafah
The text says gathering on the day of Arafah (9th) in imitation of pilgrims is 'not anything' – meaning it is not a Shariah-recognized act of worship entailing reward. Some say it is makruh if done for imitation.
The phrase 'ليس بشيء' negates its validity as a meritorious act, not its physical existence.
5
Summarize practical implications
Combine the rulings: The imam teaches takbir and sacrifice in the sermon; the prayer can be performed on 10th-12th; takbir is recited aloud after fard prayers during the days of tashriq; and gathering on Arafah for imitation is not a virtuous act.
These are specific to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُعَلِّمُ في الخطبة تكبير التشريق ، والأضحية ويصلّي بعذر أو بغيره أيامها لا بعدها، والاجتماع يوم عرفة تشبها بالواقفين ليس بشيء وتجب تكبيرات التشريق [1] قوله : تكبيرات ؛ أي الأحكام المتعلقة بتكبير التشريق، وأحكام الأضحية. [٢]قوله : والأضحية ؛ بضم الهمزة، وكسر الحاء المهملة، بينهما ضاد معجمة ساكنة، وأصله أضحوية على وزن أفعولة ، وهم اسم لما يذبح تقرباً في أَيَّامِ النَّحْرِ من عاشر ذي الحجة إلى الثاني عشر. (۳) قوله : ويصلي ... الخ ؛ يعني تجوز صلاة عيد الأضحى في أيام الأضحية، وهي العاشر والحادي عشر والثاني عشر لا بعدها ؛ لأنها مؤقتة بوقت الأضحية، نعم إن أخَّرها عن العاشر بغير عذر أساء ؛ لمخالفة السنة الثابتة. كذا في «البناية». [٤] قوله : تشبهاً بالواقفين؛ أي لحصول المشابهة بالحجاج الواقفين بعرفات يوم عرفة، وهو بفتحات : اسم التاسع من ذي الحجة. [٥]قوله : أي ليس بشيء ؛ أشار إلى أنه ليس المراد نفي الشيئية مطلقاً، فإنّه غيرُ صحيح، وغير لائق لأن يذكرَهُ الفقيه، بل نفي كونه معتبراً شرعاً، وهو ما يترتب عليه الثواب. [٦]قوله : فلا ؛ أي لم يعرف كونه قربة فلا يكون واجباً ولا مستحباً، نعم ؛ يكون مباحاً، ومنهم من قال : إنه مكروه إن كان للتشبه بالحجاج الواقفين. [۷]قوله : وتجب ؛ قال في «فتح القدير» (۱) : اختلف في أنها واجبة أو سُنَّة ، والأكثر على أنها واجبة، ودليل السنية مواظبته . [۸] قوله : تكبيرات التشريق ؛ هو مصدر شرق اللحم : إذا بسط في الشمس ليجف ؛ لأنهم كانوا يشرقون فيه اللحم، وأضيفت إليه التكبيرات ؛ لوقوعها في أيامه ، وقبل التشريق الجهر بالتكبير.
And he teaches in the sermon the takbir al-tashriq, and the sacrifice. And he prays, with or without excuse, during its days, not after it. And gathering on the day of Arafah in imitation of those standing (at Arafah) is nothing. And takbirat al-tashriq are obligatory. [1] His saying: 'takbirat' means the rulings related to takbir al-tashriq and the rulings of the sacrifice. [2] His saying: 'the sacrifice' is with dammah on the hamzah and kasrah on the ha, between them a silent dad, its original is 'adhawiyyah' on the pattern of 'af'uulah, and it is a name for what is slaughtered as an act of drawing near on the days of sacrifice from the 10th of Dhul Hijjah to the 12th. (3) His saying: 'and he prays... etc.' means the Eid al-Adha prayer is permissible during the days of sacrifice, which are the 10th, 11th, and 12th, not after them, because it is time-bound to the time of the sacrifice. Yes, if he delays it beyond the 10th without an excuse, he sins because he violates the established sunnah. So in al-Binayah. [4] His saying: 'in imitation of those standing' means achieving resemblance to the pilgrims standing at Arafah on the day of Arafah, which with fatha is the name of the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. [5] His saying: 'that is not anything' indicated that what is meant is not the negation of thingness absolutely, for that is incorrect and unbecoming for a faqih to mention; rather it is the negation of it being considered valid in the Shariah, which is that reward is attached to it. [6] His saying: 'so not' means it is not known to be a supererogatory act, so it is neither obligatory nor recommended; rather it is permissible. And some say: it is disliked if done to imitate the standing pilgrims. [7] His saying: 'and are obligatory' said in Fath al-Qadir: There is disagreement over whether they are obligatory or sunnah, and the majority are that they are obligatory, and the evidence for sunnah is his (the Prophet's) continuity. [8] His saying: 'takbirat al-tashriq' is the verbal noun from 'sharaqa al-lahm' when it is spread in the sun to dry, because they used to dry the meat during that time. The takbirat are attributed to it because they occur during its days, and before tashriq the takbir is said loudly.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings related to Eid al-Adha. First, the imam teaches takbir al-tashriq and the rulings of the sacrifice in the Eid sermon. Second, the Eid prayer is valid on the days of sacrifice (10th–12th of Dhul Hijjah), not after; if one delays it beyond the 10th without excuse, it is sinful. Third, gathering on the day of Arafah (9th) to imitate the pilgrims standing at Arafah is 'not anything'—meaning it is not considered a virtuous act entailing reward. The commentary explains that it is not absolutely nothing in the sense of nonexistent, but rather not recognized by the Shariah as a meritorious act. It is either permissible (mubah) or makruh if done for imitation. Fourth, takbirat al-tashriq are obligatory (wajib) according to the majority, though some say sunnah; the evidence for sunnah is the Prophet's continuous practice. The text also defines 'al-udhiyyah' (sacrifice) linguistically and explains the etymology of 'tashriq' as drying meat in the sun.

Key Terms
تكبيرات التشريق (takbiraat al-tashriiq): Loud recitation of 'Allahu Akbar' during the days of tashriq (11th-13th of Dhul Hijjah) after every fard prayer, traditionally associated with drying meat.
الأضحية (al-udhiyyah): The animal slaughtered as a sacrifice on the days of Nahr (10th-12th of Dhul Hijjah) to draw near to Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is a recommended act of worship.
B) It is obligatory.
C) It is considered nothing by the Shariah, not entailing reward.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Takbirat al-tashriq are wajib; Eid prayer is valid on 10th-12th; gathering on Arafah for imitation is not a meritorious act.

The Obligation and Wording of Takbirat al-Tashriq
Ruling on the obligatory nature and wording of takbirat al-tashriq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact wording of takbirat al-tashriq and identify its ruling (wajib) in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Takbirat al-tashriq are wajib after every fard prayer, with a specific formulation that is agreed upon.

Takbirat al-tashriq are a distinctive feature of the days of Eid al-Adha. In this lesson, we examine the ruling and the precise formulation as taught by the Hanafi school, focusing on the obligation and wording.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text explicitly states 'تجب' (are obligatory). Note that the ruling is wajib, not fard, because the evidence is zanni in Hanafi usul.
The distinction between wajib and fard affects the level of sin if omitted.
2
Memorize the wording
The text provides the exact Arabic: 'الله أكبر الله أكبر، لا إله إلا الله، والله أكبر الله أكبر، ولله الحمد'. This is the standard Hanafi formulation.
Some have slight variations, but this is the most authenticated.
3
Note the time frame
The takbirs begin from Fajr of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah). The end time is disputed (covered in next lesson), but the text mentions 'to Asr of the Eid day' as Abu Hanifa's view and 'to Asr of the last day of tashriq' as the relied-upon view.
This lesson focuses on the obligation and wording; the time dispute will be detailed separately.
4
Recognize the conditions for obligation
The takbirs are wajib after each fard prayer performed in a 'mustahabb' congregation (i.e., a congregation that is recommended, such as for men). The text specifies conditions: resident in the city, a woman following a man, and a traveler following a resident.
These conditions are shurut al-wujub (conditions of obligation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُعَلِّمُ في الخطبة تكبير التشريق ، والأضحية ويصلّي بعذر أو بغيره أيامها لا بعدها، والاجتماع يوم عرفة تشبها بالواقفين ليس بشيء وتجب تكبيرات التشريق ويُعَلِّمُ في الخطبة تكبيرات التشريق ، والأضحية . ويصلي بعذر أو بغيره أيامها لا بعدها، والاجتماع يوم عرفة تشبها بالواقفين ليس بشيء ) : أي ليس بشيء معتبر يتعلق به الثواب ، فإنَّ الوقوف في مكان مخصوص ، وهو عرفات قد عُرِفَ قُربة، وأما في غيرها فلا . وتجب تكبيرات التشريق ) وهو قوله : الله أكبر الله اكبر ، لا إله إلا الله، والله أكبر الله أكبر، ولله الحمد، من فجر عرفة عُقَيْب كلِّ فرض أُدّي بجماعة مستحبة على المقيم بالمصر، ومقتدية برَجُل، ومسافر مقتد بمقيم إلى عصرِ العيد، وقالا : إلى عصر آخر أيام التشريق ، وبه يعمل، ولا يدعه المؤتم . وهو قوله : الله أكبر الله اكبر لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر الله أكبر، ولله الحمد، من فجر عرفة عقيب كلِّ فرض أُدِّي بجماعة مستحبة احتراز عن جماعة النساء وحدهن على المقيم بالمصر، ومقتدية برَجُل ، ومسافر مقتد بمقيم إلى عصر العيد، وقالا : إلى عصرِ آخر أيام التشريق، وبه يعمل ، ولا يدعه المؤتم ، من ولو ترك إمامه. والله أعلم .
And he teaches in the khutbah the takbir of tashriq and the sacrifice. And he prays with or without excuse during its days, not after them. And the gathering on the day of Arafah in imitation of those standing (at Arafah) is nothing. And the takbirs of tashriq are obligatory. And he teaches in the khutbah the takbirs of tashriq and the sacrifice. 'And he prays with or without excuse during its days, not after them, and the gathering on the day of Arafah in imitation of those standing is nothing' – meaning it is not a matter of consideration by which reward is attached, for standing in a specific place, which is Arafat, is known to be a form of worship, but at other than it, it is not. 'And the takbirs of tashriq are obligatory' – and it is his saying: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illa Allah, Wa Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, Wa lillahi al-hamd, from the dawn of Arafah following every obligatory prayer performed in a congregational group that is recommended, upon the resident in the city, and a woman following a man, and a traveler following a resident, until the Asr of the Eid day. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: until the Asr of the last day of tashriq. And according to it (their view) practice is done, and the follower does not abandon it even if his imam leaves it. And it is his saying: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illa Allah, Wa Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, Wa lillahi al-hamd, from the dawn of Arafah following every obligatory prayer performed in a congregation that is recommended, as a precaution against the congregation of women alone, upon the resident in the city, and a woman following a man, and a traveler following a resident, until the Asr of the Eid day. And the two said: until the Asr of the last day of tashriq. And according to it practice is done, and the follower does not abandon it even if his imam leaves it. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on takbirat al-tashriq, the takbirs said during the days of tashriq (11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah). The author first mentions that the imam teaches these takbirs in the khutbah. Then he addresses a related ruling: the Eid prayer can be performed on the days of sacrifice (10th, 11th, 12th) with or without excuse, but not after. A separate point: gathering on the day of Arafah (9th) in imitation of pilgrims standing at Arafah is not a meritorious act, because the virtue is specific to the actual location of Arafat. Then the main ruling: takbirat al-tashriq are wajib (obligatory). The wording is given: 'Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illa Allah, Wa Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, Wa lillahi al-hamd'. The time begins from Fajr of the day of Arafah (9th) and continues after every obligatory prayer performed in a congregation that is mustahabb (recommended group). It is obligatory upon: (1) a resident in the city, (2) a woman who follows a man (i.e., prays behind a male imam), (3) a traveler who follows a resident imam. The end time according to Imam Abu Hanifa is Asr of the Eid day (10th). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), it ends at Asr of the last day of tashriq (13th). The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is the view of the Sahibayn, as indicated by 'wa bihi ya'mal' (and according to it practice is done). The follower does not abandon the takbirs even if his imam leaves them, meaning the follower should still recite them himself. The proof for the wording is that it is narrated from the Prophet ﷺ and from the Companions (Umar, Ibn Mas'ud, Ali, Ibn Abbas) that they used to say these words after prayers during these days.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbīr al-tashrīq): The specific phrases of Allahu Akbar etc. recited after obligatory prayers from Fajr of Arafah until Asr of the last day of tashriq (in the relied-upon view).
أيام التشريق (ayyām al-tashrīq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah, days following Eid al-Adha when meat is dried (tashriq).
مستحبة (mustaḥabbah): Recommended congregational prayer, as opposed to a mere permissible congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) الله أكبر الله أكبر، لا إله إلا الله، والله أكبر الله أكبر، ولله الحمد
B) الله أكبر كبيراً والحمد لله كثيراً
C) سبحان الله والحمد لله ولا إله إلا الله والله أكبر
D) لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر ولله الحمد

Key Takeaway
Takbirat al-tashriq are wajib after every fard prayer in a mustahabb congregation, with a specific wording, from Fajr of Arafah until Asr of the last tashriq day (mufta bihi).

Takbir of Tashriq: Wording and Timing
Ruling on the wording and timing of takbir tashriq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wording and timing of the takbir of tashriq according to the Hanafi school and identify the relied-upon position regarding its duration.

Core Idea
The takbir of tashriq, recited from Fajr of Arafah until Asr of the last day of Tashriq, is a confirmed sunnah for those praying in congregation.

This lesson examines the ruling on the takbir of tashriq, a special magnification recited after obligatory prayers during the days of Eid and Tashriq. The source passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the wording, timing, and who is obligated to recite it, along with an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the end time. Understanding this ruling ensures you perform this sunnah correctly according to the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wording of the takbir
State the exact phrases as given in the matn: 'Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar, la ilaha illa Allah, wa Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar, wa lillahi al-hamd'.
This is the established wording transmitted from the Prophet.
2
Determine the starting time
The text states 'min fajr 'Arafah'.
It begins from Fajr of the Day of Arafah (9th of Dhul Hijjah).
3
Determine the ending time
Note the difference: Abu Hanifa said until Asr of Eid (10th), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said until Asr of the last day of Tashriq (13th). The text says 'wa bihi ya'mal' – the relied-upon position is the latter.
The mufta bihi is until Asr of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
4
Identify who must recite it
It is recommended for: a resident in the city, a woman following a man in congregation, and a traveler following a resident imam. It excludes the congregation of women alone, which is makruh.
The follower must recite even if the imam leaves it.
5
Apply the rule for followers
The text explicitly says 'wa la yada'uhu al-mu'tam' – the follower should not abandon the takbir even if the imam does.
This includes the case where the imam forgets or deliberately leaves it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب العيدين
وهو قوله : الله أكبر الله اكبر ، لا إله إلا الله، والله أكبر الله أكبر، ولله الحمد، من فجر عرفة عُقَيْب كلِّ فرض أُدّي بجماعة مستحبة على المقيم بالمصر، ومقتدية برَجُل، ومسافر مقتد بمقيم إلى عصرِ العيد، وقالا : إلى عصر آخر أيام التشريق ، وبه يعمل، ولا يدعه المؤتم
وهو قوله : الله أكبر الله اكبر لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر الله أكبر، ولله الحمد، من فجر عرفة عقيب كلِّ فرض أُدِّي" بجماعة مستحبة) احتراز " عن جماعة النساء وحدهن على المقيم بالمصر، ومقتدية برَجُل ، ومسافر مقتد بمقيم إلى عصر العيد، وقالا : إلى عصرِ آخر أيام التشريق، وبه يعمل ، ولا يدعه المؤتم ) ،
ولو ترك إمامه. والله أعلم . ١ ] قوله : وهو قوله ؛ الضمير إلى القائل، المستفاد من القول أو إلى المكبر المستفاد التكبير، وهذه الألفاظ هي المأثور عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه كان يكبرُ بهنَّ بعدَ الصَّلاةِ من غداة عرفة إلى عصرِ أيَّامِ التشريق ، أخرجه ابن أبي الدنيا. وكذلك روى عن عمر الله عند ابن أبي شَيْبَة، وابن أبي الدنيا، وعن ابن مسعود له أيضاً عندهما ، وعن علي وابن عباس له وغيرهما، وقد بسطنا كل ذلك في سباحة الفكر في الجهر بالذكر». [٢] قوله : أدي ؛ بصيغة المجهول صفةٌ لفرض ، واحترز به عن القضاء، وإن كان بجماعة إلا أن يكون قضاء صلاةٍ من صلواتِ أيَّامِ التَّشريق من ذلك العام فيها. كذا في «البحر»، وغيره.
[٣] قوله : احتراز ؛ يعني التَّقييد بقوله : «مستحبه» ؛ احتراز عن جماعة النساء فإنها ليست مستحبة ، بل مكروهة عند أكثر أصحابنا كما مرّ. [ ] قوله : ومقتدية ؛ يعني المرأة المقتدية بالرجل، فتجب عليها بالتبعية، لكنّها لا تجهر، بل تقولها سراً. [0] قوله : مسافر مقتد بمقيم ؛ فتجب عليه تبعاً، وفي عكسه تجب على المؤتم دون الإمام.
[٦] قوله : وبه يعمل ؛ بصيغة المجهول، وهو من علامات الفتوى ؛ وذلك لكونه موافقاً الأخبار والآثار كما أشرنا إليه.
(1) وفي (الملتقى» (ص ٢٥) : وعليه العمل، وفي الدر المختار (١) : (٥٦٤) : وعليه الاعتماد والعمل والفتوى في عامة الأمصار وكافة الأعصار، ولكن رجّح صاحب «الفتح» (٢ : ٤٩) قوله.
Book of Prayer, Chapter of the Two Eids. And it is his saying: Allah is Greatest, Allah is Greatest, there is no god but Allah, and Allah is Greatest, Allah is Greatest, and to Allah is all praise, from the dawn of Arafah immediately after every obligatory prayer performed in congregation – recommended – for the resident in the city, and a woman following a man, and a traveler following a resident, until the afternoon of Eid. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: until the afternoon of the last day of Tashriq, and it is acted upon, and the follower should not leave it even if his imam leaves it.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the takbir of tashriq, specifically its wording and timing. The matn states that the takbir is recited from Fajr of the Day of Arafah until Asr of the day of Eid, immediately after every fard prayer performed in congregation, and it is mustahabb (recommended). It applies to a resident in the city, a woman following a man (by being in congregation with him), and a traveler following a resident imam. The commentary explains that the wording is the established one from the Prophet (PBUH), as reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya and others. It clarifies that 'performed' (أدي) refers to ada' (timely performance), not qada' (make-up), unless the make-up is for a prayer of the days of Tashriq of that same year. The condition 'recommended' (مستحبة) excludes the congregation of women alone, which is makruh according to most of our scholars. The woman following a man must say the takbir silently. The traveler following a resident must also say it, but in the opposite case, only the follower says it, not the imam. Regarding the timing, Abu Hanifa says until Asr of Eid, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say until Asr of the last day of Tashriq; the relied-upon position is that of the two, and it is the basis for fatwa. The follower should not abandon the takbir even if his imam does.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): Specific phrases of magnification recited after obligatory prayers during the days of tashriq
مستحبة (mustahabbah): Recommended; an act whose performance is desirable but not obligatory
مقتدية (muqtadiyah): A woman who follows a man in prayer (as a muqtadi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, until when is the takbir of tashriq recited?
A) Until the Asr of the day of Eid
B) Until the Asr of the last day of Tashriq
C) Until the Maghrib of the last day of Tashriq
D) Until the Fajr of the last day of Tashriq

Key Takeaway
The takbir of tashriq is a confirmed sunnah recited after each fard prayer from Fajr of Arafah until Asr of the last day of Tashriq, and the follower must recite it even if the imam leaves it.
