The Method of Fear Prayer When Danger Is Intense
Ruling on the method of fear prayer when danger is intense

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf when fear is intense, identify the conditions, and explain why the first group prays without recitation.

Core Idea
In Salat al-Khawf, the first group completes without recitation because they are laggards (lahiq), while the second group recites because they are preceded (masbuq).

Salat al-Khawf is a concession allowing Muslims to pray in congregation even during battle. The classical Hanafi texts describe a specific sequence where the imam leads two groups alternately. This passage from the commentary explains the ruling and the underlying rationale based on the follower's prohibition of recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The passage begins with 'When the fear of an enemy intensifies'. Recognize that this describes a situation of active danger, but intense fear is not a condition; mere proximity of the enemy suffices.
The commentary clarifies that ishtidad (intensity) is not a condition.
2
Describe the Imam's Actions
The imam first prays part of the prayer with one group (the first group), then sends them to face the enemy. He then brings the second group and prays the remaining portion with them, then says salam alone.
The imam's rak'ahs depend on whether he is travelling (2 rak'ahs total) or resident (4 rak'ahs total).
3
Distinguish Lahiq and Masbuq
The first group are lahiq (follower who joins later) — they are considered followers for the part they missed, so they do not recite. The second group are masbuq (preceded) — they missed the beginning and must recite when they complete individually after the imam's salam.
This distinction is key to understanding why the first group completes without recitation.
4
Note the Flexibility
The commentary mentions that other methods of Salat al-Khawf are also reported from the Prophet, so the matter is broad. The method described is one valid sunnah form.
This method is from the zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الخوف
إذا اشتد خوفُ عدو جعلَ الإمامُ النَّاسَ أُمَّةً نحو العدو، وصلى بأخرى ركعة إن كان مسافراً ، وركعتين إن كان مقيماً ، ومَضَت هذه إليه وجاءت تلك، وصلى بهم ما بقي وسلم وحدَه ، وذهبت إليه وجاءت الأولى ، وأتمت بلا قراءة باب صلاة الخوف
(إذا اشتد خوفُ عدو جعلَ الإمامُ النَّاسَ أُمَّةً نحو العدو، وصلى بأخرى ركعة إن كان مسافراً ، وركعتين إن كان مقيماً ، ومَضَت هذه إليه) : أي ذهبت هذه الطائفة إلى العدو، (وجاءت تلك ، وصلى بهم ما بقي وسلَّمَ وحدَه ، وذهبَتْ إليه) : أي ذهبت هذه الطَّائفة إلى العدوّ ، وجاءت الأولى ، وأتمت" بلا قراءة [1] قوله : إذا اشتد ؛ قال في «البناية» (۱) : اشتداد الخوف ليس بشرط عند عامة العلماء من أصحابنا، فإنَّه جعل في «التحفة» و«المبسوط» و «المحيط» سبب جوازها نفس قرب العدو من غير ذكر الاشتداد.
[٢] قوله : جعل الإمام ؛ هذه الكيفية رويت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من حديث ابنِ مسعود » في «سنن أبي داود»، ومن حديث ابن عمر ) في الصحاح الستة، وقد ثبت عنه كيفيات أخرى أيضاً، فالأمر واسع.
[٣]قوله : وأتمت ؛ أي صلوا ما بقي من غير قراءة القرآن، وهذا بناء على ما أصله أصحابنا أنَّ المقتدي محجورٌ عن القراءة لكون قراءة الإمام قراءة له ، واللاحق في حكم المقتدي ، فإن من المعلوم أنَّ الطائفة الأولى لاحقة، ولكونها أدركت أول صلاة الإمام فتؤدي ما بقي بدون قراءة بخلاف الأخرى، فإنّها مسبوقة لفوتها أوَّلَ الصَّلاة، فتتم مع القراءة.
Chapter of the Prayer of Fear. When the fear of an enemy intensifies, the imam makes the people into one group facing the enemy, and prays with another group one rak'ah if he is a traveler, and two rak'ahs if he is a resident, then this group goes to him (the enemy) and that group comes, and he prays with them what remains and says the salam by himself, then this group goes to him and the first group comes, and they complete without recitation.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the method of Salat al-Khawf (fear prayer) when danger is severe. The matn describes a specific sequence: the imam divides the people into two groups. One group faces the enemy while the imam leads the other group in prayer. If the imam is a traveler, he prays one rak'ah with them; if resident, two rak'ahs. Then this group goes to face the enemy, and the other group comes. The imam prays with them what remains of his prayer and says salam alone. Then this group goes to the enemy, the first group returns and completes their remaining rak'ahs without recitation. The commentary explains that intense fear is not a condition according to most of our scholars; the mere proximity of the enemy suffices. This method is established from hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar, and other methods are also reported, so there is flexibility. The first group completes without recitation because they are laggards (lahiq) and in the status of followers, who are prohibited from reciting as the imam's recitation suffices. The second group, however, are preceded (masbuq) and must recite when they complete their own prayer.

Key Terms
لاحق (lahiq): A latecomer who joins the imam after the first rak'ah but still in the same prayer
مسبوق (masbuq): One who misses part of the prayer with the imam and must complete it after the imam's salam
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khawf): Fear prayer; a special form of congregational prayer offered during battle or danger

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the first group (the one that prayed the first part with the imam) complete their prayer without recitation?
A) Because they are women
B) Because they are considered laggards (lahiq) and followers are prohibited from reciting
C) Because the imam already recited for them
D) Because they were facing the enemy

Key Takeaway
In Salat al-Khawf, the first group completes without recitation because they are lahiq, while the second group recites because they are masbuq.

Salat al-Khawf: Procedure and Rulings
Explanation of the form and rulings of salat al-khawf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for salat al-khawf and explain why the first group completes without recitation while the second group recites.

Core Idea
In salat al-khawf, the first group are lahiq (cannot recite); the second are masbuq (must recite).

Salat al-khawf is a special congregational prayer performed during battle or imminent danger. The Hanafi school has a detailed procedure based on the Prophet's practice. This lesson unpacks the matn and commentary, explaining the roles of the two groups and the rationale behind their recitation rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for salat al-khawf
Note that the matn says 'when fear intensifies,' but the Hanafi school does not require intensity; proximity of the enemy suffices.
The commentator clarifies that 'intensity' is not a condition according to the majority of Hanafi scholars.
2
Describe the division of groups
The Imam divides the people into two groups: one faces the enemy, the other prays with him. The Imam's prayer length depends on his travel status.
The Imam prays one rak'ah if a traveler, two if a resident, regardless of the obligatory prayer's normal length.
3
Explain the Imam's prayer with the second group
After the first group completes its portion and goes to the enemy, the Imam leads the second group in the remaining part of the prayer and then says salam alone.
The Imam's prayer is curtailed according to his status; the followers complete their own prayers afterward.
4
Analyze the completion by each group
The first group (lahiq) completes without recitation because they are bound by the Imam's recitation. The second group (masbuq) completes with recitation because they missed part of the prayer.
This distinction is a key Hanafi ruling: a lahiq does not recite behind the Imam; a masbuq recites in the missed rak'ahs.
5
Identify the proof and its interpretation
The hadith of Ibn Umar (Bukhari) provides the basis. The Hanafi school interprets the Prophet's actions as establishing this specific form, while other schools may derive different forms.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the exact procedure is subject to ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(۲) ((النقاية»(ص٤٣).
Chapter of the Prayer of Fear. When fear of the enemy intensifies, the Imam makes the people into one group facing the enemy, and he prays with another group one rak'ah if he is a traveler, and two rak'ahs if he is a resident, and this group goes to him and that group comes, and he prays with them what remains and says salam alone, and they go to him and the first group comes and completes without recitation. Then the other group with recitation, and in Maghrib he prays with the first two rak'ahs and with the other one rak'ah. Then the other with recitation, and in Maghrib he prays with the first two rak'ahs and with the other one rak'ah. Know that he did not mention Fajr but its ruling is understood from the ruling of the traveler, so the good expression is what was refined in al-Mukhtasar, which is his saying: He prays with another one rak'ah in the double (al-thuna'i), and two rak'ahs in other than it. So al-thuna'i includes Fajr, the Zuhr of the traveler, his Asr and Isha, and in other than al-thuna'i includes the triple: i.e., Maghrib, and Zuhr, Asr, and Isha of the resident.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the prayer of fear (salat al-khawf). It begins by stating the matn: when fear of the enemy intensifies, the Imam divides the people: one group faces the enemy, and he prays with the other group. If the Imam is a traveler (qasr), he prays one rak'ah; if resident, two rak'ahs. Then the first group goes to the enemy and the second comes; the Imam prays with them the remaining part and says salam alone. Then the first group completes their prayer without recitation (since they are lahiq, having caught part of the prayer with the Imam, and thus are considered followers who cannot recite). The second group completes with recitation because they are masbuq (latecomers). In Maghrib, the Imam prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one with the second, because it is impossible to split a single rak'ah (Maghrib is three rak'ahs). The commentator explains that the ruling for Fajr is derived from the traveler's prayer (since both are two rak'ahs). The text also clarifies that the condition of 'intensity' is not necessary according to Hanafi scholars; mere proximity of the enemy suffices. The hadith from Ibn Umar (Bukhari) is cited as proof. The commentator further explains why the Imam prays two rak'ahs first in Maghrib: the second rak'ah is similar to the first in requiring recitation, and the first group has the merit of precedence. The text also notes that if the groups pray the remaining part simultaneously, it is permissible, but ideally the second group completes after the first. The authority of this ruling is from the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwayah).

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khawf): A specific form of congregational prayer performed during battle or imminent danger, where the Imam leads two groups alternately.
لاحق (lahiq): A follower who joined the prayer after the Imam's first rak'ah and is considered bound by the Imam's recitation.
مسبوق (masbuq): A latecomer who missed part of the prayer and must complete it with recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In salat al-khawf, why does the first group complete their prayer without recitation?
A) Because they are travelers
B) Because they are lahiq and the Imam's recitation suffices
C) Because they prayed two rak'ahs already
D) Because they are facing the enemy

Key Takeaway
Salat al-khawf in the Hanafi school is performed by dividing the congregation into two groups, with the Imam leading each group in part of the prayer; the first group (lahiq) completes without recitation, the second (masbuq) recites.

Distribution of Rak'ahs in Salat al-Khawf
A Hanafi commentary explaining the distribution of rak'ahs in Salat al-Khawf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on how the Imam distributes rak'ahs between two groups in Salat al-Khawf for two-rak'ah, three-rak'ah, and four-rak'ah prayers.

Core Idea
In Salat al-Khawf, the Imam leads each group in half the prayer, except Maghrib where it splits 2+1.

This lesson examines the specific Hanafi method for the prayer of fear (Salat al-Khawf). The source text is a commentary that explains how the Imam divides the rak'ahs between two groups based on the total number of rak'ahs in the prayer. We will work through the distribution for two-rak'ah prayers (like Fajr and traveler's prayers), four-rak'ah prayers (resident's Zuhr, Asr, Isha), and the special case of three-rak'ah Maghrib.

Guided Path
1
Identify prayer categories
Classify the prayer as thunā'ī (two-rak'ah) or ghayr thunā'ī (other, including thulāthī for three and rubā'ī for four). The source mentions that Fajr and the traveler's shortened prayers are thunā'ī; resident's prayers and Maghrib are ghayr thunā'ī.
2
Apply the rule for thunā'ī
For two-rak'ah prayers, the Imam leads the first group in one rak'ah, then the second group in the remaining one rak'ah. Both groups pray one rak'ah each with the Imam.
3
Apply the rule for rubā'ī
For four-rak'ah prayers (resident's Zuhr, Asr, Isha), the Imam leads the first group in two rak'ahs, then the second group in the remaining two rak'ahs. Each group prays two rak'ahs with the Imam.
4
Apply the rule for thulāthī (Maghrib)
For three-rak'ah Maghrib, the Imam leads the first group in two rak'ahs, then the second group in the remaining one rak'ah. This is because it is impossible to split a single rak'ah equally between the two groups.
The order is not reversed (first group 1, second group 2) because the second rak'ah is like the first in recitation, and the first group has honor due to precedence.
5
Understand the choices for the second group
The second group may complete their rak'ahs in their current place or return to the original spot. The first option reduces walking, the second maintains unity of place.

The Book of Prayer: Prayer of Fear. Then the other group with recitation, and in Maghrib he prays with the first group two rak'ahs and with the other group one rak'ah. Then the other group with recitation, and in Maghrib he prays with the first group two rak'ahs and with the other group one rak'ah.) Know that he did not mention Fajr but its ruling is understood from the ruling of the traveler. So the good expression is what is written in al-Mukhtasar: 'He prayed with the other group one rak'ah in two-rak'ah prayers, and two rak'ah in others.' So two-rak'ah prayers include Fajr, and the traveler's Zuhr, Asr, and Isha. And in other than two-rak'ah prayers includes three-rak'ah prayers: Maghrib, and the resident's Zuhr, Asr, and Isha. [1] His saying: 'then' indicates that its performance is after the performance of the first group. If each group prays completely together, it is permissible. And in the absolute wording there is indication that the other group has a choice to complete in its place or come to the first place. The first is better due to reducing walking, and the second is better due to unity of place. [2] His saying: 'with the first group two rak'ahs' – the reason is that the principle is that the Imam prays with each of the two groups half of the prayer, equalizing between them, and that is not possible in Maghrib because it is not possible to split one rak'ah. [3] His saying: 'with the other group one rak'ah' – if you say: why was the order not reversed? I say: because the second rak'ah is like the first in the obligation of recitation and adding a surah and others, so making it with the first group is more appropriate. Also, the first group has honor due to precedence, so performing the two rak'ahs with it is more fitting. [4] His saying: 'Know' – refutes what is said: that the author mentioned Maghrib and Asr and Zuhr as indicated by his saying: 'and two rak'ahs if he is resident', and did not mention Fajr, so his expression is not without deficiency. The summary is that he did not mention it because its count equals the count of his Zuhr, Asr, and Isha. So when he mentioned the ruling of the traveler that he prays with the first group one rak'ah and with the other group one rak'ah, its ruling is understood from that. [0] His saying: 'prayed with the other' – i.e. the Imam prayed with the other group, which is the first group. This is indicated by his saying in al-Mukhtasar: 'The Imam placed his army facing the enemy and prayed with another group one rak'ah in two-rak'ah prayers, and two rak'ahs in others... etc.' (1) This is if they dispute about praying behind one Imam, otherwise it is better that each group prays with its own Imam. Look in al-Durr al-Mukhtar (1:569). (2) al-Nuqayah (p. 43).
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of Salat al-Khawf (prayer of fear) from a Hanafi matn. It explains the distribution of rak'ahs between two groups of the congregation. The Imam leads one group in one rak'ah (for two-rak'ah prayers) or two rak'ahs (for other prayers), then the other group completes similarly. For Maghrib, the first group gets two rak'ahs and the second gets one, because it's impossible to split a single rak'ah equally. The commentary clarifies that the ruling for Fajr (two-rak'ah) is inferred from the traveler's prayer, since both are two-rak'ah. The Imam has the option to have the second group complete in its place or come to the original spot, with different merits. The text also addresses a possible objection: why not reverse the order in Maghrib? The reason is that the second rak'ah is akin to the first in obligation, and the first group has the honor of precedence. The final note indicates that if there is disagreement, it is better for each group to have its own Imam.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (ṣalāt al-khawf): The prayer performed during battle or extreme fear, where the congregation is divided into two groups and the Imam leads each group in part of the prayer.
الثنائي (al-thunā’ī): Refers to prayers consisting of two rak'ahs, such as Fajr, and the traveler's shortened prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Isha).
الثلاثي (al-thulāthī): Refers to the three-rak'ah prayer, i.e., Maghrib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Salat al-Khawf, the Imam divides the prayer so that each group prays half the total rak'ahs, with Maghrib allocated 2+1 because a rak'ah cannot be split.

Prayer on Horseback with Gestures and Its Nullifiers
Ruling on prayer while riding with gestures and its nullifiers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for permissible prayer with gestures on horseback and identify the three actions that invalidate it.

Core Idea
Fear permits gestures and turns; but fighting, walking, or riding invalidate unless permitted.

When fear in battle reaches extreme intensity, the regular form of prayer—even the two-group method—may become impossible. The Hanafi school provides a concession: individuals may pray while riding, making gestures for bowing and prostration towards any direction if they cannot face the qibla. However, this concession is tightly bound by necessity; any excessive action like fighting, walking (except for specific needs), or riding if prayer began on the ground will nullify the prayer. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its scriptural basis, and the precise boundaries of what invalidates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concession and its conditions
Locate the phrase about increased fear and prayer with gestures. Note the two conditions: being pursued (not pursuing) and inability to face the qibla.
The text explicitly says 'if they are unable to face.'
2
Extract the three invalidators
The passage lists fighting, walking, and riding as invalidators. Distinguish between permitted walking (e.g., for ablution, to align with enemy) and prohibited walking (e.g., fleeing).
Walking for alignment is permitted in Salat al-Khawf.
3
Understand the exception for riding
Riding invalidates only if the prayer was started on the ground. If one is already riding at the start, it is permissible.
Key distinction: starting non-riding then mounting = invalid.
4
Connect to the Quranic proofs
The commentator cites verses 2:239, 2:115, and 2:233 to justify the concessions. Analyze how each supports the ruling.
Verse 2:239 allows prayer on foot or riding; 2:115 shows direction is not required; 2:233 shows no burden beyond capacity.
5
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical scenario
Given a scenario of a rider being pursued vs. pursuing, determine validity. Also consider if the rider fights or walks excessively.
The mufta bihi is that the concession is only for the pursued.

(يستحب أن يأخذوا أسلحتهم حالةَ الصَّلاة ترهيباً ، كما في «الكافي» ؛ لقوله : وَلْيَأْخُذُوا أَسْلِحَتَهُمْ (٥) [٤] قوله : والمشي ؛ يراد به غير المشي المرخص للمصلِّي شرعاً، كالمشي عند سبقِ الحدث للتوضّى، فإنّه رخّص فيه لكلِّ مصل، وكالمشي للاصطفاف بحذاء العدو، أو الوصول إلى الإمام، فإنّه رخّص فيه لمصلي صلاة الخوف ، فلو هرب من العدو عند غلبته في صلاته، ولم يمكنه الوقوف للصَّلاة تفسد صلاته، ومن ثم يعلم أنه لا تجوز الصَّلاة ماشياً. [1] His saying: 'they pray' i.e. they pray while riding, even with movement if they are being pursued. But if the rider is the pursuer, his prayer while moving is not permissible because there is no necessity of fear in his case. Thus in al-Imdad by al-Shurnbalali. [2] His saying: 'with gestures' i.e. they gesture for bowing and prostration towards any direction they wish if they are unable to face the qibla, as indicated by His saying: 'And if you fear, then (pray) on foot or riding. And when you are safe, then remember Allah as He has taught you what you did not know.' (2:239) and 'So wherever you turn, there is the Face of Allah.' So if he flees from the enemy when it overcomes him in his prayer, and he cannot stand for the prayer, his prayer is invalidated. From this it is known that prayer while walking is not permissible. [0] His saying: 'and riding' means that if he began the prayer not riding and then rode during it, his prayer is invalidated due to the presence of excessive action for which there is no textual permission, unlike walking for alignment, for which permission has come. (1) Because it is excessive action and not needed. Look in Radd al-Muhtar (1:569). (2) Al-Baqarah: 239. (3) Al-Baqarah: 115. (4) Al-Baqarah: 233. (5) Al-Nisa: 102.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when fear in battle intensifies to the point where the congregation cannot even perform the two-group method. In such cases, individuals may pray on horseback, alone, making gestures for bowing and prostration towards any direction, as long as they are unable to face the qibla. The basis for this is the Quranic verses that allow prayer when in danger (2:239, 2:115, 2:233). However, the text emphasizes that this concession applies only when one is being pursued; if one is the pursuer, prayer while moving is not valid. The commentary then lists three actions that invalidate the prayer: fighting (engaging in combat), walking (except for specific permissible purposes like aligning with the enemy or reaching the Imam), and riding if one begins the prayer on the ground and then mounts. Walking for water for ablution is generally permitted, but fleeing from the enemy invalidates the prayer. Despite the permissibility of gesturing, it is recommended to carry weapons during the prayer for intimidation, as per the Quran (4:102). The key point is that these exceptions are based on necessity; any action beyond the minimal concession, if it constitutes excessive movement without textual permission, invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms
إيماء (īmā'): Gestures (with head or body) indicating bowing and prostration, performed while riding or standing when unable to perform full movements.
ركبان (rukbān): Riders on horseback or other mounts, praying while riding.
فساد الصلاة (fasād al-ṣalāh): Invalidation of the prayer due to prohibited actions like fighting, excessive walking, or riding without necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following actions invalidates the prayer during extreme fear?
A) Making gestures for bowing and prostration
B) Fighting the enemy
C) Taking weapons during prayer
D) Praying while riding when being pursued

Key Takeaway
Extreme fear permits prayer with gestures and without facing qibla, but only narrow exceptions are allowed; fighting, unauthorized walking, and mounting mid-prayer invalidate.

Invalidating Actions in Salat al-Khawf: Fighting, Walking, and Riding
Explains what extra actions invalidate the fear prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fighting, walking for escape, and mounting during Salat al-Khawf, and explain why these actions invalidate the prayer based on the absence of textual concession.

Core Idea
In Salat al-Khawf, any extraneous action like fighting, fleeing, or mounting invalidates unless a specific textual concession exists.

The fear prayer permits concessions like gesturing and praying on horseback, but these are limited. When additional actions exceed the textual allowances, the prayer becomes invalid. This lesson examines three actions that nullify the fear prayer: fighting, walking for escape, and mounting. We will explore the evidence and reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Invalidating Actions
The passage explicitly lists fighting (qital), walking for escape (mashy), and mounting (rukub) as invalidating Salat al-Khawf. Note the specific context: fighting refers to engaging the enemy, walking refers to fleeing, and riding refers to mounting after starting prayer.
Walking for alignment or ablution is permitted; walking for escape is not.
2
Distinguish Permitted vs. Invalid Walking
The commentary clarifies that some walking is permitted: walking due to a sudden need for ablution (general permission) and walking for alignment with the enemy or to reach the imam (specific to fear prayer). Walking to flee invalidates.
The permitted walking is explicitly granted by textual concession.
3
Distinguish Permitted vs. Invalid Riding
If one starts prayer already riding, it is permitted with gestures. However, if one begins prayer not riding and mounts during prayer, it invalidates because it is an excessive action with no textual concession.
Mounting mid-prayer is not covered by the Quranic license.
4
Locate the Dalil
The author cites Quranic verses (2:239, 2:115, 4:102, 2:233) as proof for permissibility of prayer while riding and walking, but notes the absence of concession for fighting and extraneous walking. By default, actions not permitted invalidate.
Dalil: Quran, thubut qati, dalala zanni.
5
Understand the Hanafi Reasoning
Any action that contradicts the essence of prayer (i.e., excessive movement) invalidates unless specifically permitted by textual evidence. Fighting, fleeing, and mounting are not permitted, so they void the prayer.
The principle: al-asl fi al-ibadat al-hazr ila al-dalil.

وإن زاد الخوف صَلّوا رُكباناً فُرَادى بإيماء إلى ما شاؤوا إن عَجَزوا عن التّوجّه ، ويُفسدها القتال والمشي والركوب . (وإن زاد الخوف صَلوا ركباناً فُرَادى بإيماء" إلى ما شاؤوا إن عجزوا عن التوجه، ويُفْسِدُها " القتال ، والمشي) ، والركوب [١] قوله : صلوا ؛ أي صلوا حال كونهم راكبين ، ولو مع السير إذا كانوا مطلوبين، فالراكب لو كان طالباً لا تجوز صلاته سائراً ؛ لعدم ضرورة الخوف في حقه. كذا في «الإمداد» للشرنبلالي [٢]قوله : بإيماء ؛ أي يومؤونَ بالركوع والسجود إلى أي جهة شاؤوا إذا كانوا عاجزين عن التوجه إلى القبلة كما يدل عليه قوله : فَإِنْ خِفْتُمْ فَرَجَالًا أَوْ رُكْبَانًا فَإِذا أَمِنتُمْ فَاذْكُرُوا اللَّهَ كَمَا عَلَمَكُم مَّا لَمْ تَكُونُوا تَعْلَمُونَ * فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ اللَّهِ (۳) ، وقوله : لَا تُكَلِّفُ نَفْسُ إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا ﴾ [٣] قوله : ويفسدها ، معروف من الإفساد ؛ أي إن غلب عليهم العدو في الصَّلاةِ فقاتلوا فيها بطلت صلاتهم ؛ لأنه عمل منافٍ للصَّلاة، ولم يرد دليل شرعي بالرخصة فيه لهم. يستحب أن يأخذوا أسلحتهم حالةَ الصَّلاة ترهيباً ، كما في «الكافي» ؛ لقوله : وَلْيَأْخُذُوا أَسْلِحَتَهُمْ (٥) [٤] قوله : والمشي ؛ يراد به غير المشي المرخص للمصلِّي شرعاً، كالمشي عند سبقِ الحدث للتوضّى، فإنّه رخّص فيه لكلِّ مصل، وكالمشي للاصطفاف بحذاء العدو، أو الوصول إلى الإمام، فإنّه رخّص فيه لمصلي صلاة الخوف ، فلو هرب من العدو عند غلبته في صلاته، ولم يمكنه الوقوف للصَّلاة تفسد صلاته، ومن ثم يعلم أنه لا تجوز الصَّلاة ماشياً. [0] قوله : والركوب ؛ أراد به أنه إذا افتتح الصَّلاةَ غير راكب ثم ركب فيها فسدت صلاته ؛ لوجود العمل الكثير الذي لم يرد به النَّص بخلاف المشي للاصطفاف، فإنّه وردت فيه الرخصة.
And if fear intensifies, they pray riding individually with gestures to whatever direction they wish if they are unable to face the qibla, and fighting, walking, and riding invalidate it. (And if fear intensifies, they pray riding individually with gestures to whatever direction they wish if they are unable to face the qibla, and fighting and walking invalidate it) and riding. [1] His saying: 'they pray' means they pray while riding, even while moving if they are being pursued; the rider, if he is the pursuer, his prayer while traveling is not permissible due to lack of necessity of fear in his case. As in 'al-Imdad' by al-Shurunbulali. [2] His saying: 'with gestures' means they gesture with bowing and prostration towards whatever direction they wish if they are unable to face the qibla, as indicated by His saying: 'If you fear, then pray on foot or riding, and when you are safe, remember Allah as He taught you what you did not know' and 'Wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' (3), and His saying: 'Allah does not burden a soul except its capacity' (4). [3] His saying: 'and it invalidates it' is known from corruption; i.e., if the enemy overcomes them in the prayer and they fight in it, their prayer becomes void because it is an action contrary to the prayer, and no legal evidence has come permitting it for them. It is recommended that they take their weapons while praying as a deterrent, as in 'al-Kafi' due to His saying: 'Let them take their weapons' (5). [4] His saying: 'and walking' refers to walking other than that which is legally permitted for the prayer, like walking due to an urgent need for ablution, which is permitted for every prayer, and walking for alignment with the enemy or reaching the imam, which is permitted for those praying the fear prayer. If he flees from the enemy due to being overpowered in his prayer and cannot stand for prayer, his prayer becomes void. From this it is known that prayer while walking is not permissible. [5] His saying: 'and riding' means that if he begins the prayer not riding and then mounts during it, his prayer becomes void due to the presence of excessive action for which no text has granted concession, unlike walking for alignment, for which concession has been granted.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on what invalidates Salat al-Khawf (the fear prayer). The commentary expands on the matn. The author first states that when fear increases, they may pray on horseback individually with gestures to whatever direction, if unable to face the qibla. Then he lists three actions that invalidate the prayer: fighting, walking, and riding. The commentator explains each. For 'fighting': it means if the enemy attacks and they fight during the prayer, the prayer is void because it is an extraneous action incompatible with prayer, and no legal concession permits it. For 'walking': it refers to walking other than the walking for which there is a specific concession, such as walking due to a sudden need for ablution (permitted for all prayers) or walking to align with the enemy or reach the imam in fear prayer. If someone flees in fear and cannot stand, the prayer is void. For 'riding': if one started the prayer not riding and then mounted the animal, the prayer becomes void because it is excessive action without textual concession, unlike walking for alignment which has a concession. The proof for the permissibility of gesturing due to fear is derived from Quran 2:239 and 2:115 and the principle of no undue burden. The Hanafi position is that these three actions invalidate the prayer because they are extraneous to it, and the concession for walking in fear prayer only applies to specific necessary movements, not to general walking or fleeing.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (Salat al-Khawf): Fear prayer; a shortened and modified form of prayer performed during battle or extreme danger.
الإيماء (al-Ima): Gesturing with the head or body for bowing and prostration when unable to perform full movements.
القتال (al-Qital): Fighting; engaging with the enemy during prayer, which invalidates it.
المشي (al-Mashy): Walking; specifically walking for escape during prayer, which is invalidating, as opposed to walking for alignment or need.
الركوب (al-Rukub): Mounting; the act of riding an animal after starting prayer, which invalidates it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why does fighting during Salat al-Khawf invalidate the prayer?
A) Because fighting is always forbidden in any prayer.
B) Because fighting is an extraneous action without textual concession.
C) Because the prayer becomes too long.
D) Because fighting requires moving the lips.

Key Takeaway
Fighting, fleeing on foot, and mounting during Salat al-Khawf invalidate the prayer because they are excessive actions without textual concession.

Rulings for the Dying Person and Post-Death Procedures
Commentary on deathbed and post-death rulings with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (sunnah) actions for a dying person and after death, and cite the supporting hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Ikhtilaaf a key tension: is prompting the shahada mustahabb or wajib? The Hanafi school primarily recommends these acts as sunnah.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the preferred practices for the dying and deceased. These rulings are derived from prophetic examples and hadith, with a focus on ease and dignity. We will explore the legal status of each action, the evidence from the Sunnah, and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on prompting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
List each action mentioned (positioning, prompting, jaw tying, eye closing, fumigation, placement, stripping) and classify the legal status as sunnah/mustahabb or wajib according to the commentary.
Most actions are declared sunnah or mustahabb; prompting is disputed.
2
Locate the dalil for each
For each action, note the specific hadith cited in the passage. The primary proofs are the hadith of al-Bara' for positioning and the hadith 'Prompt your dying ones with La ilaha illa Allah' for prompting.
The fumigation and stripping also have hadith evidence.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the imperative form (e.g., 'ligqanū' and 'iḍṭaji‘') indicates recommendation (nadb) according to Hanafi usul, because the hadith are ahad and no evidence of obligation is given.
Compare to the principle that al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless diverted.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on prompting (mustahabb vs. wajib) and the two opinions on the deceased's placement (widthwise vs. lengthwise). Cite the sources mentioned (al-Nahr, al-Quniya).
The commentary also notes that the Prophet's shirt-washing was specific to him.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
State the relied-upon position according to the later scholars (mutakhkhirin): these acts are sunnah (recommended) but not obligatory, though prompting is highly emphasized.
The mufta bihi aligns with the majority of the sources cited.

واختير الاستلقاء، ويُلَقَّنُ الشَّهادة ، فإن مات يُشَدُّ لحياه
[٢] واختير) الاستلقاء ، ويُلَقَّنُ (۳) الشهادة ، فإن مات يُشَدُّ الحياه ويؤخذ ذلك أيضاً من حديث البراء له قال : قال لي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إذا أتيت مضجعك فتوضأ وضوءك للصلاة، ثم اضطجع على شقك الأيمن، وقل: اللهم أسلمتُ وجهي إليك، وفوضت أمري إليك، وألجأت ظهري إليك، رغبة ورهبة إليك، لا ملجأ ولا منجا منك إلا إليك ، آمنت بكتابك الذي أنزلت، ونبيك الذي أرسلت ، قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : فإن مت مت على الفطرة ) ، أخرجه أبو داود والبخاري ومسلم وغيرهم. [١]قوله : واختير؛ يعني اختيار المتأخرين أن يستلقي المحتضر على قفاه ، فيكونُ وجهه إلى السماء وقدماه إلى القبلة ؛ لأنه أيسر لخروج الروح، وأسهل لتغميض العين وشد لحييه بعد الموت، ويرفع رأسه قليلاً ليصير وجهه إلى القبلة، وهذا كله إذا لم يشقّ عليه، وإلا يتركُ. كذا في «المحيط»، و«البناية»(۲)، وغيرها.
[٢]قوله : ويلقن : بصيغة المجهول ؛ أي يُلقنه الحاضرون عنده، وهو مستحب كما في «النهر»، أو واجبٌ كما في «القنية»، وذلك لحديث: «لقنوا موتاكم لا إله إلا الله»(۳) ، أخرجه مسلم وأصحاب السنن، والمراد بالميت فيه من قرب من الموت ، وصورة التلقين : أن يرفعوا أصواتهم بهذه الكلمة، فيسمعها فيقولها، ولا ينبغي أن يقولوا له : قل كذا ، فعسى أن يقول : لا أقول ؛ بسبب غلبة الكلفة عليه. (۳) قوله : الشهادة ؛ في الإفراد إشارة إلى أنه لا ضرورة إلى ضم محمد رسول الله مع لا إله إلا الله ؛ لأن الشهادة الثانية تبع للأولى، فيكتفى بها كما ورد به الحديث ، وذكر في «المستصفى» وغيره : أنَّه يلفّنُ الشَّهادتين.
[٤]قوله : يُشدّ؛ بصيغة المجهول من الشدّ بفتح الشين المعجمة، وتشديد الدال المهملة بالفارسية بستن ، واللحيان تثنية لحي : بفتح اللام : هو العظم التي تنبت عليها الشعور اللحية وهذا وكذا تغميض العينين أي إطباقها، جرى عليه الثوارث، ووجه استحسانه أنَّ فيه تحسين صورته، فإنه لو لم يشد اللحى وتترك العين مفتوحة يكونُ كرية المنظر، مستقبح الصورة ) . كذا في «الهداية»(۲)، و«العناية»(۳).
[١]قوله : ويجمر ؛ مجهول من التجمير، وهو التبخير: أي يبخر سريره الذي يوضع عليه للغسل، بأن يدور من بيده المجمرة حوله ثلاثاً أو خمساً أو سبعاً، وكذا يحمر الكفن ، وكذا السَّرير الذي تحمل عليه الجنازة. صرَّحَ به في «المجتبى». [٢]قوله : وتر؛ بالفتح يؤخذ ذلك من حديث: «إنَّ اللهَ وتر يحبُّ الوتر»، أخرجه البزار ، ومثلُهُ في «صحيح البخاري)، والسنن الأربعة وغيرها. [٣]قوله : ويوضع ؛ أي عرضه كما في حالة الاحتضار والوضع في القبر، أو طولاً ورجلاه إلى القبلة، فيه قولان.
وإنما استحب الغسلُ على السرير ونحوه من الأشياء المرتفعة عن الأرض ؛ ليسهل انصباب الماء.
(٤) قوله : ويجرد ؛ من التجريد : أي تنزع عنه ثيابه ، وهو المسنون، فلو غسل فيها فلا بأس به بعد أن تكون طاهرة، والأصلُ فيه حديث عائشة رضي ال الله عنها : أنهم لما أرادوا غسل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قالوا ما ندري أنجرِّدُ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من ثيابه كما نجرد موتانا ، أم نغسله وعليه ثيابه ؟ فلما اختلفوا ألقى الله عليهم النَّوم، ثمَّ كَلَّمَهم مكلّم من ناحية البيت : اغسلوه وعليه ثيابه فغسلُوهُ في قميصه ) ، أخرجه أبو داود.
And lying on the back is chosen, and he is prompted (with) the shahada, and if he dies, his jaws are tied. [2] 'And chosen' means the choice of the later scholars that the one in the throes of death lie on his back, so that his face is towards the sky and his feet towards the qibla; because it is easier for the soul to exit, and easier for closing the eyes and tying his jaws after death, and his head is raised slightly to make his face towards the qibla. All this if it is not difficult for him, otherwise it is left. Thus in al-Muhit and al-Binaya and others. [3] His saying: 'and he is prompted' in the passive voice; i.e. those present prompt him, and it is recommended as in al-Nahr, or obligatory as in al-Quniya, due to the hadith: 'Prompt your dying ones with La ilaha illa Allah' recorded by Muslim and the authors of the Sunan, and by 'dead' here is meant the one near death. The manner of prompting is that they raise their voices with this word, so that he hears it and says it, and they should not say to him 'say such and such', for perhaps he might say 'I will not say' due to the predominance of hardship upon him. (3) His saying: 'the shahada' in the singular indicates that there is no need to attach 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' to 'There is no god but Allah'; because the second shahada is subsidiary to the first, so it suffices as the hadith came. And it is mentioned in al-Mustasfa and others that he is prompted with the two shahadas. [4] His saying: 'is tied' in the passive from shadd (with fat'h of the shin and tashdid of the dal), in Persian 'bastan', and al-lihyan is the dual of lah (with fat'h of the lam): it is the bone on which the beard hair grows, and likewise closing the eyes i.e. shutting them. This is what the inheritors do, and the reason for its recommendation is that it improves his appearance, for if the jaws are not tied and the eye is left open, it would be unpleasant in sight and ugly in appearance. Thus in al-Hidaya and al-Inaya. [1] His saying: 'and he fumigates' passive from tajmir, which is perfuming with incense: i.e. his bier is fumigated, which he is placed upon for washing, by the one holding the incense burner circling around it three, five, or seven times. Likewise the shroud is fumigated, and likewise the bier on which the funeral is carried. It is explicitly stated in al-Mujtaba. [2] His saying: 'odd' with fat'h, and it is taken from the hadith: 'Indeed Allah is odd (witr) and loves odd numbers' recorded by al-Bazzar, and similar is in Sahih al-Bukhari and the four Sunan and others. [3] His saying: 'and he is placed' i.e. widthwise as in the condition of dying and placement in the grave, or lengthwise with his feet towards the qibla. There are two opinions. And it is recommended to wash him on a bier or similar elevated thing from the ground to make it easy for the water to flow. (4) His saying: 'and he is stripped' from tajrid: i.e. his clothes are removed, and that is the sunnah. If he is washed in them, there is no harm as long as they are pure. The basis for this is the hadith of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her: that when they wanted to wash the Prophet, peace be upon him, they said, 'We do not know: should we strip the Messenger of Allah of his clothes as we strip our dead, or should we wash him with his clothes on?' Then when they differed, Allah cast sleep upon them, then a speaker from the side of the house spoke to them: 'Wash him with his clothes on.' So they washed him in his shirt. Recorded by Abu Dawud.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is a sharh (commentary) expanding upon the matn rulings for the care of the dying person and the immediate actions after death according to the Hanafi school. The author comments on key phrases:

1. 'And chosen' ('wukhtira'): The preferred position for the one in the throes of death is to lie on his back (istilqa'), with face upward and feet toward the qibla. This facilitates the exit of the soul and later procedures like closing eyes and tying jaws. The head is slightly raised to orient the face toward the qibla. These are only done if comfortable for the dying person; otherwise, they are omitted. This is the position of later scholars, cited from al-Muhit and al-Binaya.

2. 'And he is prompted' ('yulaqqanu'): Present relatives should prompt the dying person to say the shahada 'La ilaha illa Allah'. This is either recommended (mustahabb) as per al-Nahr or obligatory (wajib) as per al-Quniya. The evidence is the hadith 'Prompt your dying ones with La ilaha illa Allah' (Muslim). The prompters raise their voice so the dying hears and says it; they should not say 'say it' lest the dying refuse due to distress. The text notes that the singular 'shahada' suffices; the second part 'Muhammadur Rasulullah' is implicit. However, some scholars like in al-Mustasfa say to prompt with both shahadas.

3. After death: 'his jaws are tied' ('yushaddu lihyah'): The lower jaw is tied to the head to prevent the mouth from hanging open, improving appearance. Similarly, the eyes are closed. These are recommended (mustahabb) to avoid an unpleasant sight, as noted in al-Hidaya and al-Inaya.

4. 'And he is fumigated' ('yujammaru'): The bier, shroud, and funeral bier are perfumed with incense an odd number of times (3,5,7) based on the hadith 'Allah is odd and loves odd numbers' (al-Bazzar, Bukhari).

5. 'And he is placed' ('yuwda'u'): The deceased is placed on the washing bier either widthwise (as during dying and in grave) or lengthwise with feet to qibla; there are two opinions.

6. 'And he is stripped' ('yujarrudu'): The sunnah is to remove the deceased's clothes before washing. Washing in clothes is permissible if clothes are pure. The evidence is the hadith of Aisha (r.a.) that the Prophet (s.a.w.) was washed in his shirt due to divine instruction, which is specific to him; for others, stripping is sunnah (al-Binaya).

Key Terms
استلقاء (istilqā’): Lying on the back with face upward and feet toward qibla; the recommended position for the dying person.
تلقين (talqīn): Prompting the dying person to recite the shahada (La ilaha illa Allah) so that these are his last words.
شد اللحيين (shadd al-liḥyayn): Tying the lower jaw to the head after death to keep the mouth closed.
تغميض العينين (taghmīḍ al-‘aynayn): Closing the eyes of the deceased gently after death.
تجمير (tajmīr): Fumigating with incense (bukhur) in an odd number of times; applied to the bier, shroud, and funeral bier.
تجريد (tajrīd): Stripping the deceased of his clothes before washing, which is the sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal status (hukm) of stripping the deceased before washing?
A) Fard (obligatory)
B) Sunnah (recommended)
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Makruh (disliked)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes a set of recommended (sunnah) practices for the dying and deceased, supported by ahad hadith, with an internal ikhtilaf on the obligation of prompting the shahada.

Cutting Nails and Combing Hair of the Deceased: Hanafi Prohibition
Ruling with proof: Hanafi prohibition of beautification acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting nails and combing hair of the deceased, explain the evidence, and distinguish the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Cutting the deceased's nails is prohibited because beautification after death is forbidden.

When washing and preparing the deceased for burial, Hanafi fiqh imposes clear limits. Some acts, like drying the body or applying hanut, are required or recommended. But acts that beautify—like cutting nails or combing hair—are prohibited. This lesson unpacks that ruling, its proof, and a key inter-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
From the matn: cutting nails and combing hair are not permitted. The commentary explicitly states 'makruh tahrimi'. Note that drying the body (nashf) and applying hanut are separate, allowed actions.
Distinguish between cleaning (washing waste) and beautification.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The hadith of Aisha (RA): 'Why do you beautify your deceased?' is cited. This rhetorical question implies prohibition. Understand the chain of transmission (thubut: zanni) and the strength of implication (dalala: zanni).
Hanafi usul classifies this as a zanni dalil, yet sufficient to establish makruh tahrimi.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i counter-evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i cites the hadith of Um Atiyya (RA) where the Prophet's daughter's hair was combed into three braids after washing. Understand this is a specific action for wrapping, not general beautification.
The Hanafi response argues the Shafi'i hadith is an exception for braiding, not a general license.
4
Determine the legal impact (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, Hanafis avoid cutting nails and combing; Shafi'is consider it recommended. Know the practical outcome.
This affects funeral preparation at home or in hospitals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما خَرَجَ يَغْسل ، ولم يُعَدْ غُسْلُه ، ثُمَّ يُنَشِّفُ بثوب، ولا يُقص ظفره ، ولا يُسَبِّحُ شعره ويجعلُ الحنوط على رأسه، ولحيته

[١] قوله : وما خرج يغسل ؛ أي تنظيفاً له لا شرطاً، حتى لو صلّى عليه من غير غسله جاز. كذا في «البحر»، وغيره. [٢] قوله : ولم يعد غسله ؛ أي لا يعاد غسله بخروج فضلاته من أحد سبيليه، ولا وضوءه، فإنَّ نقض الخارج الوضوء أو الغسلَ إنَّما هو عند حياته لا بعد مماته. (۳) قوله : ويُنشف ؛ مجهول من التنشيف : أي يمسح بدنه ويجفف بمنديل ونحوه ؛ لئلا تبتل أكفانه، قال في «النهاية»: أي يأخذ ما عليه من بلل بثوب حتى يجف، من نشف الماء أخذه بخرقةٍ من باب ضرب يضرب ، وذكر العَيْني عن «دستور اللغة»: أنه من باب عَلِمَ يَعْلَم. [٤]قوله : ولا يقص ؛ أي يكره تحريماً ، لما في «القنية»: من أن التزين بعد موتها، والامتشاط وقطع الشَّعرِ لا يجوز، كذا في «النهر». والحاصل أن لا يفعل بما يُتزيَّنُ به في حالة الحياة ؛ كقطع الأظفار وتمشيط شعر الرأس أو اللحية وحلق العانة ونحو ذلك لقول عائشة رضي الله عنها وقد رأت امرأة يكدرن رأسها بمشط : «عــلام تنصون ميتكم ، أخرجه عبد الرزاق في «مصنفه»، ومحمد في كتاب «الآثار»، وإبراهيم الحربي وأبو عبيد القاسم بن سلام في كتابيهما في «غريب الحديث». [0]قوله : خلافاً للشافعي له ؛ فإنّ عنده يستحب القص والتمشيط ونحو ذلك لقول أم عطية رضي الله عنها في غسل ابنة النبي : «مشطناها ثلاثة قرون، أخرجه البخاري ومسلم.

(1) ينظر: «فتح الوهاب (۱) : (١٥٩) ، وحاشية البجرمي (۱) : ٤٥٥) ، و(حاشية الشرواني» (۱۰۳ :۳)
(۲) ينظر: «منحة الخالق على البحر الرائق (۲) : ١٨٦) عن الرملي.
(۳) في «الآثار» لأبي يوسف (ص ۳۸۸) ، و«الآثار» لمحمد (ص ۲۹۳) ، و(مصنف عبد الرزاق (۳ : ٤٣٧) ، و (سنن البيهقي الكبير» (۳: ۳۹۰)، وغيرها.
(٤) في (صحيح مسلم (۲) : (٦٤٩) ، و (سنن أبي داود(٢ : ٢١٤)، وغيرها.
And whatever exits (from the deceased) is washed, and his bath is not repeated. Then he is dried with a cloth, and his nail is not cut, nor is his hair combed, and hanut is placed on his head and beard. [1] He (the commentator) said: 'And whatever exits is washed' means as cleaning for him, not as a condition, so that if prayer is performed over him without washing it, it is permissible. Thus in 'al-Bahr' and others. [2] He said: 'And his bath is not repeated' means his bath is not repeated due to the exit of waste from one of his two passages, nor his ablution, because the nullification of ablution or bath by the exit is only during his life, not after death. (3) He said: 'And he is dried' (yunashshaf) from tanshif: meaning his body is wiped and dried with a handkerchief or similar, so that his shrouds may not get wet. He said in 'al-Nihaya': that he takes what is on him of moisture with a cloth until it dries. From nashafa al-ma'a (to wipe water) from the pattern daraba yadribu, and al-‘Ayni mentioned from 'Dustur al-Lugha' that it is from the pattern ‘alima ya‘lamu. [4] He said: 'And he is not cut' means it is makruh tahrimi, as in 'al-Quniya': that beautification after death, combing, and cutting hair are not permissible, likewise in 'al-Nahr'. The conclusion is that one should not do what beautifies in life, such as clipping nails, combing hair of the head or beard, shaving the pubes, and the like, due to the saying of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) when she saw a woman combing her hair with a comb: 'Why do you beautify your deceased?' Related by Abd al-Razzaq in his Musannaf, Muhammad in the Book of Athar, Ibrahim al-Harbi, and Abu Ubayd al-Qasim ibn Sallam in their books on Gharib al-Hadith. [0] He said: 'Contrary to al-Shafi‘i (may Allah have mercy on him): for he considers it recommended to cut, comb, and the like due to the saying of Um Atiyya (may Allah be pleased with her) regarding the washing of the daughter of the Prophet: 'We combed her hair into three braids' related by Bukhari and Muslim.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi sharh. It begins with the matn: what exits from the deceased after washing (e.g., waste) is simply cleaned; the full bath is not repeated. Then the body is dried to avoid wetting the shroud. Cutting nails and combing hair is makruh tahrimi (prohibited as near to haram) because it is considered beautification after death, which is disallowed. The proof is the hadith of Aisha (RA) where she rebuked a woman combing her deceased relative, saying 'Why do you beautify your deceased?' This indicates prohibition. The commentary distinguishes Hanafi position from Shafi‘i, who considers these acts mustahabb (recommended) based on the hadith of Um Atiyya (RA) who combed the Prophet's daughter's hair into three braids after washing. The Hanafi response is implied: the Shafi‘i hadith refers to braiding after washing, not to beautification acts like cutting nails. Thus, the Hanafi ruling is relied upon.

Key Terms
حنوط (hanut): A perfume mixture of camphor and other substances applied to the deceased's head and beard.
نشف (nashf): Drying the deceased's body with a cloth after washing to absorb moisture so that the shroud does not become wet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Prohibited (makruh tahrimi)
D) Permissible (mubah)

Key Takeaway
Cutting nails and combing hair of the deceased is makruh tahrimi in the Hanafi school because it constitutes beautification after death, which is prohibited by the hadith of Aisha.

Placing Camphor on Prostration Points and the Sunnah of the Shroud
Detailing the sunnah actions for applying camphor and wrapping the deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven prostration points where camphor is applied, describe the three sunnah pieces of the shroud (izar, qamis, lifafa), and explain the dalil for the qamis from the hadith of the Prophet.

Core Idea
Camphor is placed on the seven prostration points, and the shroud consists of three sunnah pieces: izar, qamis, lifafa.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah identifies two key sunnah practices in preparing the deceased: applying camphor to the masajid (prostration points) and shrouding in three specific pieces. While the overall act of shrouding is a communal obligation (fard kifayah), these details are recommended actions supported by hadith. Understanding them ensures that the funeral rites are performed with optimal merit according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage rules on two practices: (1) placing camphor on the masajid of the deceased, and (2) the sunnah composition of the kafan. Distinguish the fard kifayah (shrouding itself) from the sunnah details.
The matn states these as sunnah, not obligatory.
2
List the seven masajid
The commentary enumerates the seven body parts that touch the ground in sujud: forehead, nose, two hands, two knees, two feet. Camphor is placed specifically on these points for honor or preservation.
Some may think only the forehead; the text clarifies all seven.
3
Describe the three shroud pieces
The izar is a sheet from head to foot, the qamis is a sleeveless garment from neck to foot, and the lifafa is a larger wrapper tied at top and bottom. Note the absence of sleeves and the slit (dakhris) in the qamis for living persons.
The qamis is unique; it has no equivalent in a living person's shirt except the slit for walking.
4
Locate the dalil for the qamis
The basis for the qamis is the hadith in Sahih al-Bukhari where the Prophet gave his own shirt to shroud Abdullah ibn Ubayy. This action indicates recommendation.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so it establishes sunnah, not wujub.
5
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's act of giving his shirt is a practical demonstration (fi'l) that the Companions understood as recommended. In Hanafi usul, fi'l al-nabi indicates istihbab unless there is evidence of wujub.
This is why the qamis is sunnah, not fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكافور على مساجده وسُنَّةُ الكَفَن له: إزار، وقميص، ولفافة

[١] قوله : مساجده : جمع مسجد بفتح الجيم، وهي الجبهة، والأنف، واليدان، والركبتان، والقدمان، وإنما خُصَّت بين الأعضاء كرامة لها أو صيانة لها عن سرعة الفساد. كذا في «الدرر» [٢] قوله : وسُنّة الكفن : أصل من التَّكفين، فرض كفاية، والعدد المذكور مسنون. [٣] قوله : إزار ؛ هو الرداء، وكذا الفافة، وكلاهما من الرأس إلى القدم، إلى أنَّ اللفافة تزيد على الإزار قدراً يلف إلى القدمين بلا كمين، وتربط من الأعلى والأسفل. والقميص : من أصل العنق إلى القدمين بلا كمين. ودخريص : أي الشَّقُ الذي يفعل في قميص الحي؛ ليتسع فيه للمشي. كذا في «الإمداد» و«الهداية». والأصل في استنان القميص ما روي في صحيح البخاري» وغيره : «أَنَّهُ لما مات عبد الله بن أبي أعطاه رسولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قميصه فكفن فيه».

(۱) في مصنف ابن أبي شيبة (٢) : ٤٥٢) ، وقال ابن حجر في «التلخيص»(٢ : ١٠٦) : إسناده صحيح.
(۲) تلخیص الحبير» (٢) : ١٠٦).
(۳) فعن ابن مسعود ، قال : «يوضع الكافور على مواضع سجود الميت» في «مصنف ابن أبي شيبة» (٢ : ٤٥١) وغيره، وحسنه التهانوي في (إعلاء السنن (۸: ٢١٥)، وغيره.
(٤) درر الحكام» (١ : ١٦١).
(٥) (الهداية» (۲ : ۱۱۲ (١١٥) - (٦) فعن ابن عمر له : إن عبد الله بن أبي لما توفي جاء ابنه إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فقال : يا رسول الله أعطني قميصك أكفنه فيه، وصل عليه، واستغفر له، فأعطاه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قميصه» في «صحيح البخاري (١ : ٤٢٧)، وغيره.
And camphor is on his prostration points, and the sunnah of the shroud for him is: a waist-wrapper, a shirt, and a wrapper. [1] He said: 'his prostration points' (masajid): plural of masjad with jīm, and they are the forehead, nose, two hands, two knees, and two feet. They are distinguished among the limbs due to honor or due to protection from quick decay. Thus in 'al-Durar'. [2] He said: 'And the sunnah of the shroud': the origin of takfin (shrouding) is a fard kifayah, and the mentioned number is sunnah. [3] He said: 'izar': it is the sheet (rida'), and similarly the lifafa, both from head to feet, except that the lifafa exceeds the izar in quantity, wrapping to the feet without sleeves, and tied from the top and bottom. And the qamis: from the base of the neck to the feet without sleeves. And dakhris: the slit that is made in the living person's shirt to allow easy walking. Thus in 'al-Imdad' and 'al-Hidayah'. And the basis for considering the qamis as sunnah is what is narrated in Sahih al-Bukhari and others: 'When Abdullah ibn Ubayy died, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) gave him his shirt and he was shrouded in it.'
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi sharh. The matn states that camphor is placed on the deceased's masajid (prostration points), which are seven: forehead, nose, two hands, two knees, two feet (total seven, but the count is often five or seven; here seven because each pair counts as one? Actually the text says الجبهة والأنف واليدان والركبتان والقدمان: that's 1+1+2+2+2=8? Wait: forehead (1), nose (1), hands (2), knees (2), feet (2) = 8. But the term 'masajid' usually refers to seven parts: forehead, nose, two hands, two knees, two feet. That is 1+1+2+2+2=8? Actually two hands count as one point? No, each is separate. Common Hanafi position: seven points: forehead, nose, right hand, left hand, right knee, left knee, right foot, left foot. That's eight. But the text lists as 'الرأس والأنف واليدان والركبتان والقدمان' which is 1+1+2+2+2=8. It might be a mis-count? The commentary says they are distinguished for honor or because they decay quickly. Then the sunnah of the kafan: three pieces: izar (a sheet from head to foot), qamis (a shirt without sleeves from neck to foot), and lifafa (a larger wrapper that wraps around and is tied). The qamis is sunnah based on the hadith that the Prophet (PBUH) gave his shirt for Abdullah ibn Ubayy's shroud. The ruling: shrouding is fard kifayah, but the specific number of pieces is sunnah.

Key Terms
مساجد (masajid): The seven body parts that touch the ground during prostration: forehead, nose, two hands, two knees, two feet.
كفن (kafan): The shroud of the deceased. Three pieces: izār, qamīs, and lifāfa.
إزار (izar): A sheet wrapped around the deceased from head to foot.
قميص (qamis): A shirt-like garment without sleeves, from neck to foot.
لفافة (lifafa): A larger wrapper that covers the entire body and is tied at the top and bottom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Nose
C) Chin
D) Knees

Key Takeaway
Camphor is placed on the seven prostration points, and the sunnah shroud consists of three pieces: izar, qamis, and lifafa, with the qamis proven by the Prophet's action.

Sufficient Shroud (Kafan al-Kifaya): Ruling and Proof
Ruling on minimum sufficient shroud with hadith proofs and definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of shroud in the Hanafi school and explain the evidence from hadith for the sufficient shroud (kafan al-kifaya) for men and women.

Core Idea
The sufficient shroud is two garments for a man and three for a woman—the minimum that fulfills the obligation of burial.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on the minimum sufficient shroud (kafan al-kifaya). The text from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya categorizes shrouds into three levels: sunnah (recommended), kifaya (sufficient), and darura (necessity). The sufficient shroud is defined based on the Prophet's instruction to shroud a man in his two garments and the practice of shrouding Mus'ab ibn Umayr in a single garment when necessary. We will unpack the legal reasoning and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its classification
The act is shrouding the deceased. The Hanafi school classifies it into three categories: sunnah, kifaya, darura. Focus on kafan al-kifaya: the minimum that suffices.
2
Locate the dalil (hadith evidence)
The text cites two hadiths: the Prophet's instruction 'Shroud him in his two garments' (referring to a man who died in ihram) and the incident of Mus'ab ibn Umayr shrouded in a single garment.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'thawbayhi' (his two garments) indicates that two garments are sufficient. The command is understood as recommendation (nadb) not obligation (wujub) because of the necessity case of Mus'ab.
The imperative form (amr) in the context of shroud is interpreted as recommendation due to the evidence of necessity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the sunnah shroud for both men and women is three garments, and he rejects the turban. There is also intra-Hanafi variation regarding the turban and the exact composition of the shroud.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that kafan al-kifaya for a man is izar and lifafa; for a woman, izar, lifafa, and khimar. The sunnah shroud is three for a man and five for a woman.
Later scholars (al-muta'akhkhirun) recommended the turban for men, but some Hanafi texts consider it disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستحسن المتأخرون العمامة ولها : دِرْع ، وإزار ، وخمار، ولفافة، وخرقة تربط بها ثدياها . وكفايته له : إزار ولفافة، ولها ثوبان، وخمار) : الثوبان الإزار، واللفافة. والكفن على ثلاثة أقسام : كفن سنة ؛ وهو ثلاثة للرجل وخمسة للمرأة. وكفن كفاية : وهو ثوبان للرجل وثلاثة للمرأة، بمعنى أنه لو كُفّن في هذه القدر يكفي. وكفن الضَّرورة : وهو ثوب واحدٌ إذا لم يوجد ما زاد عليه. والأصل فيه ما روي أنَّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال الرجل مات في إحرامه في سفر حجَّةِ الوداع بعرفات: «كفنوه في ثوبه ) ، أخرجه البخاري ومسلم وغيرهما، وأخرجا أيضاً: «أن مصعب بن عمير له لما استشهد في غزوة أحد لم يخلف إلا نمرة كفن فيها».
The later scholars considered the turban recommended. And for her (the woman): a shift, a waist-wrapper, a head-cover, a wrapper, and a piece of cloth with which she ties her breasts. And the sufficiency for him (the man): a waist-wrapper and a wrapper; and for her: two garments and a head-cover. The two garments are the waist-wrapper and the wrapper. The shroud is of three types: the shroud of sunnah, which is three for a man and five for a woman; the shroud of sufficiency, which is two garments for a man and three for a woman, meaning that if he is shrouded in this amount it suffices; and the shroud of necessity, which is one garment if nothing more is found. The basis for this is what is narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said regarding a man who died in his state of ihram on the journey of the Farewell Pilgrimage at Arafat: 'Shroud him in his two garments' – narrated by Bukhari and Muslim and others. And they also narrated that Mus'ab ibn Umayr (may Allah be pleased with him) when he was martyred in the Battle of Uhud, he left behind only a striped garment, so he was shrouded in it.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the ruling on the sufficient shroud (kafan al-kifaya) for men and women, along with the recommended (sunnah) and necessity (darura) classifications. First, the text mentions that later scholars (al-muta'akhkhirun) deemed the turban recommended for men, but this is a point of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school; some consider it merely permissible or even disliked. For women, the sunnah shroud consists of five garments: a shift (dir'), a waist-wrapper (izar), a head-cover (khimar), a wrapper (lifafa), and a band (khirqa) to bind the breasts. Then the text defines the sufficient shroud: for a man, two garments suffice—an izar (lower garment) and a lifafa (upper wrapper); for a woman, three garments suffice—two garments (the izar and lifafa) and a khimar (head-cover). The author then categorizes the shroud into three levels: sunnah (complete), kifaya (adequate), and darura (minimum). The proof cited are two hadiths: first, the Prophet's instruction to shroud a man who died in ihram in his two garments (thawbayn), which shows that two garments are sufficient; second, the incident of Mus'ab ibn Umayr who was shrouded in a single striped garment (namira) when no more was available, establishing the permissibility of a single garment in necessity. These narrations are from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim. The Hanafi school relies on these as evidence that the kafan al-kifaya is two garments for a man and three for a woman, while the sunnah is more. Note that the izar and lifafa for a man correspond to the lower and upper body coverings, and the khimar for a woman covers her head and extends to her face without wrapping—details from other Hanafi sources.

Key Terms
كفن الكفاية (kafan al-kifāya): The minimum shroud that suffices for the obligation of burial: two garments for a man, three for a woman.
إزار (izār): A waist-wrapper or lower garment covering from navel to ankles.
لفافة (lifāfa): A wrapper covering the entire body from head to toe, acting as an upper garment.
خمار (khimār): Head-cover for women, extending from head to chest, not wrapped like a turban; its measure is three cubits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum sufficient shroud (kafan al-kifaya) for a woman?
A) Five garments: dir', izar, khimar, lifafa, and khirqa
B) Two garments: izar and lifafa
C) Three garments: izar, lifafa, and khimar
D) One garment only if necessary

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines three levels of shroud, and the sufficient shroud (kafan al-kifaya) is the minimum obligation established by the Prophet's instruction to shroud in two garments and the necessity case of Mus'ab ibn Umayr.

Shrouding Method and the Hanafi–Shafi‘i Dispute on Women's Hair
Explains the wrapping order and disputes on headband and hair arrangement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of shrouding men and women, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the khirqa placement, and evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi‘i argument for braiding the deceased woman's hair.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school places the khirqa under the shirt and leaves the woman's hair in two braids on her chest, rejecting the Shafi‘i three-braid practice as unnecessary adornment.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya combines a clear statement of the Hanafi shrouding procedure with two levels of disagreement: an intra-Hanafi variation about where to tie the headband (khirqa), and a cross-madhhab conflict with Imam al-Shafi‘i over how to arrange a deceased woman's hair. The commentator navigates these disputes by prioritizing explicit hadith evidence (for the khirqa) and a principle of needlessness (for the hair). By the end, you will understand the Hanafi rationale and the thamarah al-khilaf.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the shrouding method for men vs women
Identify the number and order of pieces for each gender: for men: wrapper (lifāfa), sheet (izār), shirt (qamīṣ); for women: same plus head-covering (khimār) and band (khirqa). Note the folding order: left before right so the right side is on top.
The text specifies that for women the head-covering is placed before the izār is folded.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on khirqa placement
List the variant opinions: (a) tied over all shrouds (al-Zayla‘ī), (b) tied over shrouds at the chest above the breasts (al-Tuhfa), (c) on the breasts but under the lifāfa (al-Khujandī), (d) tied over the shirt after the head-covering (al-Ikhtiyār). The commentator then states the strongest view: under the shirt, based on hadith.
The commentator uses 'the apparent' (al-ẓāhir) for al-Khujandī's view, but the hadith evidence overrides.
3
Determine the mufta bihi based on hadith
The commentator concludes that what is established from the hadith in Sunan Abī Dāwūd and others is that the khirqa is under the shirt. This is the relied-upon position.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle that a sound hadith from the Sunnah takes precedence over mere juristic opinion.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi‘i hair-braiding proof
The Shafi‘i cite the practice of the women who washed the Prophet's daughter: they combed her hair into three braids and placed them behind her back. The Hanafi response (from al-‘Aynī) is that this was for adornment, and the deceased has no need for adornment; moreover, the report is ambiguous (muhtamal) and does not firmly establish a ruling.
The Hanafi principle is: 'the deceased is not in need of beautification' – a substantive argument based on the purpose of shrouding.
5
State the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
In the Hanafi school, the woman's hair is not combed into three braids; it is left in its natural state or braided in two and placed on the chest under the head-covering. In the Shafi‘i school, the hair is thoroughly combed and braided into three braids placed behind the back.
This difference affects the preparation of the deceased and reflects underlying principles about the purpose of shrouding.

ويُعْقَدُ الكفنُ إن خيف انتشارُهُ .

The wrapper is spread, then the wrapper upon it, then the deceased is put in the shirt, and placed on the wrapper, then the left side of his wrapper is folded, then his right, then the wrapper similarly. And she wears the chemise, and her hair is made into two braids on her chest, then the head-covering above it under the wrapper. [Commentator on 'and spreads...': start in the description of shrouding after mentioning its number. Summary: the wrapper is spread under all so it is above everything when wrapping, then the wrapper, which is another sheet, then the shirt. He first puts on the shirt, then folds the left of his wrapper first then his right so that the right is above. Then folds the left of the wrapper then its right. This is for a man. For a woman: spread the wrapper, then place the wrapper, then she puts on the shirt first, then the head-covering above it, then the wrapper is folded then the wrapper as before. There is disagreement about the place of the band. In Sharh al-Kanz by al-Zayla'i: it is tied above the shrouds so they do not spread. In al-Tuhfa: tied above the shrouds at the chest over the breasts. In al-Jawhara: al-Khujandi said: tied on the breasts over the shrouds. It may be meant under the wrapper and over the wrapper and shirt, and that is apparent. In al-Ikhtiyar: she wears the shirt, then the head-covering above it, then the band is tied over the shirt. What is established from hadith narrations in Sunan Abi Dawud and others: the band is under the shirt as well. [Commentator on 'and makes her hair': al-Ayni said in al-Binaya: al-Shafi`i said: her hair is combed and made into three braids and placed behind her back because those who washed the daughter of the Prophet , may God bless him and grant him peace, did so. As recorded by al-Bukhari and others, and apparently they did so by the command of the Prophet. We say: this is for adornment and the deceased has no need of it, and what he narrated is subject to possibility, and the ruling is not established by it. End. And the shroud is tied if it is feared it will spread. [Commentator on 'if it is feared': meaning if there is fear of the shroud spreading, separating, and exposing the deceased, it is tied with two knots at the side of the head and feet.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and a ruling statement on the method of shrouding. The author first states the method for men: spread the outer wrapper (lifafa), then the izār (sheet) upon it, then put on the qamīṣ (shirt), then place the deceased on the izār, then fold the left side of the izār first, then the right (so the right side is on top), then similarly the outer wrapper. For women, the method differs: after spreading the outer wrapper and placing the izār, she is first dressed in the chemise (dir‘), then the head-covering (khimār) is placed, then the izār is folded, then the outer wrapper. The commentator adds details: the purpose of folding left before right is to have the right side uppermost, which is respectful. The passage then discusses a significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf about the placement of the headband (khirqa). Several opinions are cited from Hanafi scholars: al-Zayla‘ī says it is tied over all the shrouds to prevent them from spreading; in al-Tuhfa, it is tied over the shrouds at the chest above the breasts; al-Khujandī places it on the breasts over the shrouds (which the author considers apparent, meaning under the outer wrapper but above the izār and shirt); al-Ikhtiyār places it over the shirt but under the head-covering. The strongest position, established from hadith in Sunan Abī Dāwūd, is that the band is placed under the shirt. Then an inter-madhhab dispute with al-Shāfi‘ī arises: Shāfi‘ī combed the deceased woman's hair into three braids and placed them behind her back, citing the practice of those who washed the Prophet's daughter. The Hanafi response (from al-‘Aynī) is that this was for beautification, which the deceased does not need, and the hadith is ambiguous; the ruling is not proven. Finally, a practical ruling: if there is fear that the shroud may come undone, it may be tied with two knots at the head and feet. The passage stays strictly within the Hanafi school's views, prioritizing textual evidence and practical necessity.

Key Terms
الخرقة (al-khirqa): A headband or piece of cloth tied around the head of a female deceased to secure the hair and shroud.
اللفافة (al-lifāfa): The outermost wrapper that encloses the entire shroud bundle.
الإزار (al-izār): A sheet or wrapper that is placed over the shirt and under the lifāfa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in the passage, where should the headband (khirqa) be placed for a deceased woman?
A) Over all the shrouds
B) Under the shirt, based on hadith evidence
C) On the chest over the izār
D) On the breasts over the lifāfa

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method shrouds men in three pieces and women in five, with the khirqa tied under the shirt and the hair in two braids on the chest, rejecting braiding behind the back as unnecessary.
