Funeral Prayer: Communal Obligation and Four Takbirs
Ruling with proof for the funeral prayer's obligation and number of takbirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the funeral prayer is fard kifayah, describe its essential elements (four takbirs performed standing), and explain the ijma-based proof for four takbirs.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer is a communal obligation of four takbirs, proven by Prophetic practice and Companions' consensus.

This lesson addresses the legal ruling of the funeral prayer (ṣalāt al-janāzah) as a communal obligation and the number of takbirs. The passage begins by declaring it fard kifāyah, then describes the method: four takbirs performed standing. It provides the evidence from the Prophet's action and the Companions' consensus. Understanding this ruling is essential for knowing when the obligation is fulfilled or when the community sins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its definition
Locate the phrase 'wa ṣalāt fard kifāyah'. Understand that the commentator explains it: an obligation on each individual, but if some perform it, the duty drops from the rest; if all neglect, all sin.
This is the standard Hanafi definition of fard kifayah.
2
Describe the method (how it is performed)
The text says 'an yukabbira rafi'an yadayhi' – he says takbir raising his hands. The commentator adds that he performs it standing, each takbir stands in place of a rak'ah. So there are four takbirs.
Standing is a condition; sitting only without excuse invalidates.
3
Locate the proof for four takbirs
The author cites two proofs: the Prophet's practice (from Sunan Ibn Majah) and the ijma (consensus) of the Companions gathered at Ibn Mas'ud's house that the takbir is four. The second proof is explicitly quoted in Arabic.
The hadith and ijma are the basis; narrations of five or six takbirs are abrogated.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah of the ijma proof
The Companions 'agreed' (ajma'ū) that the takbir in funerals is four. This agreement is binding evidence (ḥujjah) for the number. The Hanafi school relies on ijma as a primary source.
The ijma is considered qaṭ'ī in dalālah (definitive in meaning) but zannī in thubūt (transmission) because it is narrated through a single chain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصلاة فرض كفاية وهي : أن يكبر رافعاً يديه ، ثُمَّ لَا رَفَعَ بعدها), خلافاً للشافعي
[قوله : أي إن أدّى ... الخ ؛ هذا هو حكم فرض الكفاية ؛ فإنه يكون فرضاً على كل واحد واحد، لكن بحيث إن أدى بعض منهم سقط عن الباقين، وإن لم يؤد واحد منهم أثم الجميع بترك الفرض ، وإن أدى الكل وجدوا ثواب الفرض، وتحقيقه في كتب الأصول.
[قوله : أن يكبر ؛ أي قائماً ، فلم يجز قاعداً بلا عذر، وهذه التكبيرات كل منها قائمة مقام ركعة. كذا في «الدر المختار». والأصل في تربيع التكبيراتِ ما ثبت في «سنن ابن ماجة» وغيره : «إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كبر على الجنازة أربعاً، وعند البيهقي : عن إبراهيم النخعي قال : «اجتمع أصحابُ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في بيت ابن مسعود الله فأجمعوا على أنَّ التكبير في الجنائز أربع»، وقد روى رواية التكبيرات الخمس والست أيضاً لكنه منسوخ كما حققه الحازمي في كتاب «الناسخ والمنسوخ».
[قوله : رافعاً يديه؛ لكون رفع اليدين مسنوناً عند تكبيرة التحريمة مطلقاً.
[قوله : خلافاً للشافعي له ؛ وكذا لأحمد ومالك ، بل قال برفع اليدين في كل تكبير أئمة بلخ من مشايخنا ، وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة له أيضاً. كذا في «شرح دررِ البحار».
And its prayer is a communal obligation. And it is: that he says the takbir raising his hands, then no raising after it, contrary to al-Shafi'i. [Commentator on 'that he says the takbir': meaning standing, so it is not permissible sitting without excuse. Each of these takbirs stands in place of a rakah. So in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. The basis for the four takbirs is what is established in Sunan Ibn Majah and others: 'The Prophet , peace be upon him, said four takbirs over the funeral.' And from al-Bayhaqi, from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, he said: 'The companions of the Messenger of God , may God bless him and grant him peace, gathered in the house of Ibn Mas'ud and unanimously agreed that the takbir in funerals is four.' And the narration of five or six takbirs has also been narrated, but it is abrogated as verified by al-Hazimi in his book al-Nasikh wa al-Mansukh. [Commentator on 'raising his hands': because raising the hands is sunnah at the takbirat al-tahrimah absolutely. [Commentator on 'contrary to al-Shafi'i': and similarly Ahmad and Malik. Rather, the scholars of Balkh from our imams said raising hands in every takbir, and it is also a narration from Abu Hanifah. So in Sharh Durar al-Bihar.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the funeral prayer (ṣalāt al-janāzah). It opens by declaring that the funeral prayer is a fard kifāyah (communal obligation). The commentator explains: it is an obligation upon each individual, but if some perform it, the rest are absolved; if none perform it, all sin; if all perform it, all obtain reward. This definition is standard in uṣūl al-fiqh. The method: the prayer consists of four takbīrs (saying 'Allāhu Akbar'), performed standing (not sitting without excuse). Each takbīr is equivalent to a rak'ah in regular prayer. The proof for four takbīrs is from ḥadīth: the Prophet himself said four takbīrs, and the Companions unanimously agreed on four in the house of Ibn Mas'ūd. Reports of five or six takbīrs are abrogated. The text then addresses raising the hands: it is sunnah to raise the hands only at the first takbīr (the taḥrīmah), and not at the subsequent ones. This is contrary to Imām al-Shāfi'ī (and Aḥmad and Mālik), who raise hands at every takbīr. However, the commentator notes that some Ḥanafī scholars (from Balkh) and a narration from Abū Ḥanīfah himself support raising at every takbīr. Despite this ikhtilāf, the established position in the Ḥanafī school is to raise only at the first takbīr.

Key Terms
فرض كفاية (fard kifāyah): A communal obligation: if some Muslims perform it, the obligation is fulfilled; if all neglect it, all sin.
تكبيرة التحريمة (takbīrat al-taḥrīmah): The first takbir that commences the prayer and enters one into the state of ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The practice of the four caliphs
B) The Prophet's own practice and the consensus of the Companions
C) The Qur'anic verse on funerals
D) The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifah alone

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) consisting of four takbirs, proven by the Prophet's practice and Companions' consensus, and standing is a condition for validity.

The Dispute on Raising Hands in Funeral Prayer
Inter- and intra-madhhab dispute on raising hands in funeral prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position (raise hands only at the first takbir), explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (Balkh scholars and a narration from Abu Hanifah), and evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, hands are raised only at the first takbir of funeral prayer, despite an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf and contrary to the Shafi'is.

This lesson examines the specific issue of raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) during the takbirs of the funeral prayer. The passage states the Hanafi position: raising hands is sunnah only at the first takbir (takbirat al-tahrimah), and not at the subsequent ones. It then notes the contrary views of Imam al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and Malik, who raise at every takbir. The passage also reveals an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: some Hanafi scholars from Balkh and even a narration from Abu Hanifah himself support raising at every takbir. Understanding this dispute helps one appreciate the process of tarjih within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position stated in the text
The base text says: 'yukabbiru rafi'an yadayhi, thumma lā rafa'a ba'dahā' – he says the first takbir raising his hands, then no raising after it. This is the relied-upon view.
The commentator emphasizes that raising hands is sunnah at the first takbir absolutely.
2
Locate the contrary inter-madhhab positions
The text says 'khilāfan lil-Shāfi'ī' and adds that similarly Ahmad and Malik hold the opposite view: they raise hands at every takbir.
The Shafi'i school is the main opponent; Ahmad and Malik are also mentioned.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The commentator notes that the scholars of Balkh from our (Hanafi) imams said raising hands in every takbir, and there is also a narration (riwāyah) from Abu Hanifah himself supporting that view.
This shows that even within the Hanafi school there was disagreement on this ruling.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
Despite the existence of the other narration, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the one stated in the base text: only raise at the first takbir. The commentator cites al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Sharh Durar al-Bihar as authorities for this tarjih.
The Zahir al-Riwayah (the established transmission) supports the first position.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The difference affects how the funeral prayer is performed. A Hanafi praying a funeral will only raise hands at the first takbir, while a Shafi'i will raise at all four. This is a visible difference in practice.
Knowing this helps avoid confusion in mixed-madhhab settings.

Funeral Prayer: Communal Obligation, Procedure, and the Quran Recitation Dispute
States ruling, procedure, and dispute on recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral prayer as fard kifayah, describe its procedure with four takbirs, and explain the inter-madhhab dispute regarding Quran recitation with evidence from hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer is pure supplication; Hanafis omit Quran recitation, unlike Shafi'is who require Fatihah.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the legal status and performance of the funeral prayer. It clarifies that it is a communal obligation and details the sequence of takbirs and supplications. A key point of disagreement between the Hanafi school and others concerns whether Quran recitation is part of this prayer. The commentator presents both the standard Hanafi view and notes a minority opinion within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling classification
What is the funeral prayer and what is its hukm? The passage states it is a communal obligation (fard kifayah). Understand the consequences: if some perform, obligation lifts; if none, all sin.
Fard kifayah vs. fard 'ayn is a key distinction.
2
Describe the procedure
List the sequence after the first takbir: thana, second takbir + salawat, third takbir + dua, fourth takbir + salam. Note that hands are raised only at the first takbir per the standard view.
The commentary mentions an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on hand-raising.
3
Locate the proof for four takbirs
The passage cites hadith from Ibn Majah and the consensus of Companions (Ibn Mas'ud's house). Understand that five or six takbirs are considered abrogated.
The dalil is ahad but considered qati' in dalalah for Hanafis.
4
Compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on Quran recitation
State each school's claim: Hanafi – no recitation, prayer is supplication; Shafi'i – Fatihah is required after first takbir. Identify the evidence for each from the passage.
Hanafi proof: hadith 'sincerely make supplication'; Shafi'i proof: qiyas on regular prayer.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response and practical difference
How does the Hanafi school rebut the opposing dalil? They distinguish funeral prayer as a supplication, not a standard prayer. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Hanafis omit recitation, making the prayer shorter.
The note about Shurunbulali's treatise shows internal Hanafi acknowledgment of the Shafi'i view's strength.

[4] قوله : رافعاً يديه؛ لكون رفع اليدين مسنوناً عند تكبيرة التحريمة مطلقاً.
[5] قوله : خلافاً للشافعي؛ وكذا لأحمد ومالك ، بل قال برفع اليدين في كل تكبير أئمة بلخ من مشايخنا ، وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة أيضاً. كذا في «شرح دررِ البحار».

ويثني ، ثم يكبر، ويُصلي على النبي ، ثُمَّ يُكبر ويدعو ، ثُمَّ يكبِّرُ ويُسلّم، ولا قراءة فيها
[1] قوله : ويثني؛ وهو الثَّناءُ المعروف مع زيادة مستحسنة، يعني: سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك، تبارك اسمك، وتعالى جدك، وجلّ ثناؤك، ولا إله غيرك. كذا في «شرح المنية».
[2] قوله : ويصلّي؛ أي بالصَّلاة التي يُصلّي بها بعد التشهد، ولو صلّى بغيرها لا بأس به.
[3] قوله : ويدعو؛ أي للميت ولنفسه وللمسلمين، بأي لفظ شاء، والمأثور أولى، وسيأتي ذكره.

The shroud is tied if its spreading is feared. Its prayer is a communal obligation: that he says takbir raising his hands, then no raising after it. [Commentary: (1) If there is fear of the shroud spreading and uncovering the deceased, it is tied with two knots at the head and feet. (2) This is the ruling of fard kifayah: it is an obligation on everyone such that if some perform it, it falls from the rest; if none do, all sin; if all do, they receive the reward. (3) 'That he says takbir' means standing; sitting without excuse is not permissible. These takbirs each stand in place of a rak'ah. The basis for four takbirs is established in Sunan Ibn Majah: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) said four takbirs over the deceased.' And al-Bayhaqi reports from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the Companions agreed on four takbirs. Narrations of five or six takbirs are abrogated. (4) 'Raising his hands' because raising hands is sunnah at the opening takbir absolutely. (5) Contrary to al-Shafi'i, and likewise to Ahmad and Malik. Rather, the imams of Balkh among our scholars say to raise hands in every takbir, and it is also a narration from Abu Hanifa.]

Then he praises, then says takbir, and sends salawat on the Prophet, then says takbir and makes supplication, then says takbir and says salam. There is no recitation in it. [Commentary: (1) 'Then he praises' is the well-known thana with a good addition: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika, tabarakasmuka, wa ta'ala jadduka, wa jalla thana'uka, wa la ilaha ghayruka.' (2) 'He sends salawat' is the salawat said after tashahhud; if he says something else, it is fine. (3) 'Supplication' is for the deceased, himself, and the Muslims, in any wording he wishes; the transmitted wording is better. (4) 'Says salam' to the right and left, raising his voice as he raises his voice in each takbir. As for supplication, thana, and salawat, the sunnah is to be silent. (5) 'No recitation' means recitation of the Quran is not obligatory nor sunnah in our view with the intention of Quran; if one recites al-Fatihah with the intention of thana, it is permissible. The basis is the hadith: 'When you pray over the deceased, sincerely make supplication for him' reported by Abu Dawud, and it is the transmitted practice from Ibn Umar and Abu Hurairah. (6) Contrary to al-Shafi'i, for with him he recites al-Fatihah after the first takbir, and it is stronger in evidence; al-Shurunbulali chose it from our companions and authored a treatise on it.]
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, a commentary on al-Wiqayah, treats the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). It first clarifies that the shroud may be tied to prevent unwrapping. Then it states that the funeral prayer is a communal obligation (fard kifayah): if some perform it, the obligation lifts from the community; if none do, all are sinful. The commentator explains the legal category of fard kifayah in detail. The procedure begins with the first takbir while raising the hands, and after that, the hands are not raised again (the standard Hanafi view). However, the commentary notes a minority Hanafi view from the scholars of Balkh and a riwaya from Abu Hanifa allowing hand-raising in every takbir. The basis for four takbirs is a hadith from Ibn Majah and the consensus of the Companions as reported by al-Bayhaqi. The commands for five or six are abrogated.

Then the text details the sequence: after the first takbir, one recites the thana (praise), then a second takbir followed by salawat on the Prophet, then a third takbir followed by dua for the deceased and all Muslims, then a fourth takbir followed by salam to right and left. The commentator specifies the wording of thana and notes that the salawat is the same as after tashahhud. Dua may be in any language, but transmitted formulas are preferred. The salam is pronounced audibly like the takbirs, while the preceding supplications are silent.

The major point of dispute is Quran recitation. According to the Hanafi school, recitation (specifically Surah al-Fatihah) is neither obligatory nor recommended in the funeral prayer. If one recites it with the intention of thana, it is permissible, but not as Quran. The proof is the hadith commanding sincere dua for the deceased, implying that the prayer is all supplication, not recitation. The Shafi'i school, however, requires recitation of al-Fatihah after the first takbir. The commentator mentions that Imam al-Shurunbulali of the Hanafi school considered the Shafi'i view stronger in evidence and wrote a treatise on it, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is to omit recitation. The passage thus presents both the standard Hanafi ruling and the inter-madhhab disagreement.

Key Terms
صلاة الجنازة (salat al-janazah): The funeral prayer performed over the deceased Muslim; it is a communal obligation consisting of four takbirs with specific supplications.
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A collective obligation; if some members of the community perform it, the obligation is lifted from all; if none perform, all are sinful.
تكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar'; in funeral prayer, it is said four times, each takbir replaces a rak'ah in terms of separating the components.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, what is the number of takbirs in the funeral prayer?
A) Three
B) Four
C) Five
D) Six

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer is a communal obligation consisting of four takbirs with supplication, and the Hanafi school omits Quran recitation based on hadith commanding sincere dua, differing from the Shafi'i school.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Actions of the Funeral Prayer and the Ruling on Recitation
Describes the sequence of the funeral prayer and the prohibition of Qur'an recitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of actions in the Hanafi funeral prayer and explain the ruling on recitation of the Qur'an, including the evidence and the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer is a pure supplication — reciting the Qur'an distracts from its purpose.

In this passage, the author lays out the prescribed actions of the funeral prayer: praise, salutation, supplication, and taslim, each after a takbir. He then emphasizes that reciting the Qur'an is not part of this prayer, contrary to the Shafi'i school. The commentary explains each element and provides the proof for the Hanafi position. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the purpose of the funeral prayer and the evidence from hadith and practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of actions
After each of the four takbirs, the Hanafi funeral prayer consists of: thana' (praise), salat (salutation upon the Prophet), dua (supplication), and taslim (final salutation). Note the specific act after each takbir.
The first takbir is followed by thana', second by salat, third by dua, fourth by taslim. Some sources mention thana' after the first takbir, then salat after the second, etc.
2
Examine the ruling on recitation
The matn explicitly states there is no recitation (qira'ah) in the funeral prayer. The commentary clarifies that it is neither obligatory (wajib) nor recommended (sunnah) to recite Qur'an, including the Fatiha, with the intention of Qur'an. If one recites Fatiha with the intention of praise, it is permissible.
The ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; the Shafi'i school holds that reciting Fatiha after the first takbir is sunnah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The primary hadith cited is: 'When you pray over the dead, be sincere in supplication for him.' This emphasizes that the prayer is fundamentally a supplication (dua), and reciting Qur'an contradicts that purpose. Also cited is the practice of Ibn Umar and Abu Hurairah, who did not recite.
The hadith is reported by Abu Dawood, Ibn Majah, Ibn Hibban. It is considered zanni al-thubut but sufficient as proof for the Hanafi position.
4
Understand the Shafi'i counter-evidence and Hanafi response
The Shafi'i school relies on the hadith of Abu Umamah: 'The sunnah in the funeral prayer is to recite the Fatiha...' The Hanafi response is that this hadith is not strong enough to override the practice of the Companions and the primary purpose of dua; it may be interpreted as permissibility rather than obligation, and it is a weaker opinion within the Hanafi school.
Some later Hanafi scholars like al-Shurunbulali considered the Shafi'i evidence stronger, but the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) remains no recitation.
5
Recognize the practical difference
In practice, a Hanafi will not recite the Fatiha, while a Shafi'i will recite it silently after the first takbir. A Hanafi following al-Shurunbulali may recite, but the madhhab position is to abstain.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the actual performance of the prayer. It affects the imam and the congregation.

And he praises (Allah), then says the takbir, and sends salutations upon the Prophet, then says the takbir and supplicates, then says the takbir and makes the taslim, and there is no recitation in it, contrary to al-Shafi'i. [Commentary: He said 'and he praises' meaning the well-known praise with a recommended addition... He said 'and he sends salutations' meaning with the salutation used after the tashahhud... He said 'and he supplicates' meaning for the deceased, himself, and the Muslims... He said 'and he makes the taslim' meaning to the right and left, raising his voice as he raises his voice with every takbir... He said 'and no recitation' meaning it is neither obligatory nor recommended in our school to recite the Qur'an in it, intending the Qur'an; if one recites the Fatiha with the intention of praise, it is permissible... He said 'contrary to al-Shafi'i' for he recites the Fatiha after the first takbir, and this is the stronger in proof, and it is what al-Shurunbulali chose from our companions... 'The sunnah in the funeral prayer is to recite the Fatiha...'
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute. The matn states the actions of the funeral prayer: after the first takbir, one praises Allah (thana'), then after the second takbir sends salutations upon the Prophet (salat), then after the third takbir makes supplication (dua), then after the fourth takbir makes the taslim. The matn emphasizes that there is no Qur'an recitation in the funeral prayer, contrary to al-Shafi'i. The commentary expands each element: the thana' is the well-known formula; the salat is the same as in tashahhud but any form suffices; the dua is for the deceased and others; the taslim is to both sides with a raised voice while the other acts are done silently. Regarding no recitation, the commentary clarifies that reciting the Qur'an (e.g., Fatiha) is neither obligatory nor sunnah in the Hanafi school because the primary purpose of the funeral prayer is supplication for the deceased, as per the hadith 'when you pray over the dead, be sincere in supplication for him.' However, if one recites Fatiha with the intention of praise (thana'), it is permissible. The dispute with al-Shafi'i: he requires recitation of Fatiha after the first takbir. The commentary notes that al-Shurunbulali chose the Shafi'i position as the stronger in proof, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is to not recite. Evidence for the Hanafi position includes the practice of Ibn Umar and Abu Hurairah (who only praised and supplicated without reciting), and the hadith from Abu Umamah which includes recitation but is interpreted as a difference in practice. The author also mentions the hadith of Abu Umamah reported by al-Shafi'i and al-Hakim supporting recitation, acknowledging the difference of opinion.

Key Terms
قراءة (qira'ah): Recitation of the Qur'an, specifically the Fatiha, in the funeral prayer.
ثناء (thana'): Praise of Allah, specifically the formula 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...'
صلاة على النبي (salat 'ala al-nabi): Sending salutations upon the Prophet, similar to that recited after tashahhud.

D) It is obligatory only for the imam.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the funeral prayer consists of praise, salutation, supplication, and taslim after each of the four takbirs, with no Qur'an recitation, based on the hadith emphasizing sincere supplication.

No Tashahhud and Supplication for a Child in Funeral Prayer
States the absence of tashahhud and the specific supplication for a deceased child.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that tashahhud is not recited in the funeral prayer and recite the prescribed supplication for a deceased child after the third takbir.

Core Idea
In the funeral prayer, no tashahhud is recited; for a child, the supplication asks Allah to make him a forerunner to the Hawd.

The funeral prayer (Salat al-Janazah) differs from the regular five daily prayers in several ways. One key difference is the absence of tashahhud, the testimony of faith recited while sitting. Another is that the supplications (dua) vary depending on the deceased — for a child, a special dua has been transmitted from the Companions. This passage from a commentary on al-Wiqayah states these two rulings concisely, with a brief explanation of the term 'farat'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the passage
Read the opening sentence: 'Wa la tashahhud' (and no tashahhud) and 'wa yaqulu fi al-sabi...' (and he says for the child...). These are the two rulings: omission of tashahhud and a specific dua for a child.
2
Recognise the liturgical timing of the dua
The dua is made 'after the third (takbir)'. The funeral prayer consists of four takbirs. The first is followed by praise (thana), the second by salawat on the Prophet, the third by this dua for the child, and the fourth concludes with salam.
The adult dua is different and is also said after the third takbir.
3
Understand the term 'farat'
The commentary explains 'faratan' (a forerunner) as one who goes ahead to the Hawd (the Prophet's basin) to prepare water. The dua asks Allah to make the child such a forerunner for his family.
This reflects a beautiful hope that the child will intercede for his parents.
4
Note the source of the dua
The commentary mentions that this supplication is transmitted from Abu Hurairah and others, recorded by al-Bayhaqi. This gives it a sound basis in the sunnah.

Source Text

And there is no tashahhud, and he says for the child after the third (takbir): 'O Allah, make him for us a forerunner (faratan).' [Commentary: He said 'and there is no tashahhud' meaning there is no recitation of tashahhud after the fourth takbir, because it has not been reported. Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding two aspects of the funeral prayer: first, there is no tashahhud (the sitting and greeting recited in regular prayers), so one does not recite the tashahhud after the fourth takbir. Second, for a deceased child (sabiyy), after the third takbir one should recite a specific supplication: 'O Allah, make him for us a forerunner (faratan).' The term 'farat' refers to someone who goes ahead to the Hawd (the Prophet's basin) to prepare water. This supplication is traced back to the practice of Abu Hurairah and others, reported by al-Bayhaqi. The absence of tashahhud is based on the lack of any transmission regarding it in the context of funeral prayer.

Key Terms
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited in regular prayers; not recited in the funeral prayer.
فرط (farat): One who goes ahead to the Hawd (the Prophet's basin) to prepare water; a forerunner.

No Tashahhud in Funeral Prayer and Supplication for a Child
Commentary on rulings and supplications in funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that tashahhud is not recited in funeral prayer and recite the correct supplication for a deceased child.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer does not include tashahhud; the du'a for a child asks Allah to make him a forerunner.

This commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies two specific rulings of the Hanafi funeral prayer: the omission of tashahhud and the prescribed supplication for a deceased child. The author supports these with reports from the Companions and explains the meaning of key terms like 'faratan' and 'dhukhran'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that tashahhud is not recited in the funeral prayer. This is the Hanafi position based on the absence of any report from the Prophet (peace be upon him) or his Companions.
This distinguishes janazah from regular prayers where tashahhud is an integral part.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the practice of Companions like Ibn 'Umar who did not recite in janazah, and the hadith of Abu Umamah that describes the sunnah as reciting Fatiha, sending salawat on the Prophet, then supplicating, then salams – no tashahhud.
The dalil is ahad (solitary) but accepted by the majority.
3
Trace the supplication for a child
After the third takbir, one says: 'Allahummaj'alhu lana faratan' (O Allah, make him a forerunner for us). This du'a is reported from Abu Hurairah and others.
The term 'faratan' means one who goes ahead to prepare water at the Hawd.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that tashahhud is recited after the fourth takbir. The Hanafi school rejects this due to lack of evidence.
The disagreement is on the content of the prayer, not its validity.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi because it is based on the established sunnah as practiced by the Companions and recorded in reliable hadith works.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah adopts this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ولا تشهد، ويقول في الصبي بعد الثالثة : اللهم اجعلهُ لنا فَرَطاً) لقوله تعالى: (ولا تشهد) أي ليست فيها قراءة التشهد بعد التكبيرة الرابعة؛ لعدم ورود ذلك. (ويقول) هذا الدعاء للطفل مأثور عن أبي هريرة وغيره، عند البيهقي وغيره. (فَرَطاً) بفتحتين: أي سابقاً إلى الحوض يهيئ الماء. وحمدت الله، وصليت على نبيه، ثم أقول: اللهم إنه عبدك وابن عبدك وابن أمتك، كان يشهد أن لا إله إلا أنت وأن محمداً عبدك ورسولك، وأنت أعلم به، اللهم إن كان محسناً فزد في إحسانه، وإن كان مسيئاً فتجاوز عن سيئاته، اللهم لا تحرمنا أجره، ولا تفتنا بعده. وعن نافع: إن عبد الله بن عمر كان لا يقرأ في الصلاة على الجنازة. وعن إبراهيم الهجري قال: أمنا عبد الله بن أبي أوفى على جنازة ابنته فكبر أربعاً، ظننا أنه سيكبر خمساً، ثم سلم عن يمينه وعن شماله، فلما انصرف قلنا له: ما هذا؟ قال: إني لا أزيدكم على ما رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصنع أو هكذا صنع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. The Book of Prayer, Chapter of Funerals. (And do not recite the tashahhud, and for a child after the third [takbir] say: 'O Allah, make him for us a forerunner.') His saying: 'and do not recite the tashahhud' i.e., there is no recitation of the tashahhud after the fourth takbir; because there is no report of that. His saying: 'and say' this supplication for the child is reported from Abu Hurairah and others, recorded by al-Bayhaqi and others. 'Faraṭan' with two fathaḥs: i.e., one who goes ahead to the Basin to prepare water. (Then he said a longer supplication...) And from Nāfi': that Ibn ʿUmar would not recite in the funeral prayer. And from Ibrāhīm al-Hajarī: he led us in prayer over his daughter, said four takbirs, then we thought he would say a fifth, then he gave salām to right and left; when asked, he said he only did as he saw the Prophet do. (O Allah, make him for us a stored treasure, O Allah, make him for us an intercessor whose intercession is accepted) i.e., a reward that precedes us... The supplication for adults is: 'O Allah, forgive our living and our dead, those present and absent, our young and old, our males and females; O Allah, whom You give life from us, give him life upon Islam; whom You take from us, take him upon faith.' And He said in the first 'Islam' and in the second 'faith' because...
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This is a commentary on the ruling that in the funeral prayer, one does not recite the tashahhud. The proof is that there is no report of doing so. Instead, after the third takbir for a deceased child, one says: 'Allahummaj'alhu lana faratan' (make him a forerunner for us). The author then supports this with hadith: Ibn 'Umar did not recite in janazah, and Ibn Abi Awfa performed four takbirs and salams as per the Sunnah, no tashahhud. For a child, the supplication is to ask that the child be a forerunner to the Basin (Hawd). The commentary also explains the words 'dhukhran' (treasure) and 'shafi'an musaffa'an' (intercessor accepted). For adults, the well-known supplication asking forgiveness for all and asking to die upon faith is mentioned, with a note on the distinction between Islam and Iman.

Key Terms
فَرَطاً (faraṭan): A forerunner who goes ahead to prepare water at the Basin (Hawd).
ذخراً (dhukhran): A stored treasure (thawāb) for the parents.
شافعاً مشفعاً (shāfi'an musaffa'an): An intercessor whose intercession is accepted.
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited in regular prayers (at-tahiyyat).

The Supplication for the Deceased and the Distinction Between Islam and Iman
Explaining the prophetic supplication for the deceased and the theological distinction between Islam and Iman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recite the prophetic supplication for the deceased, state its ruling in the Hanafi school, and explain the wisdom behind the use of 'Islam' and 'Iman' in the du'a.

Core Idea
The funeral supplication is a sunnah; 'Islam' governs life, 'Iman' governs death.

The funeral prayer includes a beautiful and profound supplication taught by the Prophet ﷺ. In this lesson, we explore the meaning of this du'a and a subtle theological distinction between Islam and Iman that the du'a highlights. Understanding this distinction enriches our practice and deepens our faith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognise that the du'a in the funeral prayer is a recommended (sunnah) act, not obligatory. The proof is the hadith itself; the imperative form indicates recommendation.
The ruling is derived from the zanni dalil.
2
Analyze the dalil
Examine the hadith 'Allahumma ighfir li-hayyina...' as the primary proof. Its transmission is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and its meaning is clear (zanni al-dalala), leading to a sunnah ruling.
The du'a is sunnah, not wajib.
3
Examine the wording
Note the dua asks for life upon Islam and death upon Iman. Reflect on why different terms are used for life and death.
The author highlights the contextual nuance.
4
Understand the distinction
Islam emphasizes outward submission and action, fitting for life where deeds are possible. Iman emphasizes inward conviction and affirmation, crucial at the moment of death when actions cease.
This distinction is the key legal and theological insight.
5
Note the theological ikhtilaf
The passage ends with a difference of opinion on the definition of Iman: some say tasdiq (affirmation) alone suffices for salvation, while the Hanafi position requires both tasdiq and iqrar (verbal confession) for worldly rulings.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اللهم اجعله لنا ذُخْراً، اللهم اجعله لنا شافعاً مشفّعاً) : أي أجراً يتقدمنا ، وأصل الفارط والفرط فيمن يتقدم الواردة. كذا في «المغرب»، والمشفّعُ الذي يُعطى له الشفاعة. والدعاء للبالغين هذا ": اللهم اغفر لحينا وميتنا، وشاهدنا، وغائبنا وصغيرنا، وكبيرنا ، وذَكَرِنا ، وأنثانا ، اللهُمَّ مَن احييته منا فأحيه على الإسلام، ومَن توفَّيَتَهُ مِنَّا فَتَوَفَّهُ على الإيمان. وإنما قال في الأَوَّل الإسلام، وفي الثَّاني الإيمان ؛ لأنَّ الإسلام والإيمان وإن كانا متحدين، فالإسلامُ يُنبيُّ عن الانقياد فكأنه دعاء في حال الحياة بالإيمان والإنقياد ، وأما عند الوفاة فقد دعا بالتّوفّي على الإيمان، وهو التصديق ، والإقرار ; يعني التصديق بالجنان بالتوحيد والرسالة وما جاء به الرسول ، والإقرار بذلك باللسان، وهذا عند البعض، وعند البعض الإيمان المنجي : هو التصديقُ فقط، والإقرار شرط لإجزاء أحكام الدُّنيا، وتحقيقه في كتب علم الكلام.
O Allah, make it for us a treasure, O Allah, make it for us an intercessor whose intercession is accepted: meaning a reward that precedes us. The origin of 'al-farit' and 'al-farat' is for one who goes ahead to prepare for the incoming. As in 'al-Mughrib'. And 'al-mushaffa' is one who is granted intercession. And the supplication for the adults is this: 'O Allah, forgive our living and our dead, our present and our absent, our young and our old, our male and our female. O Allah, whomever You keep alive among us, keep him upon Islam, and whomever You cause to die among us, cause him to die upon Iman.' And he only said in the first 'Islam' and in the second 'Iman' because while Islam and Iman are united, Islam indicates submission, so it is as if he supplicated during life for Iman and submission. And at the time of death, he supplicated for dying upon Iman, which is tasdiq (affirmation) and iqrar (confession). That is, affirmation in the heart of tawhid, messengership, and what the Messenger brought, and verbal confession of that. This is according to some; according to others, the saving Iman is only affirmation, and confession is a condition for the implementation of worldly rulings. Its verification is in books of theology.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage explains the well-known supplication for the deceased in the funeral prayer. The author clarifies two key phrases: "ذخراً" (treasure) means a reward stored for the time of need, and "شافعاً مشفعاً" means an intercessor whose intercession is accepted. The supplication itself is the famous hadith: 'اللهم اغفر لحينا وميتنا...' The author then addresses a subtle point: why does the supplication say 'أحيه على الإسلام' (keep him upon Islam) but 'توفه على الإيمان' (cause him to die upon Iman)? He explains that Islam and Iman are essentially the same in sharia—every Muslim is a believer and vice versa—but here the wording distinguishes based on context. Islam emphasizes outward submission and action, which is present during life. Iman emphasizes inward conviction and confession, which is appropriate at death since actions cease. The passage ends with a note on the definition of Iman: some say it requires both internal affirmation and verbal confession, while others say affirmation alone suffices for salvation, with confession being only a condition for worldly legal rulings.

Key Terms
الاسلام (al-Islam): Outward submission and compliance with commands, emphasizing action.
الايمان (al-Iman): Internal affirmation (tasdiq) of the heart, and verbal confession (iqrar).
شفاعة (shafa'ah): Intercession on behalf of the deceased, accepted by Allah.

Key Takeaway
The funeral du'a is a sunnah that beautifully distinguishes Islam (action in life) from Iman (conviction at death).

The Imam's Standing Position in Funeral Prayer
Ruling on the imam's standing position in janazah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for validity of janazah prayer alignment and explain the recommended standing position for the imam, including the intra-Hanafi difference between the general view and Abu Hanifa's narration.

Core Idea
Alignment of any part is a condition; standing at the chest is recommended, and Abu Hanifa differentiates between men and women.

This lesson clarifies the imam's position relative to the deceased in the janazah prayer. The text first establishes that alignment of any part of the deceased with the worshipper is a condition for the prayer's validity. Then it discusses the recommended position—standing by the chest—and notes a narration from Abu Hanifa that distinguishes between a male (head) and a female (middle/chest) deceased. We will examine the proof and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for validity
Read the first part: 'alignment of a part of the deceased with the one praying is a condition for the validity of the prayer.' Note that any part suffices.
This is a shart, not a rukn.
2
Identify the recommended position
The text states: 'Standing parallel to the chest is recommended for both man and woman.' This is the general view. The wisdom given is that the chest is the seat of faith and the prayer is intercession.
Mandub is synonymous with sunnah in Hanafi terminology.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
The text reports a narration from Abu Hanifa: the imam stands at the head of a male and at the middle (chest) of a female. This differs from the general view that the chest applies to both.
This is an ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
4
Examine the dalil
Two hadith are cited: (1) Anas ibn Malik stood at the head of a man. (2) The Prophet ﷺ stood at the middle of a woman, interpreted as the chest. These support Abu Hanifa's view.
The hadith are ahad, so they indicate recommendation, not obligation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Hidayah and other works prefer the narration from Abu Hanifa. Thus the relied-upon position is to stand at the head for a man and at the chest for a woman, while still satisfying the condition of alignment.
The general view (chest for both) is also valid but less preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقوم المصلِّي بحذاء صَدْرِ الميت اعلم أنّ محاذاة جزء من أجزاء الميت للمصلي شرط لصحة الصَّلاة، والقيام بحذاء الصدر للرَّجل والمرأة كليهما مندوب، وعللوه بأنـه محـل الإيمان ، فيناسب القيام بمحاذاته للصَّلاة التي هي شفاعة له، وذكر في «الهداية» وغيرها : أنه رُوي عن أبي حنيفة له أنه يقومُ عند رأس الرجل وبحذاء وسط المرأة، وبه ورد الحديث. فعن أبي غالب قال: صليت مع أنس بن مالك على جنازة رجل فقام حيال رأسه. وعن سمرة بن جندب: إن النبي صلى على امرأة فقام وسطها. والوسط هو الصدر.
And the one praying stands parallel to the chest of the deceased. Know that alignment of a part of the deceased with the one praying is a condition for the validity of the prayer. Standing parallel to the chest is recommended for both man and woman. They explained it because it is the seat of faith, so it is appropriate to stand parallel to it for the prayer which is intercession for him. And it is mentioned in al-Hidayah and others that it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he stands at the head of the man and parallel to the middle of the woman, and the hadith came accordingly. For from Abu Ghallib: I prayed with Anas ibn Malik over the funeral of a man and he stood opposite his head. And from Samura ibn Jundub: The Prophet ﷺ prayed over a woman and stood at her middle, and the middle is the chest.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage addresses the proper positioning of the imam relative to the deceased during the janazah prayer. The author first states the ruling: the one praying stands by the chest of the deceased. He clarifies that actually having any part of the body aligned is a condition for validity, but standing by the chest is recommended (mandub). The wisdom behind this is that the chest is the seat of faith (iman), and the janazah prayer is a form of intercession for the deceased, so it is fitting to face the locus of faith. The author then notes a narration from Abu Hanifa that the imam stands at the head of a male deceased and at the middle of a female deceased. This is supported by hadith: Anas ibn Malik stood at the head of a man, and the Prophet ﷺ stood at the middle of a woman, which is interpreted as the chest (since the middle of the body is around the chest). The passage thus shows that the recommended position is debated: the general view considers the chest for both, while a specific narration differentiates between men and women. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to al-Hidayah is the latter: at the head for men and middle for women.

Key Terms
محاذاة (muhadhaat): Alignment; the condition that a part of the deceased's body be directly in front of the person praying.
مندوب (mandub): Recommended; an action that is commendable but not obligatory.
وسط (wasat): Middle; interpreted here as the chest area of the body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The condition for janazah prayer validity is alignment of any part; the imam's standing at the chest is recommended, and the mufta bihi position differentiates between male (head) and female (chest).

6 min
Position of the Imam in Funeral Prayer
Ruling and rationale for imam's position relative to deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (mandub) position of the imam in Hanafi funeral prayer and explain the rationale, the condition of alignment, and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Stand by the chest – it is the seat of faith and the best intercession.

In the funeral prayer, the imam's position relative to the deceased is a detail that reflects deep wisdom. The dua's wording changes from 'Islam' to 'Iman' based on life and death, and the imam's placement by the chest honors the heart as the locus of faith. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence, and the reasoning behind the preferred position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the position of the imam in the janazah prayer. Identify the hukm: alignment of any part is a condition (shart), and standing by the chest is recommended (mandub/sunnah).
Distinguish between condition (shart) and recommended (sunnah).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith from Samura ibn Jundub that the Prophet stood at the 'middle' (wasat) of a woman's funeral. This is a sunnah ahad hadith.
Hadith is in Sunan al-Tirmidhi and Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the recommended position? The word 'wasat' is interpreted by Hanafi scholars as the chest area, since the chest is between the upper and lower body.
The interpretation is key to reconciling with Abu Hanifa's view.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
What is the intra-Hanafi difference? Abu Hanifa is reported to say stand at the head for a man and at the middle for a woman. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is chest for both.
The ikhtilaf is over the exact meaning of 'wasat'.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Why does the chest position become the relied-upon view? Because 'wasat' is understood as the chest, which is the locus of faith (iman), making it more appropriate for intercessory prayer.
The tarjih authority includes later commentators like Al-Hidayah.

كتاب الصلاة باب الجنائز ويقوم المصلِّي بحذاء صَدْرِ الميت وإنما قال في الأَوَّل الإسلام، وفي الثَّاني الإيمان ; لأنَّ الإسلام والإيمان وإن كانا متحدين، فالإسلامُ يُنبيُّ عن الانقياد فكأنه دعاء في حال الحياة بالإيمان والإنقياد ، وأما عند الوفاة فقد دعا بالتّوفّي على الإيمان، وهو التصديق ، والإقرار، وأمَّا الإنقياد وهو العمل فغير موجود في حال الوفاة وبعده. [٢] ( ويقوم المصلي بحذاء صَدْر الميت الإسلام يشعر عن الانقياد كما يفيد قوله : قَالَتِ الْأَعْرَابُ وَامَنَّا قُل لَّمْ تُؤْمِنُوا وَلَكِن قُولُوا أَسْلَمْنَا (١) ، وقوله في حكاية سيدنا إبراهيم : أَسْلَمْتُ لِرَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ (۲) ، وهو بالعمل بالجوارح، وهو إنّما يوجد في حالة الحياة فلذا دعي حالة الحياة، وأما حالة الموتِ فالانقياد مفقود فلذا ذكر لفظ الإيمان. [1] قوله : وهو التصديق والإقرار ; يعني التصديق بالجنان بالتوحيد والرسالة وما جاء به الرسول ، والإقرار بذلك باللسان، وهذا عند البعض، وعند البعض الإيمان المنجي : هو التصديقُ فقط، والإقرار شرط لإجزاء أحكام الدُّنيا، وتحقيقه في كتب علم الكلام. [٢]قوله : ويقوم ; اعلم أنّ محاذاة جزء من أجزاء الميت للمصلي شرط لصحة الصَّلاة، والقيام بحذاء الصدر للرَّجل والمرأة كليهما مندوب (۳)، وعللوه بأنـه محـل الإيمان ، فيناسب القيام بمحاذاته للصَّلاة التي هي شفاعة له، وذكر في «الهداية» وغيرها : أنه رُوي عن أبي حنيفة له أنه يقومُ عند رأس الرجل وبحذاء وسط المرأة، وبه ورد الحديث. وعن سمرة بن جندب له : إن النبي صلى على امرأة فقام وسطها» في «سنن الترمذي»(۳) : ٣٥٣)، وصححه، و صحيح البخاري (۱) : (۱۲۵) ، وغيرها، والوسط هو الصدر، فإن فوقه يديه ورأسه وتحته بطنه ورجليه. ينظر : ((التبيين»(١ : ٢٤٢)، وغيرها.
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Funerals. And the one praying stands parallel to the chest of the deceased. He only said in the first [dua] 'Islam' and in the second 'Iman' because Islam and Iman, though similar, Islam indicates submission; so it is like a supplication during life for faith and submission. At death, he supplicates for dying upon Iman, which is affirmation and confession. Submission, which is action, is not present at death or after. [2] 'And the one praying stands parallel to the chest of the deceased': Islam indicates submission, as evidenced by His saying: 'The Bedouins said, 'We believe.' Say, 'You have not believed, but say, 'We have submitted'' (49:14), and His saying in the story of Ibrahim: 'I have submitted to the Lord of the worlds' (2:131). And it is action with the limbs, which only exists during life, so it is called the state of life. At death, submission is absent, so the word Iman is mentioned. [1] His saying: 'It is affirmation and confession': meaning affirmation in the heart of Tawhid, prophethood, and what the Messenger brought, and confession of that with the tongue. This is according to some; according to others, saving faith is only affirmation, and confession is a condition for implementing worldly rulings. Its verification is in books of theology. [2] His saying: 'And he stands': Know that alignment of a part of the deceased with the one praying is a condition for the validity of the prayer. Standing parallel to the chest for both man and woman is recommended (mandub). They reasoned it because it is the locus of faith, so standing parallel to it is appropriate for the prayer, which is intercession for him. It is mentioned in Al-Hidayah and others that it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he stands at the head of a man and parallel to the middle of a woman, and the hadith has come with that. And from Samura ibn Jundub that the Prophet prayed over a woman and stood at her middle – in Sunan al-Tirmidhi and he authenticated it, and Sahih al-Bukhari, etc. And 'middle' is the chest, for above it are his hands and head, and below it his stomach and legs. See Al-Tabyin, etc.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of the position of the imam in funeral prayer. The author first explains why the duas use 'Islam' in the first takbir and 'Iman' in the second: Islam connotes outward submission (actions), which is present during life, while Iman is inner belief and confession, which is what one truly needs at death. Then the ruling on the imam's position: the condition for validity is that some part of the deceased be parallel to the imam. The recommended (mandub) position is to stand by the chest for both men and women, because the chest is the seat of faith, and the prayer is intercession. However, a narration from Abu Hanifa states he stands at the head of a man and at the middle (chest) of a woman, and this is supported by hadith. The author reconciles by noting that 'middle' equals chest. The key point is that the imam should align with the chest area, as that is the locus of faith, making the intercession more fitting.

Key Terms
الإيمان (al-īmān): Belief in the heart (tasdiq) and confession by the tongue (iqrar); according to some, tasdiq alone is core, iqrar is for worldly application.
الإسلام (al-islām): Outward submission (inqiyad) through actions of the limbs, based on Quran 49:14 and 2:131.
محاذاة (muḥādhāt): Alignment of the imam with a part of the deceased; a condition (shart) for validity of funeral prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi funeral prayer, where is the recommended (mandub) position for the imam to stand?
A) At the head of the deceased regardless of gender
B) By the chest of the deceased for both men and women
C) At the center of the body for men and at the head for women
D) At the feet of the deceased

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi funeral prayer, the imam should stand by the chest of the deceased for both men and women, as it is the seat of faith and the best intercession.

Order of Precedence for Leading Funeral Prayer (Hanafi)
Order of precedence for imamate in funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchical order of who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer and explain why the sultan and qadi precede the wali.

Core Idea
The ruler and judge take precedence over the deceased's guardian due to their general authority.

The funeral prayer is a collective obligation, but who should lead it? The Hanafi school establishes a clear hierarchy based on authority. The ruler (sultan) represents the Prophet, the judge (qadi) has general authority, and the guardian (wali) comes last. This lesson unpacks that order and the conditions for its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
Read the text to list: sultan, qadi, imam of district, wali (in order of 'asaba).
This is the core ruling.
2
Understand the sultan's priority
The sultan is first because he stands in place of the Prophet, who has authority over believers by Quranic text.
Dalil: Quran 33:6.
3
Distinguish the qadi and imam
The qadi has general authority; the imam of district is preferred over the wali only if more virtuous, otherwise the wali comes first.
Imam's preference is mandub, wali's right is wajib.
4
Explain the wali's right and its consequences
The wali can permit another to lead, and if someone else leads without permission, the wali may repeat the prayer.
The wali's right is enforceable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳] [٤] عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية (۲) والأحق بالإمامة السلطان ، ثُمَّ القاضي، ثُمَّ إمام الحي، ثم الولي على ترتيب العصبات، ولا بأس بإذنِهِ في الإمامة، فإن صلى غيرهم يعيد الولي إن شاء، ولا يصلي غيره بعده والأحق بالإمامة السلطان ، ثُمَّ القاضي، ثُمَّ إمام الحي، ثُمَّ الولي" على ترتيب العصبات، ولا بأس بإذنِهِ في الإمامة ، فإن صلى غيرهم يعيد الولي إن شاء، ولا يصلي غيره بعده فقد صح عن أنس : أنه صلى على جنازةِ الرَّجل والمرأة فقام بحذاء الرأس في الأول، وبحذاء العجيزة ووسط السَّرِيرِ في الثَّاني ، وقال : هكذا كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يفعل ) ، أخرجه أبو داود والترمذي وابن ماجة وغيرهم. (1) [١]قوله : والأحق ; يعني أنَّ الأحق بالإمامة في صلاة الجنازة السلطان إن حضر ; لأنه قائم مقام النبي ، والنبي أولى بالمؤمنين من أنفسهم بنص القرآن، فإن لم يحضر فالقاضي ; لأنه صاحب ولاية عامة، فإن لم يحضر فإمام المحلة في الصلوات الخمس (٢) ، وتقديمه على الولي مندوب بشرط أن يكون أفضل من الولي، وإلا فالأولى هو الوليّ، وأما تقديم الولاة فواجب. كذا في «المجتبى» وغيره. (۲) قوله : ثم الولي ; أي ولي الميت وقريبه على ترتيب العصبات، فيقدم الأقرب على الأبعد، ولا ولاية لامرأة أو صبي أو معتوه ونحوه ذلك، والأب يقدم على الابن ; لكونه أسن على الأصح. كذا في «البحر» (۳). [۳] قوله : بإذنه ; أي إذا أذنَ الوليُّ لغيره بالصَّلاة يوْمُ ذلك المأذونُ له ; لأنَّ الحق للولي فله إسقاطه. [٤] قوله : فإن صلى ; أي إن صلى غير مَن ذُكِر ممن ليس له حقُّ التَّقديم ولم يتابعه الولي أعاد الصَّلاةَ إن شاء ; لأنَّ الحقِّ كان له ، وأما إذا صَلَّى الولي فلا يجوز
[3] [4] 'Umda al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya. (2) And the most entitled to lead [in funeral prayer] is the sultan, then the qadi, then the imam of the district, then the wali in the order of 'asaba. There is no harm in his permission [for another] to lead. If someone other than them prays, the wali may repeat the prayer if he wishes, and no one else may pray after him. And the most entitled to lead is the sultan, then the qadi, then the imam of the district, then the wali in the order of 'asaba. There is no harm in his permission for leadership. If someone other than them prays, the wali may repeat the prayer if he wishes, and no one else may pray after him. It is authentically reported from Anas that he prayed over the funeral of a man and a woman, so he stood parallel to the head for the first, and parallel to the buttocks and middle of the bier for the second, and said: 'Thus the Messenger of Allah used to do.' Reported by Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and others. (1) [1] His saying: 'the most entitled': It means that the most entitled to lead in funeral prayer is the sultan if present, because he stands in the place of the Prophet, and the Prophet is more entitled to the believers than themselves by Quranic text. If he is not present, then the qadi, because he has general authority. If he is not present, then the imam of the district in the five daily prayers. His preference over the wali is recommended (mandub) on condition that he is more virtuous than the wali; otherwise the wali is more appropriate. As for preferring the awliya' (guardians), it is obligatory. This is stated in al-Mujtaba and others. (2) His saying: 'then the wali': meaning the wali of the deceased and his relative according to the order of 'asaba, so the closer is preferred over the farther. There is no authority for a woman, a boy, an insane person, etc. The father is preferred over the son because he is older, according to the most correct view. This is stated in al-Bahr. (3) [3] His saying: 'with his permission': meaning if the wali permits another to pray, that permitted person may lead, because the right belongs to the wali, so he may drop it. [4] His saying: 'if he prays': meaning if someone other than those mentioned, who has no right of precedence, prays and the wali does not follow him, the wali may repeat the prayer if he wishes, because the right was his. But if the wali prays, no one else may do so after him.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage establishes the hierarchical order of who has the primary right (ahqaq) to lead the funeral prayer. The order is: (1) the sultan (ruler), (2) the qadi (judge), (3) the imam of the district (who leads the five daily prayers), and (4) the wali (guardian/relative) according to the order of 'asaba (agnatic heirs). The sultan has priority because he represents the Prophet; the qadi has general authority; the imam of the district is preferred over the wali only if he is more virtuous, otherwise the wali comes first. The wali's right is such that if he permits another to lead, it is valid because he can waive his right. If someone without the right leads and the wali does not follow, the wali may repeat the prayer. If the wali leads, no one else may lead after him. The hadith of Anas shows the Prophet's practice of standing at the head for a man and at the buttocks/middle for a woman, but this is not the main topic here; it is cited as a proof for the permissibility of different positions, though the commentary focuses on imamate.

Key Terms
الولي (al-walī): The guardian of the deceased, usually a relative according to 'asaba order, who has the primary right to lead the funeral prayer.
العصبات (al-'aṣabāt): Agnatic heirs (male relatives through the male line) in order of closeness: e.g., son, then father, then brother, etc.
الأحق بالإمامة (al-aḥaqq bil-imāma): The person with the primary right to lead the funeral prayer based on authority or guardianship.
المندوب (al-mandūb): Recommended; the preference of the imam of district over the wali is mandub (not obligatory).
الواجب (al-wājib): Obligatory; the right of the wali to lead is considered wajib (necessary).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who has the greatest right to lead the funeral prayer if the sultan, qadi, imam of the district, and wali are all present?
A) The wali
B) The imam of the district
C) The sultan
D) The qadi

Key Takeaway
The ruler and judge take precedence over the deceased's guardian in leading funeral prayer due to their general authority.

Most Entitled to Lead Funeral Prayer and Sunnah Positioning
Ruling on imamah priority and sunnah standing position

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer and explain the sunnah standing position for the imam.

Core Idea
The ruler leads as the Prophet's deputy; the sunnah position differs for men and women.

This lesson establishes the mandatory order of leadership in funeral prayer, beginning with the ruler and descending through the judge and local imam to the guardian. It also details the sunnah practice of the imam's standing position based on the hadith of Anas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hierarchy
State the order: ruler, judge, local imam, guardian. Note the basis for each priority.
The guardian's order follows agnate inheritance.
2
Understand the legal basis
Analyze why the ruler is first (Quranic authority), judge (general authority), and imam (only if more virtuous than guardian).
Precedence of these authorities is wajib.
3
Analyze the guardian's role
The guardian holds the right to lead but can delegate or repeat the prayer if another leads without permission.
Permission valid; repetition allowed only if guardian did not follow.
4
Examine the proof for standing position
Review the hadith of Anas: imam stands at the head for a man and at the hips/middle for a woman.
This is a sunnah from prophetic practice.
5
Apply the ruling
Recognize the obligatory nature of the hierarchy and sunnah of standing, and ensure correct practice.
Ignoring the hierarchy invalidates the priority but not the prayer itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأحق بالإمامة السلطان، ثم القاضي، ثم إمام الحي، ثم الولي على ترتيب العصبات، ولا بأس بإذنه في الإمامة، فإن صلى غيرهم يعيد الولي إن شاء، ولا يصلي غيره بعده فقد صح عن أنس : أنه صلى على جنازة الرجل والمرأة فقام بحذاء الرأس في الأول، وبحذاء العجيزة ووسط السرير في الثاني، وقال : هكذا كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يفعل ) ، أخرجه أبو داود والترمذي وابن ماجة وغيرهم.

[1] قوله : والأحق؛ يعني أن الأحق بالإمامة في صلاة الجنازة السلطان إن حضر؛ لأنه قائم مقام النبي، والنبي أولى بالمؤمنين من أنفسهم بنص القرآن، فإن لم يحضر فالقاضي؛ لأنه صاحب ولاية عامة، فإن لم يحضر فإمام المحلة في الصلوات الخمس، وتقديمه على الولي مندوب بشرط أن يكون أفضل من الولي، وإلا فالأولى هو الوليّ، وأما تقديم الولاة فواجب. كذا في «المجتبى» وغيره.

[2] قوله : ثم الولي؛ أي ولي الميت وقريبه على ترتيب العصبات، فيقدم الأقرب على الأبعد، ولا ولاية لامرأة أو صبي أو معتوه ونحوه ذلك، والأب يقدم على الابن؛ لكونه أسن على الأصح. كذا في «البحر».

[3] قوله : بإذنه؛ أي إذا أذن الولي لغيره بالصلاة صوم ذلك المأذون له؛ لأن الحق للولي فله إسقاطه.

[4] قوله : فإن صلى؛ أي إن صلى غير من ذكر ممن ليس له حق التقديم ولم يتابعه الولي أعاد الصلاة إن شاء؛ لأن الحق كان له، وأما إذا صلى الولي فلا يجوز
And the most entitled to lead is the ruler, then the judge, then the imam of the locality, then the guardian according to the order of agnates. There is no harm in his permission regarding leading. If someone other than them prays, the guardian may repeat if he wishes, and no one else prays after him. It has been authentically reported from Anas that he prayed over the funeral of a man and a woman, so he stood opposite the head for the first and opposite the buttocks and middle of the bier for the second, and said, 'Thus did the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, do.' It was recorded by Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and others.

[1] His statement: 'And the most entitled' means that the most entitled to lead in the funeral prayer is the ruler if present, because he stands in the place of the Prophet, and the Prophet is more entitled to the believers than themselves by the text of the Quran. If he is not present, then the judge because he has general authority. If he is not present, then the imam of the locality in the five prayers, and giving him precedence over the guardian is recommended provided he is better than the guardian, otherwise the guardian is more proper. As for giving precedence to those with authority (the mentioned ones), it is obligatory. So in al-Mujtaba and others.

[2] His statement: 'Then the guardian' means the guardian of the deceased and his relative according to the order of agnates, so the closer is given precedence over the farther. There is no guardianship for a woman, a child, an insane person, or the like. The father is given precedence over the son because he is older according to the most correct view. So in al-Bahr.

[3] His statement: 'by his permission' means that if the guardian permits someone else to pray, that one should be prayed upon (the deceased) because the right belongs to the guardian and he may drop it.

[4] His statement: 'Then if he prays' means if someone other than those mentioned who have no right of precedence prays and the guardian does not follow him, he may repeat the prayer if he wishes because the right belonged to him. But if the guardian prays himself, it is not permissible (for someone else to pray afterward).
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the hadith. It first establishes the hierarchy of who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer: the ruler (sultan), then the judge, then the imam of the locality, then the guardian of the deceased in the order of agnate inheritance. The commentary explains that the ruler is prioritized because he represents the Prophet, and the Prophet is more entitled to the believers as per Quranic text. If the ruler is absent, the judge takes precedence due to his general authority. The imam of the locality is preferred over the guardian only if he is more virtuous; otherwise, the guardian is better. The commentary emphasizes that giving precedence to these authorities (rulers, judges, etc.) is obligatory. The guardian’s permission for another to lead is valid because the right is his to delegate. If someone else leads without permission, the guardian may repeat the prayer if he wishes. The hadith of Anas is then cited as proof for the sunnah position of the imam: standing at the head for a man and at the hips/middle of the bier for a woman. This ruling is based on the practice of the Prophet, recorded in major hadith collections.

Key Terms
الولي (al-wali): The guardian of the deceased, usually a close male relative, who has the primary right to lead or authorize the funeral prayer.
السلطان (al-sultan): The political ruler or head of state, given precedence in leading funeral prayer due to representing the Prophet's authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The father of the deceased
B) The judge
C) The imam of the locality
D) The oldest son

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates strict precedence in funeral leadership (ruler, judge, imam, guardian) and prescribes a sunnah standing position based on the gender of the deceased.

Prayer over Grave and Prohibition of Prayer While Riding
Ruling on praying over grave and prohibition of praying while riding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on praying over a grave after burial and praying the funeral prayer while riding, and explain how istihsan overrides qiyas in the latter case.

Core Idea
Prayer over a grave is permitted before decomposition; prayer while riding is prohibited by istihsan despite qiyas.

In this passage from al-Hidayah and its glosses, we examine two scenarios related to the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The first deals with praying over the grave of a person who was buried without being prayed upon. The second addresses whether one may perform this prayer while riding an animal. Both rulings rely on the Hanafi principle of istihsan (juristic preference) to set aside the apparent analogy (qiyas jali). By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply these rulings and understand the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
Separate the issue of praying over the grave from the issue of praying while riding. Note that both cases involve the funeral prayer, but the context (time/place) and the manner (standing vs. riding) differ.
2
Apply the apparent analogy (qiyas jali)
A superficial analogy would permit both because the funeral prayer lacks bowing and prostration, thus it is considered mere supplication (dua). Under this view, no standing is required, so riding would be acceptable.
Qiyas jali: what first comes to mind.
3
Identify the istihsan and its basis
For grave prayer, a specific hadith (the Prophet prayed over a grave after a month) overrides qiyas. For prayer on a ride, the presence of takbir (tahrima), taslim, conditions of purity, and facing qibla make it akin to a regular prayer; hence istihsan requires standing and prohibits riding.
Istihsan is a stronger evidence (hadith, necessity) or a more relevant analogy.
4
Note the precondition for grave prayer
The grave prayer is only valid if the body has not begun to decompose. The estimation of three days (from Abu Yusuf) is not fixed; the correct view is to rely on expert opinion (ijtihad) due to variations in climate and the deceased's condition.
Decomposition (tafaskh) prevents validity.
5
Conclude the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
The Hanafi school holds: (1) Grave prayer is permissible before decomposition, and the period is determined by ijtihad. (2) Prayer while riding is not permissible; one must dismount and stand. These positions are based on zahir al-riwayah and confirmed by later authorities like Ibn al-Humann.
Zahir al-riwayah: the six core books of Imam Muhammad.

كتاب الصلاة باب الجنائز

ومن لم يصل عليه، فدفن صلي على قبره ما لم يظن أنه تفسخ، وقد قدر بثلاثة أيام، ولم يجز راكباً استحسانا، الاستحسان : هو الدليل الذي يكون في مقابلة القياس الذي يسبق إليه الأفهام، فالقياس هاهنا أن يجوز راكباً؛ لأنه ليس بصلاة؛ لعدم الأركان، بل هو دعاء، والاستحسان أنها هي صلاة من وجه؛ لوجود التحريمة، فلا يترك القيام من غير عذر احتياطاً لغيره أن يصلي ثانياً؛ لأن الفرض قد تأدى بأداء صاحب الحق، والتنفل بهذه الصلاة غير مشروع عندنا. كما في «الهداية»، وحواشيها.

[0]
سُنَّةً

[1] قوله : على قبره؛ نقل عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الصلاة على القبر في أحاديث مخرجة في الصحاح، وفي بعضها: «أنه صلى بعد شهر».

[2] قوله : وقد قدر؛ هذا التقدير مروي عن أبي يوسف، والصحيح إحالة ذلك إلى أكبر الرأي؛ لاختلاف مدة التفسخ باختلاف حال الميت في السمن والهزال، واختلاف الزمان والمكان. كذا في «البناية».

[3] قوله : هو الدليل؛ سواء كان ذلك قياساً أو سنة أو آية أو إجماعاً، وبه يعلم أن الاستحسان ليس بخارج عن الأدلة الأربعة، وما يلحق بهما، وتفصيله في كتب الأصول.

[4] قوله : لعدم الأركان؛ كالركوع والسجود والجلوس.

[5] قوله : لوجود التحريمة؛ ولوجود السلام واشتراط الطهارة واستقبال القبلة ونحوهما لها مما يشترط للصلوات، ولذا أطلق عليها لفظ : الصلاة؛ إطلاقاً شائعاً.

[6] قوله : احتياطاً؛ أي للاحتياط، فإن القيام فرض في الفرائض لا يترك من غير عذر.
Book of Prayer – Chapter of Funerals

And whoever has not prayed over him, and he is buried, he is prayed over his grave as long as it is not thought that he has decomposed – and it has been estimated at three days – and it is not permissible while riding by way of istihsan. Istihsan is the evidence that is in opposition to the analogy that first comes to minds. So the analogy here is that it is permissible while riding because it is not a prayer due to the lack of essential components, but rather it is supplication. And the istihsan is that it is indeed a prayer in some respects due to the presence of the takbir (tahrima), so one should not leave standing without an excuse as a precaution lest someone else should pray a second time, because the obligation has been fulfilled by the one who has the right, and performing a supererogatory act with this prayer is not legislated according to us. As in al-Hidayah and its glosses.

[0]
Sunnah.

[1] His statement: 'over his grave' – It is narrated from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, praying over the grave in hadiths recorded in the Sahih collections, and in some of them: 'He prayed after a month.'

[2] His statement: 'and it has been estimated' – This estimation is narrated from Abu Yusuf, and the correct view is to refer that to the better opinion because the period of decomposition differs according to the condition of the deceased in terms of obesity and emaciation, and variation of time and place. As in al-Binaya.

[3] His statement: 'it is the evidence' – Whether that is an analogy, a sunnah, a verse, or a consensus, and by this it is known that istihsan is not outside the four evidences and what is attached to them. Its detail is in the books of usul.

[4] His statement: 'due to the lack of essential components' – Such as bowing, prostration, and sitting.

[5] His statement: 'due to the presence of the tahrima' – And due to the presence of the taslim, the condition of purity, facing the qiblah, and similar things that are required for prayers, and therefore the term 'prayer' is applied to it commonly.

[6] His statement: 'as a precaution' – meaning for precaution, because standing is obligatory in obligatory prayers and not left without a valid excuse.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from istihsan and hadith. It addresses two issues: (1) Praying over the grave after burial – if someone died and was not prayed upon before burial, it is permissible to pray at the grave as long as the body is not thought to have started decomposing. The timeframe is estimated at three days according to Abu Yusuf, but the correct view is to rely on expert opinion since decomposition varies. This is supported by hadith of the Prophet praying over a grave after a month. (2) Praying while riding – the apparent analogy (qiyas jali) would permit it because the funeral prayer without bowing and prostration is essentially supplication (dua). However, istihsan (juristic preference) rules that it is not permissible while riding because the funeral prayer has aspects of a regular prayer: it includes the opening takbir (tahrima), concluding salutation (taslim), conditions of purity and facing the qiblah. Therefore, it is treated like a prayer, and standing is obligatory unless there is a valid excuse. The commentary emphasizes that the precaution is taken to avoid someone else repeating the prayer, since the obligation is fulfilled by the one with the right to lead, and performing another funeral prayer voluntarily is not legislated in the Hanafi school. The passage clarifies that istihsan is a legitimate source of law within the four primary sources.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A juristic preference that sets aside a clear analogy (qiyas jali) in favor of a stronger evidence (such as sunnah, consensus, or necessity).
التفسخ (al-tafaskh): Decomposition of the body after burial, which prevents prayer over the grave due to impurity and change.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the reason for preferring istihsan over qiyas in the case of praying on a ride?
A) Because the prayer lacks bowing and prostration
B) Because the prayer includes the opening takbir and other prayer conditions
C) Because the Prophet never prayed on a ride
D) Because it is always better to stand while praying

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits prayer over the grave before decomposition but prohibits praying while riding, using istihsan to prioritize the prayer-like elements over the lack of physical pillars.

Funeral Prayer on the Grave and While Riding (Istihsan)
Commentary on ruling and istihsan definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer over a grave and while riding, and explain how istihsan overrides the apparent qiyas.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas when a stronger consideration (like prayer attributes) demands standing.

This lesson examines two related rulings: (1) prayer over the grave of a deceased person if the funeral prayer was missed, and (2) the prohibition of performing that prayer while riding. The key is understanding how istihsan, a distinctive Hanafi proof, outweighs the apparent analogy that would allow riding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is the funeral prayer over a buried person. The default ruling (istihsan-driven) is that it is permissible before decomposition, but not while riding.
The passage clarifies that the prayer is not a formal prayer with pillars, yet it shares enough attributes to require standing.
2
Understand the apparent qiyas (qiyas jaliy)
Apparent qiyas would analogize the funeral prayer to a mere supplication (since it lacks bowing, prostration, etc.) and thus permit riding.
This is the weaker analogy that first comes to mind.
3
Analyze the istihsan argument
Istihsan argues that the funeral prayer, though not a full prayer, includes elements of prayer (takbir, salutation, facing qibla, purity) and is therefore treated like a prayer. Thus, riding is impermissible.
The presence of the opening takbir (tahrimah) is the key attribute linking it to formal prayer.
4
Examine the intra-madhhab difference on timing
Abu Yusuf estimated three days before decomposition, but the correct view relies on the imam's judgment based on the deceased's condition and environment.
This shows the Hanafi methodology of preferring ijtihad over a fixed numerical estimation.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
In contemporary practice, if a burial occurs without the funeral prayer, one may pray at the grave as long as the body is not decomposed. Riding a vehicle to the grave is not allowed unless there is a valid excuse (e.g., disability).
The precaution ensures the prayer is performed properly and others may repeat if needed.

ومن لم يصلّ عليه ، فَدُفِنَ صُلِّي على قبره ما لم يظن أنه تفسخ ولم يجز راكباً
