The Book of Prayer, Chapter of Funerals. And whoever does not pray over him, and he is buried, prayer is performed over his grave as long as it is not thought that he has decomposed, and it is not permissible while riding, by istihsan. And whoever does not pray over him, and he is buried, prayer is performed over his grave as long as it is not thought that he has decomposed, and it has been estimated at three days, and it is not permissible while riding by istihsan. Istihsan: it is the evidence that is in opposition to the analogy that first comes to minds. So the analogy here is that it is permissible while riding, because it is not a prayer due to the lack of pillars, rather it is a supplication, and istihsan is that it is a prayer in one respect due to the presence of the opening takbir, so standing is not abandoned without an excuse out of precaution so that another may pray a second time, because the obligation has already been fulfilled by the performance of the one entitled, and performing this prayer as a supererogatory act is not legislated according to us, as in Al-Hidayah and its glosses. [0] [1] His statement: 'over his grave'; it is narrated from the Messenger of Allah (صلى الله عليه وسلم) the prayer over the grave in hadiths extracted in the Sahihs, and in some of them: 'He prayed after a month.' [2] His statement: 'and it has been estimated'; this estimation is narrated from Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), and the correct view is to refer that to the greater opinion due to the differing period of decomposition according to the condition of the deceased in fatness and thinness, and the difference of time and place. This is in Al-Binayah. [3] His statement: 'it is the evidence'; whether that evidence is a qiyas or a sunnah or a verse or consensus, and by it it is known that istihsan is not outside the four evidences and what is attached to them, and its detail is in the books of usul. [4] His statement: 'due to the lack of pillars'; like bowing, prostration, and sitting. [5] His statement: 'due to the presence of the opening takbir'; and due to the presence of the salutation and the condition of purification and facing the qibla and the like for it which are required for prayers, and therefore the word 'prayer' is applied to it frequently. [6] His statement: 'out of precaution'; meaning for precaution, for standing is obligatory in obligatory prayers and is not abandoned without an excuse.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn from Al-Wiqayah. It addresses two rulings: (1) If a person dies without the funeral prayer being performed and is buried, it is permissible to pray over his grave as long as there is no assumption that the body has decomposed. The timeframe is estimated at three days, but the correct view is that it depends on the circumstances (body fat, weather, etc.) as stated by Abu Yusuf. (2) Performing this prayer while riding is not permissible according to istihsan, even though qiyas (analogy) would allow it. The analogy would be that it is not a formal prayer (since it lacks pillars like bowing and prostration) but rather a supplication, so riding should be allowed. However, istihsan overrides this because the prayer has some attributes of prayer, such as the opening takbir (tahrimah), salutation, facing qibla, and purity. Therefore, to avoid missing a required element (standing), one must not ride unless there is an excuse. This precaution ensures that others can pray a second time if needed, as the obligation has been fulfilled by the first prayer. The commentator clarifies that istihsan is not a source outside the four primary evidences; it can be based on qiyas, sunnah, Quran, or ijma. The definition of istihsan given here is 'the evidence that opposes the apparent qiyas' (i.e., the qiyas jaliy). The passage also notes that performing this prayer as a supererogatory act is not allowed in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): An evidence that opposes the apparent qiyas (qiyas jaliy) in preference of a stronger consideration; here it overrides the analogy that would allow riding.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer; its presence makes the janazah prayer analogous to formal prayer.
تفسخ (tafassukh): Decomposition of the body after burial; prayer over grave is valid only before decomposition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it impermissible (lā yajūz) to perform the funeral prayer on a grave while riding, even though the apparent analogy (qiyas jaliy) would allow it?
A) Because riding is haram in all prayers.
B) Because the prayer has the opening takbir (tahrimah) and other prayer attributes, so it is treated like a formal prayer.
C) Because the grave is impure.
D) Because the imam must stand for the congregation.

Key Takeaway
Istihsan overrides apparent qiyas when the act shares key features of a formal prayer, requiring standing and prohibiting riding unless excused.

Karahah of Funeral Prayer in the Mosque and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary on the ruling of funeral prayer in a mosque with intra-Hanafi dispute on cause and degree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two causes for karahah of funeral prayer in a mosque according to Hanafi scholars and identify the dispute on its degree (tahrimi vs tanzihi).

Core Idea
The karahah of funeral prayer in the mosque hinges on two different causes: potential soiling or the mosque's exclusive purpose for five prayers.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on performing the funeral prayer in a congregational mosque. The text presents a dispute among Hanafi scholars about the cause (illa) for the disliked nature of this action, leading to differences in rules when the deceased is outside the mosque. Additionally, later scholars differ on whether the dislike is prohibitively strong (tahrimi) or merely light (tanzihi). We will explore the hadith evidence and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and base ruling
The act is performing the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) in a congregational mosque (masjid jama'ah). The base ruling from the matn is that it is disliked (makruh) if the deceased is inside the mosque. If the deceased is outside, scholars differ.
Note the distinction: the rule changes based on the deceased's location and the cause for karahah.
2
Two causes for karahah
Some scholars (first group) say the cause is the suspicion of soiling (talawwuth) the mosque with impurities from the deceased. If the deceased is outside, this suspicion is absent, so no karahah. Others (second group) say the mosque is built exclusively for the five daily prayers, so any other prayer, including janazah, is disliked regardless of the deceased's location.
This difference determines the ruling when the deceased is outside: first group says no karahah, second says karahah.
3
Evidence from hadith and practice
The primary evidence is the hadith: 'Whoever prays over a deceased in the mosque, nothing is for him' (no reward or possibly invalid prayer). The Prophet's habit was to go to the musalla, not pray janazah in the mosque. The incident of praying for Sahl and Suhayl in the mosque is taken as a specific case showing validity, not general permission.
The hadith’s chain is considered hasan by Ibn al-Qayyim. The practice of the Prophet supports karahah.
4
Dispute on the degree of karahah
Later scholars dispute whether the karahah is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked, close to haram) or tanzihi (lightly disliked). Qasim ibn Qutlubugha favored tahrimi; Ibn al-Humam preferred tanzihi. Most later scholars lean toward tahrimi.
The difference affects whether the act is sinful (tahrimi) or merely non-recommended (tanzihi).
5
Exceptions and operative ruling
The karahah only applies when there is no excuse. If there is a valid excuse (e.g., rain, or i'tikaf for someone already in the mosque), the karahah is removed. The more cautious view (tahrimi) is preferred, but the school allows the prayer in the mosque with an excuse.
This shows the practical application: in normal circumstances, avoid praying janazah in the mosque; but if unavoidable, it is valid (though preferably avoided).

Source Text

عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية
وكرهت في مسجد جماعة إن كان الميت فيه، وإن كان خارجه اختلف المشايخ
(وكرهت في مسجد جماعة " إن كان الميت فيه ، وإن كان خارجه اختلف المشايخ) اختلاف المشايخ بناءً على أنّ علةَ الكراهة عند البعض (۱) توهم تلويث المسجد، فإن كان الميت خارجه لا تكره عندهم، وعند البعض أن المسجد لم يبن إلا للصلوات الخمس، فالميتُ وإن كان خارجا يكره عندهم أيضاً.
[1] قوله : وكرهت ؛ قيل تحريماً، كما حققه قاسم بن قطلوبغا في رسالة مستقلة له، وإليه مال أكثر المتأخرين، وقيل : تنزيها، ورجّحه المحقق ابن الهمام في «الفتح» (۳)، وتلميذه ابن أمير حاج في «الحلبة» وغيرهما.
والأصل فيه حديث: «مَن صلى على ميِّتِ في المسجد فلا شيء له، أخرجه أبو داود وابن ماجه وابن أبي شَيْبَةَ وغيرهم، وقد تكلّم في سنده، لكن حققَ ابنُ القيم في «زاد المعاد) ، وغيره : أنَّ سنده حسن محتج به.
ويؤيده أنَّ النبي لم يكن من عادته الصلاة على الجنازة في مسجده مع شرفه، بل كان يخرج إلى المصلى، وقد ثبت عنه أنه صلى على سهل وسهيل في المسجد، أخرجه مسلم وغيره، وهو واقعةُ حال لا عموم له، ويحمل على بيان للأجزاء، وقد فصلنا ما يتعلق بهذا المقام في «التعليق الممجد) () ، وغيرُه، ثم الكراهة إنّما . عدم العذر، فإن كان فلا كراهة؛ كالمطر واعتكاف من له حقُّ التَّقدم. كذا في «الحلبة». [٢]قوله : مسجد الجماعة ؛ الذي تؤدى فيه الصَّلاة بالجماعة، واحترز به عن المسجد الذي بني لصلاة الجنائز. [٣]قوله : اختلاف المشايخ ... الخ ؛ يعني عللَ بعض المشايخ كراهة صلاة الجنازة في المسجدِ بأنَّ فيه توهم تلوّث المسجد؛ لاحتمال أن يخرج نجس من منافذ الميت ويقع في المسجد، وقد أمرنا بتنظيف المساجد وتجنيبها عما يوهم ذلك .
And it is disliked (to perform the funeral prayer) in a congregational mosque if the deceased is inside it, and if he is outside, the scholars differed. His statement: 'And it is disliked in a congregational mosque if the deceased is inside it, and if he is outside, the scholars differed.' The difference among the scholars is based on the fact that the cause of dislike according to some (1) is the suspicion of soiling the mosque, so if the deceased is outside it, it is not disliked according to them. And according to others, the mosque was only built for the five daily prayers, so the deceased, even if outside, is disliked according to them as well. [1] His statement: 'and it is disliked'; it is said (to be) tahriman (prohibitively disliked), as verified by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha in an independent treatise, and this is the view of most later scholars. And it is said (to be) tanzihan (lightly disliked), and this was preferred by the investigator Ibn al-Humann in Al-Fath (3) and his student Ibn Amir Haj in Al-Halba and others. The basis for it is the hadith: 'Whoever prays over a deceased in the mosque, nothing is for him.' It was recorded by Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, Ibn Abi Shaybah, and others, and its chain was criticized, but Ibn al-Qayyim in Zad al-Ma'ad and others verified that its chain is hasan (good) and can be used as evidence. It is supported by the fact that the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) did not habitually pray the funeral prayer in his mosque despite its merit, but rather he used to go out to the prayer ground. And it has been established that he prayed over Sahl and Suhayl in the mosque, recorded by Muslim and others, and that is a specific incident not generalizable, and it is interpreted as showing its validity (permissibility). We have detailed what relates to this topic in Al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad and elsewhere. Then, the dislike (karahah) is only when there is no excuse; if there is an excuse (such as rain or i'tikaf for one who has the right to be in the mosque), then there is no dislike. This is in Al-Halba. [2] His statement: 'congregational mosque'; the one in which prayer is performed with congregation, and it restricts to this as opposed to the mosque built specifically for funeral prayers. [3] His statement: 'the difference among the scholars...'; meaning some scholars explained the dislike of funeral prayer in the mosque due to the suspicion of soiling the mosque because of the possibility that impurity may exit from the orifices of the deceased and fall in the mosque, and we have been commanded to clean mosques and keep them away from that which might cause such suspicion.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on performing the funeral prayer in a mosque. The matn states that it is disliked (makruh) in a congregational mosque if the deceased is inside, and if outside, there is disagreement among the Hanafi scholars. The commentator explains that the disagreement stems from two different causes (illa) for the karahah. One group of scholars holds that the dislike is due to the possibility of the mosque being soiled by impurities from the deceased; therefore, if the deceased is outside the mosque, this cause is absent, and the prayer would not be disliked. Another group holds that the mosque is built exclusively for the five daily prayers, so any other prayer, including funeral prayer, is disliked in a mosque, regardless of whether the deceased is inside or outside. The degree of karahah is also disputed: some later scholars (like Qasim ibn Qutlubugha) deem it tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), while Ibn al-Humam and his student consider it tanzihi (lightly disliked). The commentary provides the hadith of Abu Hurayra as evidence: 'Whoever prays over a deceased in the mosque, nothing is for him,' meaning no reward or the prayer is invalid. The hadith's chain is discussed but deemed hasan by Ibn al-Qayyim. The Prophet's practice is cited: he normally prayed janazah in the prayer ground, not in the mosque, but there is an authentic report that he prayed over Sahl and Suhayl in the mosque, which is taken as a specific incident showing validity rather than establishing a general rule. The commentary clarifies that the dislike applies only when there is no excuse; if there is a valid reason like rain or i'tikaf, the prayer in the mosque is not disliked. It also specifies that the ruling is for a mosque built for congregational prayers, not for a mosque specifically built for funeral prayers.

Key Terms
كراهة تحريمية (karahah tahrimiyyah): A prohibition-level dislike; the act is forbidden but not with the same evidence as haram; requires leaving and is sinful if done.
تلويث المسجد (talawwuth al-masjid): Soiling the mosque with impurity; a cause for karahah according to some Hanafi scholars.
مسجد جماعة (masjid jama'ah): A mosque built for the five daily congregational prayers, as opposed to a mosque specifically for funerals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the basis for the difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars regarding the karahah of funeral prayer in a mosque when the deceased is outside the mosque?
A) Disagreement on the authenticity of the hadith.
B) Disagreement on the cause (illa) of the karahah: some say it is due to potential soiling, others say because the mosque is only for the five daily prayers.
C) Disagreement on whether the deceased is clean or not.
D) Disagreement on the number of congregants.

Key Takeaway
The karahah of funeral prayer in a congregational mosque arises from two possible causes, and the degree is disputed; the relied-upon view is tahrimi but excused by necessity.

Funeral Prayer in the Mosque: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on janaza prayer in mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi positions on funeral prayer in the mosque and state the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer in a congregational mosque is disliked unless the deceased is outside; the cause of dislike determines the scope.

The Hanafi school holds differing views on why funeral prayer is disliked in a mosque. Some scholars attribute it to the fear of soiling the mosque, while others insist that mosques are exclusively for the five daily prayers. This lesson examines both positions, their basis in the hadith and practice of the Prophet, and the preferred ruling that is acted upon today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The matn states that performing funeral prayer in a congregational mosque is disliked if the deceased is inside the mosque. If the deceased is outside, there is a difference among the mashayikh.
The base ruling sets the stage for the dispute.
2
Extract the two causes of dislike
First cause: fear of soiling (tawahhum talwīth) due to possible najāsa from the deceased. Second cause: the mosque was built only for the five daily prayers and similar acts, so any other act is disliked.
Each cause leads to a different scope of dislike.
3
Trace the consequence of each cause
If cause is soiling: dislike only when the deceased is inside (since if outside, no risk). If cause is exclusivity: dislike absolutely, even if the deceased is outside.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
4
Evaluate the evidence
The primary evidence is the hadith 'Whoever prays over a deceased in the mosque has nothing' (hasan chain). It is supported by the Prophet's usual practice of praying in the musalla, except for two known cases which are interpreted as specific permissions.
The hadith is used to support the dislike, though it is open to interpretation.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is that the dislike is only when the deceased is inside, based on the cause of soiling. This is the position adopted in al-Mabsut and al-Muhit, and it is the one acted upon.
Ibn al-Humam and others tarjīh the tanzīhī classification over tahrimī.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكرهت في مسجد جماعة إن كان الميت فيه، وإن كان خارجه اختلف المشايخ. اختلاف المشايخ بناءً على أنّ علةَ الكراهة عند البعض توهم تلويث المسجد، فإن كان الميت خارجه لا تكره عندهم، وعند البعض أن المسجد لم يبن إلا للصلوات الخمس، فالميتُ وإن كان خارجا يكره عندهم أيضاً. قيل تحريماً، وقيل تنزيهاً، ورجّحه المحقق ابن الهمام في الفتح. والأصل فيه حديث: «مَن صلى على ميِّتِ في المسجد فلا شيء له، أخرجه أبو داود وابن ماجه وابن أبي شَيْبَةَ وغيرهم، وقد تكلّم في سنده، لكن حققَ ابنُ القيم في زاد المعاد وغيره: أنَّ سنده حسن محتج به. ويؤيده أنَّ النبي لم يكن من عادته الصلاة على الجنازة في مسجده مع شرفه، بل كان يخرج إلى المصلى، وقد ثبت عنه أنه صلى على سهل وسهيل في المسجد، أخرجه مسلم وغيره، وهو واقعةُ حال لا عموم له، ويحمل على بيان الأجزاء. ثم الكراهة إنّما عدم العذر، فإن كان فلا كراهة؛ كالمطر واعتكاف من له حقُّ التقدم. كذا في الحلبة. قوله: مسجد الجماعة؛ الذي تؤدى فيه الصلاة بالجماعة، واحترز به عن المسجد الذي بني لصلاة الجنائز. قوله: اختلاف المشايخ... الخ؛ يعني عللَ بعض المشايخ كراهة صلاة الجنازة في المسجد بأنَّ فيه توهم تلوّث المسجد؛ لاحتمال أن يخرج نجس من منافذ الميت ويقع في المسجد، وقد أمرنا بتنظيف المساجد وتجنيبها عما يوهم ذلك. فعلى هذا لا تكره إذا كان الميت خارج المسجد، والمصلى داخله، ومنهم من علل بأنَّ المساجد إنما بنيت للصلوات الخمس ونحوها، فلا يؤدى فيه غير ما بنيت له، فعلى هذا تكره مطلقاً.
It is disliked [to pray] in a congregational mosque if the deceased is in it, and if he is outside the mosque, the scholars differed. The difference among the scholars is based on the fact that the cause of dislike according to some is the fear of soiling the mosque, so if the deceased is outside, it is not disliked according to them. According to others, the mosque was built only for the five daily prayers, so even if the deceased is outside, it is disliked according to them as well. It is said [to be] prohibitively disliked, and it is said [to be] authoritatively disliked, and the scholar Ibn al-Humam in al-Fath considered the latter to be preponderant. The basis for it is the hadith: 'Whoever prays over a deceased person in the mosque has nothing' - reported by Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, Ibn Abi Shayba and others. Its chain has been discussed, but Ibn al-Qayyim in Zad al-Ma'ad and others have verified that its chain is good and can be used as evidence. It is supported by the fact that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was not accustomed to praying over the deceased in his mosque despite its honor, but rather he would go out to the musalla. And it is established that he prayed over Sahl and Suhayl in the mosque, as reported by Muslim and others. This is a specific case and is not general in application, and it is interpreted as an indication of permissibility. Then, the dislike is only when there is no excuse. If there is an excuse, there is no dislike, such as rain or i'tikaf of one who has the right to that. Thus in al-Hulba. His statement: 'Mosque of congregation' refers to the mosque in which prayers are performed in congregation, distinguishing it from a mosque built specifically for funeral prayers. His statement: 'The difference of the scholars... etc.' means: some scholars have attributed the dislike of funeral prayer in the mosque to the fear of soiling the mosque, due to the possibility that najasa (impurity) may come out of the deceased's body and fall in the mosque, and we have been commanded to keep the mosques clean and free from what might cause that. According to this, it is not disliked if the deceased is outside the mosque while the prayer is performed inside. Others have attributed the dislike to the fact that mosques are built only for the five daily prayers and similar acts of worship, so nothing else should be performed there. According to this, it is disliked absolutely.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on performing the funeral prayer (salat al-janaza) in a congregational mosque. The matn states that it is disliked (makruh) if the deceased is inside the mosque. If the deceased is outside, there is a difference of opinion among the Hanafi scholars. The commentary explains the reasoning behind the two positions: one cause is the fear of soiling the mosque due to possible impurity from the deceased, so if the deceased is outside, there is no such fear and thus no dislike. The other cause is that mosques are built for the five daily prayers and not for funerals, so it is disliked in all cases. The text also mentions that there is a difference as to whether the dislike is tahrimi (prohibitive) or tanzihi (preventive), with Ibn al-Humam preferring the latter. The primary evidence is the hadith: 'Whoever prays over a deceased person in the mosque has nothing.' Though there is discussion about its chain, later scholars like Ibn al-Qayyim considered it hasan (good). It is supported by the practice of the Prophet who usually prayed in the musalla outside, except in two known cases which are considered specific exceptions. The dislike is lifted if there is a valid excuse like rain or itikaf. The commentary further clarifies that the ruling applies only to mosques used for congregational prayers, not to mosques built specifically for funeral prayers. The overall conclusion is that funeral prayer in the mosque is disliked unless there is an excuse, with the mufta bihi position being the one that distinguishes based on whether the deceased is inside or outside the mosque.

Key Terms
مسجد جماعة (masjid jamā‘ah): A mosque in which the five daily prayers are performed with congregation, as opposed to a mosque built specifically for funeral prayers.
كراهة (karāhah): Legal dislike, which can be either tahrimi (prohibitive) or tanzihi (preventive); the text notes both possibilities.
تلويث (talwīth): Soiling or contaminating, specifically with najasah (ritual impurity) like blood or discharge from the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when is the dislike of performing funeral prayer in the mosque removed?
A) When the deceased is inside the mosque.
B) When there is a valid excuse such as rain or i'tikaf.
C) When the mosque is built for funeral prayers.
D) When the imam is a great scholar.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi ruling is that funeral prayer in a congregational mosque is disliked only if the deceased is inside, and the dislike is removed by a valid excuse.

Funeral of a Newborn: Washing, Naming, and Prayer
Funeral rulings for deceased newborn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the rulings on washing, naming, and funeral prayer for a deceased newborn based on the presence of istihlal and state the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Death of a newborn: washing and naming always obligatory, prayer only if istihlal occurred.

When a newborn dies shortly after birth, the family must fulfil certain funeral obligations. The key question is whether the child showed signs of life (istihlal) after birth. The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance on washing, naming, and praying over the child, with a difference between the earlier transmitted view (Zahir al-Riwayah) and the later chosen view (mukhtar). This lesson unpacks those rulings and their evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three funeral acts
The passage mentions three acts: naming (tasmiya), washing (ghusl), and funeral prayer (salat al-janaza). Determine which are conditional on istihlal.
Naming and washing are unconditional; prayer is conditional.
2
Define istihlal
The commentary explains that istihlal originally means raising voice at sight of the new moon; here it means crying or any movement indicating life. Understand its role as a sign of live birth.
The hadith uses 'yastahillu' meaning cries out.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
The hadith 'The child is not prayed over... until he cries' is cited. Identify how it proves the ruling: it makes istihlal a condition for prayer.
Hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Zahir al-Riwayah states that if the newborn does not cry, he is not washed. But the text says 'wa huwa al-mukhtar' (the chosen view) that he is washed. Understand the basis and which view is mufta bihi.
The chosen view considers the child as having been born alive even without crying.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a newborn who dies immediately without any movement, decide whether to wash, name, and pray. Apply the mufta bihi view.
Wash and name yes; prayer no.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومَن وُلِدَ فمات سمّي وغُسل، وصلي عليه إن استهل، وإلا أُدْرِجَ في خرفة، ولم يصل عليه وغُسل، وهو المختار. صبي سبي فمات، إن سُبي بلا أحد أبويه، أو مع أحدهما فأسلم عاقلاً، أو أحدهما صلى عليه، وإلا فلا. قوله: غسل؛ لأنه خرج حيّاً في الدنيا فيعطى له حكم الأحياء، والأصلُ حديث: «الطِّفلُ لا يصلى عليه، ولا يرث، ولا يورث حتى يستهل»، أخرجه الترمذي والنسائي وابن ماجة وغيرهم. قوله: إن استهل؛ الظاهرُ أنه قيد للصلاة، فإنَّ الغسل ليس بمختص به، وكذا التسمية فإن الغير المستهل بل السَّقط الذي استبانَ بعض خلقه أيضاً يُسمى لينادى باسمه في الحشر، وقد ورد: «سموا أسقاطكم، فإنهم فَرَطَكم». والاستهلالُ في الأصل: رفع الصوت عند رؤية الهلال، ثم استعمل في مطلق رفع الصوت، والمراد به رفع الصوت بالبكاء، أو ما يقوم مقامه مما يدلُّ على أنه خرج حيا من تحريك عضو ونحوه. قوله: هو الأوّل؛ لأنه نفس من وجه، بدليل حصول الاستيلاد، وبه انقضاء العدة، ولا يلزم من سقوط الصلاة سقوط الغسل، كما في الكافي. كذا في البناية. قوله: صبي... الخ؛ اعلم أنه إذا صبي فلا يخلو إما أن يكون مع أحد سبي
Whoever is born and dies, he is named and washed. And prayer is performed over him if he cries (istahalla). Otherwise, he is wrapped in a cloth and not prayed over, but washed. This is the chosen view. A captive child who dies: if he was captured without either of his parents, or with one of them and that one embraced Islam while being sane, or the other, then prayer is performed over him. Otherwise, not. His statement: 'Washed' because he came out alive into the world, so he is given the ruling of the living. The basis is the hadith: 'The child is not prayed over, nor does he inherit, nor is he inherited from until he cries out.' Reported by al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah and others. His statement: 'If he cries' is apparently a condition for the prayer, for washing is not specific to him, and similarly naming, for even one who does not cry, rather a miscarried child whose some parts have formed, is also named so that he may be called by his name at the resurrection. It has been reported: 'Name your miscarried children, for they will be your forerunners.' Al-istihlal originally means raising the voice at the sight of the new moon, then it was used for absolute raising of voice. What is meant is raising the voice by crying, or what takes its place that indicates that he came out alive, such as moving a limb or the like. His statement: 'It is the first' because he is considered a soul in one respect, due to the occurrence of istilad (giving birth) and by it the waiting period ends. The dropping of the prayer does not necessitate dropping the washing, as in al-Kafi. Thus in al-Binaya. His statement: 'A captive child...' know that when a boy is captured, it is not free from the possibility that he is with one of the captors...
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage gives rulings on two cases: (1) a newborn who dies, and (2) a captive child who dies. For the newborn, if he cries (istihlal) after birth, he is named, washed, and the funeral prayer is performed. If he does not cry, he is wrapped in a cloth and washed, but not prayed over. The hadith 'The child is not prayed over... until he cries' is used as evidence. Crying indicates life. The commentary clarifies that washing and naming are not conditional on istihlal; even a miscarried fetus that has formed limbs is washed and named. The prayer is specific to those who cried after birth. For the captive child, the ruling depends on his relationship with his parents at the time of capture. If he was captured alone (without any parent) or with one parent who was a sane Muslim at the time of capture, then he is considered Muslim and the funeral prayer is performed. If neither parent was Muslim, then he follows the religion of the majority of the captors? The text says 'or one of them prayed over him' meaning if one parent is Muslim. Otherwise, no. The commentary on this part is cut off but the ruling is clear.

Key Terms
استهلال (istihlāl): Crying of the newborn after birth; originally means raising voice at sight of moon, used here for any indication of life such as crying or movement.
خرفة (khirqah): A piece of cloth in which the deceased newborn is wrapped if he did not cry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi chosen view (mukhtar), a deceased newborn who did not cry after birth should be:
A) Washed and prayed over.
B) Washed but not prayed over.
C) Not washed but prayed over.
D) Neither washed nor prayed over.

Key Takeaway
Washing a deceased newborn is obligatory regardless of istihlal; funeral prayer requires istihlal.

Funeral of a Captive Child
Rulings on funeral prayer for a deceased captive child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when funeral prayer is performed over a captive child based on the Islamic status of his parents at the time of capture.

Core Idea
Captive child's funeral prayer depends on the parents' Islam status at capture.

When a minor child is taken captive in war, his religious status is uncertain. The Hanafi school gives him the ruling of Islam if one of his parents was a Muslim at the time of capture (or if he was captured alone). This affects funeral rites. This lesson explains the conditions for performing funeral prayer over such a child.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage considers two possibilities: (a) the child is captured alone (with no parent), or (b) captured with one parent. In each case, the Islam of that parent at the time of capture matters.
If captured with both parents, the rule may differ but not mentioned here.
2
Check the condition for scenario (a)
If captured without either parent, the child is considered Muslim by default according to the Hanafi principle that a minor captive is Muslim, so funeral prayer is performed.
This is based on the principle of following the majority or the dar al-harb status.
3
Check the condition for scenario (b)
If captured with one parent, look at that parent's state. If that parent embraced Islam and was sane at the time of capture, the child is Muslim and prayer is performed. If not, prayer is not performed.
The parent's Islam must be at the moment of capture.
4
Apply the ruling
Given a specific scenario, determine the status and decide whether prayer is valid.
Always confirm the capture context.

Ruling on Stillborn Child: Washing and Prayer
States ruling on stillborn: prayer if cries, otherwise not.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing and praying over a stillborn child, and identify the condition of istihlal.

Core Idea
A stillborn child is washed and named but prayed over only if he cried.

The death of an infant shortly after birth raises practical questions about funeral rites. In this passage, the author presents the Hanafi ruling on washing, naming, and praying over a stillborn child. He also discusses an internal difference within the school and supports the chosen position with a hadith and logical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the treatment of a stillborn child. The passage states: the child is named, washed, and prayed over if he cried (istahalla); otherwise, he is wrapped in a cloth, washed, but no prayer.
The first statement is the selected (mukhtar) view.
2
Locate the dalil
The basis is a hadith from al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah: 'The infant is not prayed over, nor inherits, nor is inherited from until he cries.'
The hadith makes istihlal a condition for prayer and inheritance.
3
Examine the condition (istihlal)
Istihlal originally means raising the voice; here it means crying or any sign of life like moving a limb. It is a condition specifically for prayer, not for washing or naming.
The author emphasizes that washing and naming are not tied to istihlal.
4
Analyze the internal dispute
Zahir al-Riwayah holds that a stillborn without signs of life is not washed; the chosen view requires washing. The commentator prefers washing because the child came out alive into the world, even momentarily.
The omission of prayer does not entail omission of washing, as analogy with other cases shows.
5
Note the practical consequence
If the child cried or moved, full funeral rites apply. If not, washing and naming are still required, but the funeral prayer is omitted.
This ruling applies only if the child's limbs are distinct; otherwise, it is not treated as a separate individual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ولد فمات سمي وغسل، وصلي عليه إن استهل، وإلا أدرج في خرفة، ولم يصل عليه وغسل، وهو المختار. وفي ظاهر الرواية : أنه لا يغسل لكن المختار هو الأول. [١]قوله : غسل ; لأنه خرج حياً في الدنيا فيعطى له حكم الأحياء، والأصل حديث: «الطفل لا يصلى عليه، ولا يرث، ولا يورث حتى يستهل»، أخرجه الترمذي والنسائي وابن ماجة وغيرهم. (٢) قوله : إن استهل ; الظاهر أنه قيد للصلاة، فإن الغسل ليس بمختص به، وكذا التسمية فإن الغير المستهل بل السقط الذي استبان بعض خلقه أيضاً يسمى لينادى باسمه في الحشر، وقد ورد: «سموا أسقاطكم، فإنهم فرطكم» (۳). والاستهلال في الأصل : رفع الصوت عند رؤية الهلال، ثم استعمل في مطلق رفع الصوت، والمراد به رفع الصوت بالبكاء، أو ما يقوم مقامه مما يدل على أنه خرج حيا من تحريك عضو ونحوه. [٣] قوله : هو الأول ; لأنه نفس من وجه، بدليل حصول الاستيلاد، وبه انقضاء العدة، ولا يلزم من سقوط الصلاة سقوط الغسل، كما في «الكافي». كذا في «البناية».
Whoever is born and dies: he is named and washed, and prayer is performed over him if he cries (istahalla); otherwise he is wrapped in a cloth and prayer is not performed over him but he is washed. This is the chosen view. And in Zahir al-Riwayah: he is not washed, but the chosen is the first. [1] His statement: 'washed' — because he came out alive into the world, so the ruling of the living is given to him. The basis is the hadith: 'The infant is not prayed over, nor inherits, nor is inherited from until he cries.' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah and others. (2) His statement: 'if he cries' — apparently it is a condition for prayer, for washing is not exclusive to it, and similarly naming; indeed the one who does not cry, even the miscarried fetus whose limbs have become distinct, is also named so that he may be called by his name at the Resurrection. And it has been reported: 'Name your miscarriages, for they will precede you.' (3) Al-istihlal originally means raising the voice at the sight of the new moon, then used for absolute raising of voice; what is meant here is raising the voice by crying, or what takes its place indicating that he came out alive, such as moving a limb and the like. [3] His statement: 'it is the first' — because he is a soul in some respect, evidenced by the occurrence of istilad (childbirth) and the completion of the waiting period thereby, and the omission of prayer does not necessitate omission of washing, as in al-Kafi. This is in al-Binaya.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm with dalil) from the chapter on funerals. It addresses the treatment of an infant who dies shortly after birth. The core ruling: if the child shows signs of life (crying or equivalent), it is treated as a full Muslim — named, washed, and the funeral prayer is performed. If no such sign appears, it is still washed and named based on hadith, but the funeral prayer is omitted. The author notes that the apparent madhhab position (Zahir al-Riwayah) does not require washing, but the chosen (mukhtar) view requires washing. The justification: the infant came out alive into the world, so some rulings of the living apply. The hadith from al-Tirmidhi et al. sets the condition of istihlal for prayer and inheritance. The commentator explains that istihlal is specifically a condition for prayer, not for washing or naming. Naming is recommended even for miscarriages so that they may be called on the Day of Resurrection. The chosen view is preferred because the infant is considered a soul in some respects, such as establishing lineage and completing the iddah. The omission of prayer does not lead to omission of washing, just as in other cases. This lesson is a memorization anchor for the Hanafi ruling on stillborn infants.

Key Terms
استهل (istahalla): To cry or show a sign of life after birth, such as moving a limb.
سقط (siqt): A miscarried fetus; if its limbs are distinct, it is named and washed but no prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen view (mukhtar) in this passage, what is the ruling on washing a stillborn child who did not cry (istihlal)?
A) He is not washed, only wrapped.
B) He is washed but no prayer is performed.
C) He is washed and prayer is performed.
D) He is not washed and no prayer.

Key Takeaway
A stillborn child is washed and named, but the funeral prayer is only performed if he showed a sign of life (istihlal).

Funeral Prayer for a Captive Child
Ruling with proof on captive child funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for performing funeral prayer over a captive child and apply the principle of taba'iyyat al-dar.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer for a captive child is wajib only if the child is deemed Muslim by capture alone or by conversion.

This passage from the sharh addresses a nuanced issue: when is funeral prayer (janazah) performed over a child taken captive in war? The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the presence and conversion of parents, and the child's own capacity to embrace Islam. The ruling is grounded in the principle that children follow the better religion of their parents, and in the absence of parents, they are considered Muslim by virtue of living in Dar al-Islam. A secondary discussion touches on the propriety of performing such a prayer inside a mosque.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صبي سبي فمات، إن سبي بلا أحد أبويه، أو مع أحدهما فأسلم عاقلاً، أو أحدهما صلي عليه، وإلا فلا. فعلى هذا لا تكره إذا كان الميت خارج المسجد، والمصلى داخله، ومنهم من علل بأن المساجد إنما بنيت للصلوات الخمس ونحوها، فلا يؤدى فيه غير ما بنيت له، فعلى هذا تكره مطلقاً. [٤]قوله : صبي... الخ ; اعلم أنه إذا صبي فلا يخلو إما أن يكون مع أحد أبويه أو لا، فإن كان الأول فمات، لم يصل عليه ; لأنه كافر تبعاً للوالدين، إلا أن يقرأ بالإسلام وهو يعقل صفة الإسلام، فإن إسلام الصبي العاقل مقبول، فإذا أسلم وهو ذو عقل وفهم يدخل في المسلمين، فيصلى عليه حينئذ، وكذا إذا أسلم أحد أبويه أو كلاهما، فإنه حينئذ يكون مسلماً بتبعية الوالدين، وإن كان عاقلاً، فإن الطفل ما لم يبلغ يتبع خير الأبوين دينا، ويجعل بتبعيتهما مسلماً، وكذا إذا سبي بدون أبويه فإنه حينئذ يكون مسلماً حكماً تبعاً لدار الإسلام، كما في اللقيط. [١] قوله : صحيح ; دلّ عليه ما ثبت في كتب السير والحديث : «إن عليا المرتضى أسلم وهو غير محتلم فقبله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم».
A captive boy who dies: if he was captured without either of his parents, or with one of them and he converts while sane, or one of them converts, then prayer is performed over him; otherwise not. Based on this, it is not disliked if the deceased is outside the mosque and the prayer is inside. Some have reasoned that mosques are only built for the five prayers and the like, so what they were not built for should not be performed therein; thus it is disliked absolutely. [4] His statement: 'boy...' etc. Know that regarding a captive boy, he is either with one of his parents or not. In the first case, if he dies, prayer is not performed over him because he is a disbeliever by following his parents, unless he reads the Shahada while understanding the nature of Islam, for the conversion of a sane boy is accepted. If he converts while possessing reason and understanding, he enters Islam and prayer is performed over him. Similarly, if one of his parents or both convert, then he becomes Muslim by following the parents, even if he is sane, because a child before puberty follows the better of his parents in religion and is made Muslim by following them. Similarly, if he is captured without his parents, then he is considered Muslim by following Dar al-Islam, like a foundling. [1] His statement: 'valid' — it is supported by what is established in books of sirah and hadith: 'Ali al-Murtada converted while not yet pubescent, and the Messenger of Allah accepted him.'
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage deals with the funeral prayer for a captive child (sabi) taken in war. The ruling distinguishes several scenarios: If the child is captured without any parent, he is considered Muslim by virtue of living in Dar al-Islam, so prayer is performed. If captured with one parent, prayer is only performed if that parent converts to Islam while sane, or if the child himself converts while sane. If neither parent converts, the child remains a disbeliever and no prayer is said. This follows the principle that children follow the better religion of their parents. The commentator also addresses a secondary issue: where the prayer may be performed. Some say it is disliked to pray over a corpse inside the mosque because mosques are for the five daily prayers; others differentiate based on the location of the deceased. The commentator supports the first scenario with the hadith of Imam Ali's conversion before puberty, proving the validity of a child's conversion. This lesson is an explanation of a ruling with proof from the sirah.

Key Terms
سبي (sabi): A child taken captive in war.
تبعية الدار (taba'iyyat al-dar): Legal status of being considered Muslim by virtue of living in Islamic territory.
تبعية الوالدين (taba'iyyat al-walidayn): Legal status of following the religion of one's parents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a captive child is captured with one of his parents, when is the funeral prayer performed over him if he dies?
A) Always, because he is a captive.
B) Only if he converted while sane, or his parent converted.
C) Only if he was captured without any parent.
D) Never, because he is a disbeliever.

Key Takeaway
Funeral prayer over a captive child is wajib only if the child is Muslim—either by capture without parents, by personal conversion while sane, or by a parent's conversion.

Ruling on Washing a Disbelieving Relative: Method and Proof
Explains the method of washing and burying a disbeliever

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing a disbelieving relative, identify the proof from the hadith of Ali, and distinguish the method from that of a Muslim.

Core Idea
A disbeliever is washed only to remove impurity, not with the rituals of a Muslim.

This lesson addresses a specific case: when a Muslim's disbelieving relative dies. The Hanafi school holds that the Muslim is obligated to wash and bury the relative, but the washing is not the full ritual ghusl given to a Muslim. Instead, it is simply pouring water to remove physical filth, like washing a najis object. The proof comes from the Prophet's instruction to Ali regarding his father Abu Talib. A condition is added: if the deceased has a disbelieving relative, it is better to leave the burial to that relative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The washing and burial of a disbeliever by his Muslim relative. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) but the washing is only ghusl al-najas (washing of impurity), not the full ghusl of a Muslim.
The obligation is based on the hadith, not on the deceased's entitlement to ritual purity.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) told Ali: 'Go, wash him, shroud him, and bury him' regarding Ali's father Abu Talib, who died as a disbeliever.
Reported by Ibn Sa'd, Abu Dawud, and al-Nasa'i; it is a sahih hadith, though ahad.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'faghsilhu' indicates obligation, but the context shows limited washing: Ali's father was a disbeliever, so the full Muslim ghusl (with wudu and sunan) is not intended. The instruction to 'wash him' is for cleanliness, not ritual purity.
Hanafis use the principle that the command is for obligation unless there is a qarina (context) indicating otherwise.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that a disbeliever should not be washed at all, based on the idea that the dead body is not owed any honor. Hanafis respond that the hadith provides a direct command, and washing is a practical necessity to avoid harm.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate, but the Hanafi position is relied upon for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كافر مات يغسله وليه المسلم غسل النجس، ويلفه في خرقة، ويحفر حفرة، ويُلقيه فيها. أي يصبُّ عليه الماء على الوجه الذي يَغْسِلُ النَّجاسات، لا كما يَغْسِلُ المسلم بالبداية بالوضوء، وبالميامن. الأصل فيه حديث علي أنه لما مات أبوه أبو طالب كافراً فأخبر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال له: «اذهب فغسلهُ وكَفِّنْهُ وواره»، أخرجَهُ ابنُ سعد في «الطبقات»، ونحوه في «سنن أبي داود» و«النَّسَائي». هذا كله إذا لم يكن له قريب كافر، فإن كان فالأولى تركه له.
A disbeliever who dies: his Muslim relative washes him with the washing of impurity (ghusl al-najas), wraps him in a cloth, digs a hole, and throws him in it. That is, he pours water on him in the manner one washes impurities, not as one washes a Muslim starting with wudu and the right side. The basis of this is the hadith of Ali that when his father Abu Talib died as a disbeliever, he informed the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he said to him: 'Go, wash him, shroud him, and bury him.' Ibn Sa'd reported it in al-Tabaqat, and similar is in Sunan Abi Dawud and al-Nasa'i. This is all if he has no disbelieving relative; if he does, it is better to leave him to him.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof regarding the funeral washing of a disbeliever. The commentator first quotes the matn: 'A disbeliever who dies: his Muslim relative washes him with the washing of impurity...' The ruling is that the washing is not the full ghusl given to a Muslim (which includes wudu, starting with the right side, etc.), but rather a simple pouring of water to remove physical impurity, like washing a najis object. Then the commentator provides the proof: the hadith of Ali washing his father Abu Talib, a disbeliever, by order of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The commentator also adds a condition: if the disbeliever has a disbelieving relative, it is better to leave the burial to that relative. This ruling is based on the Hanafi position that a disbeliever is not entitled to the same ritual honors as a Muslim, and the washing is merely for cleanliness.

Key Terms
غسل النجس (ghusl al-najas): The simple washing of impurity by pouring water over the body to remove physical filth, without the rituals of wudu or starting with the right side.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the correct method of washing a disbeliever in the Hanafi school?
A) Full ghusl with wudu and starting from the right side
B) Simply pouring water to remove impurity, without wudu
C) Washing with soap and camphor
D) No washing at all; bury as is

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: washing a disbelieving relative is wajib but only as ghusl al-najas (simple impurity removal), based on the hadith of Ali.

Ruling on Funeral Prayer for a Captured Child (Sabi)
Ruling with proof on sabi's Islam status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios that determine whether a captured child is considered Muslim for funeral prayer and apply them to novel cases.

Core Idea
A captured child's Islamic status for funeral prayer depends on whether he is taken alone, with a parent, and his own rationality.

When a child is captured from dar al-harb, his religious status is not automatically the same as an adult's. The Hanafi school provides clear rules based on the child's capture circumstances and his own capacity for faith. This lesson unpacks those rules and the proof from the Prophet's acceptance of Ali's early Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three capture scenarios
Child captured without parents, with one parent, with one parent but no one accepts Islam or child irrational.
These scenarios are mutually exclusive.
2
Determine Islamic status in each scenario
Without parent: Muslim by dar. With parent: not by dar; depends on own or parent's Islam.
The ruling for funeral prayer follows from Islamic status.
3
Apply the condition of rationality (aql)
If the child himself accepts Islam, he must be rational (aql) for it to be valid. Irrational acceptance is invalid.
Rationality means understanding the meaning of faith.
4
Note the proof from the hadith of Ali
The Prophet accepted Ali's Islam before puberty, showing that a rational minor's Islam is valid.
This hadith is the primary evidence for the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإنَّه إذا سبي بلا أحد أبويه يكون مسلماً تبعاً للدار، فيصلى عليه. وإن سبي مع أحد أبويه فحينئذ لا يكون تبعاً للدار، فإن أسلم هو، والحال أنَّه عاقل فإسلامه صحيح، فيصلى عليه. وإن أسلم أحدهما يكون مسلماً تبعاً لأحدهما، فيصلى عليه. وإلا فلا، أي إن سبي مع أحد أبويه، ولم يُسْلِمُ أحد من أبويه، ولا هو عاقل لا يصلى عليه، فهذا يشمل ما إذا لم يُسْلِمْ أصلاً، أو أسلم وهو غير عاقل. دَلَّ عليه ما ثبت في كتب السير والحديث: إنَّ عليا المرتضى أسلم وهو غير محتلم فقبله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم.
For if he is captured without [either of] his parents, he is a Muslim by virtue of the abode (dar), so prayer is performed over him. If he is captured with one of his parents, then he is not by virtue of the abode. If he himself accepts Islam, and he is rational, then his Islam is valid, so prayer is performed over him. If one of his parents accepts Islam, he becomes a Muslim by following that parent, so prayer is performed over him. Otherwise no: that is, if he is captured with one of his parents, and none of his parents accepts Islam, and he himself is not rational, then prayer is not performed over him. This includes the case where he does not accept Islam at all, or he accepts Islam but is not rational. Evidence for it is what is established in the books of biography and hadith: that Ali al-Murtada accepted Islam while he was not yet pubescent, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) accepted it.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof explaining when a child captured in war (sabi) is considered Muslim for the purpose of funeral prayer. The commentator explains the rule: if the child is captured alone (without parents), he is automatically considered Muslim because the dar al-harb is dar al-kufr and the dar al-Islam makes him Muslim by default (like a foundling). So the funeral prayer is performed over him. If he is captured with one parent, he does not automatically become Muslim by the dar; his status depends on his own acceptance of Islam or that of his parent. If he himself embraces Islam while he is rational (aql, i.e., capable of understanding), his Islam is valid and he is prayed over. If one of his parents embraces Islam, he follows that parent and is considered Muslim. If neither parent accepts and he does not accept or is not rational, then he is not Muslim and no funeral prayer is performed. The commentator provides the proof: the hadith of Ali accepting Islam before puberty, showing that a rational minor's Islam is valid.

Key Terms
السبي (as-sabi): A child taken captive from dar al-harb.
غير محتلم (ghayr muhtalim): Not yet reached puberty (i.e., a minor).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is funeral prayer performed over a child captured from dar al-harb with one parent?
A) Always, because he is in dar al-Islam
B) Only if he himself accepts Islam rationally
C) Only if one parent accepts Islam
D) Either the child (if rational) or one parent accepts Islam

Key Takeaway
A captured child is considered Muslim for funeral prayer if captured alone, or if captured with a parent and either the child (if rational) or the parent accepts Islam.

Sunnah of Carrying the Bier
Describes the recommended method of carrying a bier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunan acts of carrying a bier and identify the evidence from hadith for each.

Core Idea
Carry the bier on four shoulders, walk briskly but don't run, and don't sit until it's placed.

This passage details the recommended method of carrying a bier during a funeral procession. The text specifies four sunan acts: carrying with four people, the order of placement on shoulders, a moderate pace less than running, and the prohibition of sitting before the bier is set down. Each ruling is supported by a hadith proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sunan acts
List the four rulings explicitly mentioned in the text: four carriers, order of lifting, brisk pace (less than running), and no sitting until placed.
These are all stressed recommendations (sunnah muakkadah).
2
Match each act to its hadith evidence
For each sunan act, find the corresponding hadith cited: Ibn Mas'ud for carrying all sides, hadith on hastening, hadith defining 'ma doona al-khabab', and hadith prohibiting sitting.
The commentator provides the proof for each ruling.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how each hadith indicates the ruling. Commands (e.g., 'falyahmil', 'asri'u') indicate recommendation; prohibitions (e.g., 'la tajlisu') indicate dislike (karahah).
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-nadb unless a qarinah indicates obligation.
4
Determine the hukm level
Confirm that all four are sunnah muakkadah, not wajib. The evidence is zanni in transmission and meaning, and there is no indication of obligation.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah, muttafaq alayh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسن في حمل الجنازة أربعة: وأن تضع مقدمها، ثم مؤخرها على يمينك، ثم مقدمها، ثم مؤخرها على يسارك، ويسرعون بها لا خبباً، وكره الجلوس قبل وضعها. عن ابن مسعود قال: «من اتبع الجنازة فليحمل بجوانب السرير كلها، فإنها من السنة»، أخرجه ابن ماجة والبيهقي. وحديث: «أسرعوا بالجنازة فإن تك صالحة فخير تقدمونها إليه، وإن تك سيئة فشر تضعونها عن رقابكم»، أخرجه البخاري. وعن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه سئل عن إسراع الجنازة فقال: «ما دون الخبب»، أخرجه أبو داود والترمذي. وحديث: «إذا تبعتم الجنازة فلا تجلسوا حتى توضع»، أخرجه أبو داود.
And it is Sunnah in carrying the bier that you carry it with four [people]: and that you place its front, then its back on your right side, then its front, then its back on your left side; and they walk briskly with it, but not at a running pace; and it is disliked to sit before it is placed down. [Reported] from Ibn Mas'ud: 'Whoever follows a funeral, let him carry the sides of the bed all of them, for that is from the Sunnah.' It was reported by Ibn Majah and al-Bayhaqi. And the hadith: 'Hasten with the funeral; if it is pious, it is good you are sending it forward, and if it is evil, it is evil you are putting off your necks.' Reported by Bukhari. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about hastening the funeral and he said: 'Less than running pace.' Reported by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi. And the hadith: 'If you follow a funeral, do not sit until it is placed down.' Reported by Abu Dawud.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof concerning the sunan (recommended practices) of carrying the bier. The matn states it is Sunnah to carry with four people, and describes the order: first the front of the bier on the right shoulder, then the back on the right, then the front on the left, then the back on the left. Then it says to walk briskly but not at a running pace (khabab). It also states it is makruh (disliked) to sit down before the bier is placed on the ground (after the funeral prayer). The commentator provides several hadith proofs: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud about carrying all sides being Sunnah, the hadith about hastening the funeral, the hadith defining the speed as less than running (ma doona al-khabab), and the hadith prohibiting sitting before placing the bier down. The textual operation is expansion_probe because the commentator is expanding the matn with proofs and details.

Key Terms
الخبب (al-khabab): A type of running pace between walking and full sprint; the text prohibits that pace.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Carrying the bier with four people, alternating shoulders, walking briskly but not running, and not sitting until placed are sunnah acts supported by authentic hadith.

Manner of Carrying the Bier on Shoulders
Ruling on carrying bier on right then left shoulders with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended sequence of carrying the bier (front then back on right, then front then back on left) and cite the hadith from Ibn Mas'ud as evidence.

Core Idea
Carry the bier on both shoulders, starting with the front on the right — that is the Sunnah.

The proper method of carrying the deceased on the bier is a Sunnah with significant merit. In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi position on how to position the bier on the shoulders, based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (radiAllahu anhu). We will see the sequence and rationale, and understand that this practice is established by the Prophet's command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence commanded
The matn instructs: place the front (muqaddam) on the right shoulder first, then the back (mu'akhkhar) on the right; then repeat the same on the left shoulder.
The commentator clarifies that the address is general to any carrier.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud states: 'Whoever follows a funeral procession should carry all sides of the bier, for that is from the Sunnah.' This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Bayhaqi.
3
Understand the rationale
Starting with the front (muqaddam) honours the head of the deceased, and starting with the right follows the principle of tayammun (preferring the right) in all good acts.
This rationale is explained in the commentary.
4
Recognize the authority level
This ruling is considered sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah) in the Hanafi school, based on the explicit phrase 'min al-sunnah'.
Some other schools consider it merely mubah, but the Hanafi mufta bihi is sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن تَضَعَ مُقدِّمها ، ثُمَّ مؤخِّرَها على يمينك، ثُمَّ مُقدِّمها ، ثُمّ مؤخّرها على يسارك۔ قوله : وإن تضع ؛ عطف على قوله : «أربعة»، والخطاب هاهنا إلى غير المتعين، وأصله ما ورد عن ابن مسعود قال : «مَن اتَّبِعَ الجنازة فليحمل بجوانب السرير كلّها ، فإنّها من السنة ) ، أخرجه ابن ماجة والبيهقي وغيرهما، في الباب أخبار مبسوطة في «البناية»، و«نصب الراية»(۳)، وغيرهما. (٢) قوله : ثم مؤخرها ؛ ذلك لشرف المتقدّم بالتقديم، واستحباب التيامن في كلِّ شيء.

(2) His saying: 'Then its back' is because the front part has honor by being placed first, and it is recommended to start with the right in everything.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn (base text) on the manner of carrying the bier, expanded by the commentator. The base text instructs the bearer to lift the bier onto the right shoulder first: first the front part, then the back part; then similarly onto the left shoulder: first the front, then the back. The commentator explains that this address is general to anyone who carries. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (radiyallahu 'anhu) that carrying all sides of the bier is from the Sunnah. The reason for starting with the front is its honor, and starting with the right is recommended in all good actions (tayammun). This is the Hanafi position: it is mustahabb (recommended) to carry the bier in this manner. There is no disagreement within the madhhab on this sunnah.

Key Terms
سرير (sarīr): The bier or stretcher upon which the deceased is carried.
تيامن (tayāmun): Starting with the right side in actions, considered recommended (mustahabb) in Hanafi fiqh.

Hastening the Funeral Procession: The Sunnah Speed
Ruling on funeral procession speed with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the speed of the funeral procession and apply the hadith evidence to distinguish between recommended brisk walking and prohibited trotting.

Core Idea
Hasten with the bier, but not to the point of trotting (khabab).

How fast should we walk when carrying the funeral bier? The matn instructs us to hasten but with a clear limit: no trotting. This lesson unpacks the prophetic evidence and the Hanafi position that brisk walking is a confirmed sunnah, while running or trotting is contrary to the sunnah. We'll trace the proof and understand the legal reasoning behind the recommended speed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? It is the manner of walking with the funeral bier. The ruling: hasten (isra') without trotting (khabab). Determine the hukm level.
The act is the gait during the procession.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites two hadith: the first from Bukhari and Muslim commanding 'asri'u' (hasten), and the second from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi clarifying the limit 'ma duna al-khabab' (less than trotting). Identify the type of dalil and its strength.
Both are ahad hadith, so zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil yield the ruling? The imperative 'asri'u' in Hanafi usul indicates command. But since the hadith does not specify a particular manner and the second hadith sets a limit, the command is interpreted as recommendation (nadb). The clarification 'ma duna al-khabab' shows that trotting is excluded.
The imperative is not for obligation due to the absence of a qarinah making it fard.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools consider walking at any moderate pace permissible (mubah), while Hanafis consider brisk walking sunnah muakkadah. Recognise the difference in legal weight.
The khilaf is in whether the command indicates obligation or recommendation.
5
State the mufta bihi
The operative ruling: it is mustahabb (recommended) to walk quickly but not to run or trot. The Hanafi school follows the zahir of the hadith as a sunnah muakkadah.
Fatwa is given on the Hanafi position of sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسرعون بها لا خَبياً. قوله : ويسرعون ؛ من الإسراع : أي يمشون بالجنازة مسرعين الحديث : «أسرعوا بالجنازة فإن تك صالحة فخير تقدمونها إليه ، وإن تك سيئة فشر تضعونها عن رقابكم ، أخرجَهُ البُخَارِي وغيره. [٤ ] قوله : لا خبباً ؛ الخَبَب : بفتحات ؛ ضرب من العد، وقد ورد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه سئل عن إسراع الجنازة فقال: «ما دون الخبب ) ، أخرجه أبو داود والترمذي.
And they hasten with it, not in a trot. His saying: 'And they hasten' is from al-isra', meaning they walk quickly with the funeral. The hadith: 'Hasten with the funeral; if it is righteous, it is good you are sending forward to it, and if it is evil, it is evil you are removing from your necks.' Narrated by Bukhari and others. [4] His saying: 'not in a trot'; al-khabab: with fatha, a type of running. And it is reported from the Prophet (sallallahu 'alayhi wasallam) that he was asked about hastening the funeral and said: 'Less than trotting.' Narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the speed of the funeral procession. The matn commands that the participants hasten (yusri'oon) but not to the extent of khabab (a gait between walking and running). The commentator cites the well-known hadith from Bukhari urging speed in carrying the funeral, with a double benefit: if the deceased was righteous, it is good being sent forward; if wicked, it is a burden being removed. The second hadith from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi clarifies the limit: speed should be less than khabab. In the Hanafi school, it is sunnah to walk briskly but not to run.

Key Terms
خبب (khabab): A specific type of fast running between walking and galloping; prohibited in funeral processions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Trotting like a horse.

Key Takeaway
Hasten with the funeral bier, but never to the extent of trotting (khabab); this is a confirmed sunnah in the Hanafi school.

Sitting Before Placing the Bier is Disliked
Ruling on sitting before placing funeral bier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting before the bier is placed down and explain the dalil and wisdom behind it.

Core Idea
Sitting before the bier is placed is makruh tanzihi — the command to stand is for readiness to assist.

When following a funeral, certain etiquettes are recommended. One of them concerns whether you may sit down while the bier is still being carried. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on this issue, supported by a hadith from Abu Dawud, and explains the legal reasoning behind the disliked nature of sitting before the bier is placed on the ground.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that sitting before the bier is placed is 'makruh' (disliked). Determine the specific act (sitting while following the funeral before the bier is set down) and its legal category (makruh tanzihi).
Makruh tanzihi means slightly disliked, not sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'When you follow a funeral, do not sit until it is placed.' Identify the source (Abu Dawud) and classify the hadith as ahad (single-chain) which gives zanni thubut.
Also note the wisdom (sirr) that standing enables cooperation in carrying.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling. The negative imperative 'la tajlisu' indicates prohibition, but the Hanafis interpret it as karahah tanzihiyyah because the underlying reason (ta'awun) lessens the severity.
The prohibition is not absolute; it is understood as advisory based on the reason.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools consider sitting at that time to be haram or makruh tahrimi. The Hanafi view differs due to the interpretation of the hadith's imperative.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on usul principles.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that it is makruh tanzihi. No tarjih is needed as it is the main view.
The mufta bihi is 'makruh' according to Zahir al-Riwayah.

Walking Behind the Bier is Preferred
Ruling on preferred position in funeral procession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred position when following a funeral according to the Hanafi school and explain the proof from the hadith of Ali.

Core Idea
Walking behind the bier is superior to walking in front, but all positions are permissible.

When attending a funeral, many wonder where to walk: in front of the bier, behind it, or beside it. The Hanafi school clarifies that while walking behind is most virtuous, the other positions are entirely permissible. This lesson unpacks the textual proof and the wisdom behind the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that walking behind the funeral bier is 'ahabb' (more beloved), indicating a recommended (mustahabb) action. Note that the text also affirms the permissibility of walking in front, to the right, or left.
The term 'ahabb' in Hanafi fiqh is used synonymously with mustahabb.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Abzi, in which 'Ali (radiyallahu 'anhu) compares the virtue of walking behind the bier to the virtue of congregational prayer over praying alone.
This hadith is recorded by 'Abd al-Razzaq in his Musannaf.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Ali's comparison explicitly indicates superiority (tafdil). The phrase 'like the virtue of congregational prayer over praying alone' shows that walking behind is more rewarding, as congregational prayer is superior to individual prayer.
The comparison establishes a clear preference, not an obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars from other schools hold that walking in front or behind are equal. However, Hanafis follow the explicit comparison from Ali. The practice of Abu Bakr and Umar walking in front was to ease the people, not to indicate equivalence.
Ibn Umar also reported seeing the Prophet (sallallahu 'alayhi wasallam) walk in front on occasion, showing permissibility.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The hadith from Ali is clear in preferring behind. The actions of the Companions (Abu Bakr, Umar, and the Prophet) show that front is permissible. Hence, the mufta bihi is that behind is superior, but other positions are allowed.
This balance avoids causing hardship while encouraging following the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمشي خلفها أحب. قوله : والمشي خلفها ؛ أي خلف الجنازة، أحبّ أي أحسنُ وأفضلُ وإِن جازَ المشي أمامها ويمينها وشمالها ، لحديث عبد الرحمن بن أبزي له قال : «كنتُ في جنازة وأبو بكر وعمر يمشيان أمامها ، وعليه يمشي خلفها ، فقلت لعلي له : أراك تمشي خلفها ، وأبو بكر وعمر يمشيان أمامها ، فقال : لقد علمـا أنَّ فضل المشي خلفها على المشي أمامها كفضلِ صلاة الجماعة على الفذ، لكنهما أحبا أن يُسرا على الناس (۳)، أخرجه عبد الرزاق في مصنفه». وفي الباب أخبار وآثار مبسوطة في تخريج أحاديث الهداية للزيلعي، والذي في السنن الأربعة وغيرها عن ابن عمر له : أنه رأى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأبا بكر وعمر يمشيان أمام الجنازة).
And walking behind it is more beloved. His saying: 'And walking behind it'; i.e., behind the funeral, 'more beloved' i.e., better and more excellent, although walking in front, to its right, and to its left is permissible. Due to the hadith of 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Abzi: 'I was at a funeral and Abu Bakr and 'Umar were walking in front of it, while 'Ali was walking behind it. I said to 'Ali: I see you walking behind it while Abu Bakr and 'Umar walk in front of it. He said: They know that the virtue of walking behind it over walking in front of it is like the virtue of congregational prayer over praying alone, but they wanted to make it easy for the people.' Narrated by 'Abd al-Razzaq in his Musannaf. And on this topic there are detailed narrations and traditions in the Takhrij Ahadith al-Hidayah of al-Zayla'i. And what is in the four Sunan and others from Ibn 'Umar that he saw the Prophet (sallallahu 'alayhi wasallam), Abu Bakr, and 'Umar walking in front of the funeral.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage addresses the preferred position for those following the funeral procession. The matn states that walking behind the bier is 'ahabb' (more beloved). The commentator clarifies that walking in front, to the right, or left is permissible (ja'iz), but walking behind is superior. The proof is the narration from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Abzi in which 'Ali (radiyallahu 'anhu) explains that the virtue of walking behind is like the virtue of congregational prayer over praying alone, but that Abu Bakr and 'Umar walked in front to ease the people (so as not to crowd the bier). Another narration from Ibn 'Umar shows the Prophet himself walked in front on occasion, indicating that both positions are acceptable but behind is better. In the Hanafi school, it is mustahabb to walk behind the bier if possible, though walking in front is not sinful.

Key Terms
خلف الجنازة (khalfa al-janazah): Walking behind the funeral bier, the preferred position.
أحبّ (ahabb): More beloved, indicating a recommended (mustahabb) action in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Walking in front of the bier.
B) Walking to the right of the bier.
C) Walking behind the bier.
D) All positions are equal.

Key Takeaway
Walking behind the funeral bier is recommended (mustahabb) and superior, but all positions are permissible.

Grave Digging: Lahd and Entering from Qibla
Ruling on grave digging with lahd and entering from qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on grave construction (lahd vs shaq) and identify the hadith proof for lahd and the practice of entering from qibla.

Core Idea
The lahd is the distinguishing sign of a Muslim grave; it is sunnah except when necessity dictates a shaq.

Proper burial is a communal obligation with detailed sunnahs. This passage addresses two specific aspects: the shape of the grave and the direction from which the body is placed. Understanding these rulings ensures that the deceased is honoured according to the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two methods
Determine what 'lahd' and 'shaq' mean as two techniques for digging the grave.
Lahd is a side niche; shaq is a central trench.
2
Locate the preferred method and its proof
The text states that lahd is better and cites the hadith 'al-lahdu lana wa al-shaqqu li-ghayrina'. Understand how this hadith functions as evidence.
This hadith is narrated by the authors of the four Sunan.
3
Recognize the exception
Note that shaq becomes permissible when lahd is not feasible (e.g., hard ground). This shows the Hanafi principle of necessity overriding sunnah.
Necessity (darura) relaxes the recommendation.
4
Understand the second ruling: entering from qibla
The text instructs that the deceased should be placed into the grave from the qibla side. This is based on the Prophet's practice when burying his Companions.
This is a separate sunnah act during burial.
5
Synthesize the complete practice
Combine both rulings: dig a lahd on the qibla side, then lower the body from the qibla direction facing the qibla.
This ensures the body is positioned correctly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويحفر القبر ويُلحد ويُدخل فيه مما يلي القبلة. قوله : ويلحد ؛ أي يجعل لحداً، لحديث: «اللحدُ لنا والشق لغيرنا ) ، أخرجَهُ أصحاب السنن الأربعة وغيرهم، وهو أفضلُ إلا عند الضرورة إلى حفر الشق. [٣] قوله : مما يلي ؛ أي يأخذ الميت في القبر من جهة القبلة، وهو المأثور عن رسولِ الله عند دفن بعض أصحابه ) ، أخرجه الترمذي وغيره.
And the grave is dug, and a niche (lahd) is made, and he is entered from the direction of the qibla. His saying: 'and a niche is made', i.e., a lahd is made, due to the hadith: 'The lahd is for us, and the shaq is for others.' Narrated by the authors of the four Sunan and others. And it is better except when there is a necessity to dig a shaq. [3] His saying: 'from the direction of', i.e., the deceased is taken into the grave from the direction of the qibla, and it is the reported practice from the Messenger of Allah (sallallahu 'alayhi wasallam) when burying some of his Companions. Narrated by al-Tirmidhi and others.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings regarding the grave. First, the grave should be dug with a 'lahd' (a niche on the qibla side) rather than a 'shaq' (a trench in the middle). The proof is the hadith: 'The lahd is for us and the shaq is for others,' meaning it is the practice of Muslims. However, if the ground is too hard to make a lahd, a shaq is permissible out of necessity. The Hanafi school considers lahd superior (afdal). Second, the deceased should be placed into the grave from the qibla side (i.e., the body is lowered facing the qibla). This is based on the practice of the Prophet (sallallahu 'alayhi wasallam).

Key Terms
لحد (lahd): A niche dug on the qibla side of the grave to place the deceased.
شق (shaq): A trench dug in the middle of the grave, used when lahd is not possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Lahd is the preferred method for Muslim graves, and entering from qibla is sunnah; shaq is only a backup when necessary.
